1 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Weber


No. 2014AP304-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 96; 372 Wis. 2d 202; 887 N.W.2d 554; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 495


September 6, 2016, Oral Argument 
November 29, 2016, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeal. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Wood. JUDGE: Gregory J. Potter. (L.C. No. 2012CF274).
State v. Weber, 2015 WI App 90, 365 Wis. 2d 606, 871 N.W.2d 866, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 728 (Oct. 8, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A police officer's entry into the garage of defendant's residence was constitutionally reasonable under the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV, and under Wis. Const. art. I, § 11 based on the exigency of hot pursuit because the officer was attempting to apprehend defendant, who had driven into the garage and parked there instead of submitting to a lawful traffic stop on a public highway; [2]-Because the officer had probable cause to believe that defendant had committed two jailable offenses under Wis. Stat. §§ 346.17(2t) (2011-2012), 946.41(1)(2011-2012), 939.51(3)(a) (2011-2012) by fleeing from the traffic stop, a limited entry into defendant's open garage for the purpose of preventing defendant's continued flight into the house was permissible, and thus defendant was not entitled to suppress evidence of drunk driving and other offenses.


OUTCOME: Decision reversed.

 

2 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Singh v. Kemper


No. 2013AP1724


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 67; 371 Wis. 2d 127; 883 N.W.2d 86; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 181


March 14, 2016, Argued 
July 13, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2013CV1540). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Racine. JUDGE: Gerald P. Ptacek.
State ex rel. Singh v. Kemper, 2014 WI App 43, 353 Wis. 2d 520, 846 N.W.2d 820, 2014 Wisc. App. LEXIS 244 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-At the time a habeas applicant was sentenced in 2010 for an offense he committed in 2008 and when he committed a second offense in 2011, Wis. Stat. § 302.113(2)(b) (2009-10) was in effect, which allowed inmates to earn positive adjustment time; [2]-The repeal of early release would impermissibly retroactively increase the applicant's punishment after he was convicted and sentenced, violating the ex post facto clauses of the Wisconsin and U.S. Constitutions, Wis. Const. art. I, § 12, and U.S. Const. art. I, §§ 9, 10; [3]-Wis. Stat. § 973.198 (2013-14), which preserved the opportunity for individuals to earn early release based on positive adjustment time earned between October 1, 2009 and August 3, 2011, impermissibly altered the procedures for procuring early release, resulting in a 90-day delay before release, in violation of the ex post facto clauses.


OUTCOME: Court of appeals affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

3 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


City of Eau Claire v. Booth


No. 2015AP869


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 65; 370 Wis. 2d 595; 882 N.W.2d 738; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 179


April 7, 2016, Oral Argument 
July 12, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County, William M. Gabler, Sr., Judge. (L.C. 2014GF804). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Eau Claire. JUDGE: William M. Gabler, Sr.
City of Eau Claire v. Booth, 2016 WI 2, 365 Wis. 2d 746, 872 N.W.2d 671, 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 734 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's 1992 conviction for operating while intoxicated (OWI) should have been charged as a second offense and prosecuted by the State, rather than a city prosecutor, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 345.65(2)(am)1.-2.; however, under Wis. Const. art. VII, § 8, the circuit court did not lack jurisdiction over the proceeding, it only lacked competency to proceed; [2]-First-offense and second-offense OWIs were offenses known at law as set forth in Wisconsin statutes, Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1), 346.65(2)(am)1.-2.; therefore, the circuit court had jurisdiction; [3]-Because the circuit court had subject matter jurisdiction over the 1992 OWI first-offense action, the civil forfeiture judgment was not void for lack of subject matter jurisdiction under Wis. Stat. § 806.07(1)(d); [4]-Defendant forfeited her challenge to the circuit court's competency by waiting 22 years to raise it.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded.

 

4 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Lands' End, Inc. v. City of Dodgeville


No. 2015AP179


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 64; 370 Wis. 2d 500; 881 N.W.2d 702; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 176


March 16, 2016, Oral Argument 
July 12, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Iowa County, Craig R. Day, Judge. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Iowa. JUDGE: Craig R. Day. (L.C. No. 2009CV108).
Lands' End, Inc. v. City of Dodgeville, 2013 WI App 128, 351 Wis. 2d 223, 838 N.W.2d 865, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 753 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court properly awarded plaintiff interest under Wis. Stat. § 807.01(4) (2013-14), the statutory rate of interest in effect when plaintiff recovered judgment, because plaintiff did not have a vested right in the interest rate at the time plaintiff made its offer of settlement, the legislature had a rational basis for changing the applicable interest and did not create an irrational or arbitrary classification, and awarding interest under the amended version of the statute did not violate Equal Protection; plaintiff made an offer of settlement under Wis. Stat. § 807.01(4) (2009-10) but did not recover a judgment until after Wis. Stat. § 807.01(4) (2013-14) took effect and did not acquire a vested right in the statutory interest rate in effect when the offer of settlement was made.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

5 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Blake v. Jossart


No. 2012AP2578


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 57; 370 Wis. 2d 1; 884 N.W.2d 484; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 171


February 24, 2016, Oral Argument 
July 6, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Blake v. Jossart, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 552 (U.S., Jan. 9, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Shelley J. Gaylord. (L.C. No. 2010CV1048). (Reported at 2015 WI App 58, 364 Wis. 2d 526, 868 N.W.2d 198). (Ct. App. 2015 - Unpublished).
Blake v. Jossart, 2015 WI App 58, 364 Wis. 2d 526, 868 N.W.2d 198, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 420 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Revocation of the petitioner's childcare certification was proper because the petitioner had a 1986 conviction for misdemeanor welfare fraud, under Wis. Stat. § 48.685(5)(br)5., the conviction made the petitioner ineligible for certification, and Wis. Stat. § 48.685(5)(br)5. neither denied the petitioner due process nor equal protection of the law; Wis. Stat. § 48.685(5)(br)5., passed rational basis review on its face, Wis. Stat. § 48.685(5)(br)5. created a classification related to social welfare legislation and did not create an impermissible irrebuttable presumption, and a rational basis existed for creating a specific classification for people convicted of offenses involving public assistance fraud.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

6 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gayton


No. 2013AP646-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 58; 370 Wis. 2d 264; 882 N.W.2d 459; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 164


March 14, 2016, Oral Argument 
July 6, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gayton v. Wis., 2017 U.S. LEXIS 1957 (U.S., Mar. 20, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dennis R. Cimpl and Ellen R. Brostrom. JUDGE: Milwaukee. (L.C. No. 2011CF73).
State v. Gayton, 2014 WI App 120, 358 Wis. 2d 709, 856 N.W.2d 345, 2014 Wisc. App. LEXIS 812 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The denial of appellant's postconviction motion was proper because, as a minor aspect of its comprehensive evaluation of appellant's character, the circuit court mentioned appellant's immigration status, which was relevant to his conviction for causing a death while operating a motor vehicle without a license and those comments did not deny appellant due process in the form of reliance on an improper sentencing factor; [2]-Review of the circuit court's sentencing comments in their entirety showed that the court imposed a harsh sentence on appellant because of his dangerous conduct operating a vehicle while intoxicated and the tragic consequences of that act; [3]-Any references to his immigration status implicated the unlawful aspects of his presence in the United States, which were directly relevant to his conviction for homicide while operating a vehicle without a license.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Jackson


No. 2014AP2238-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 56; 369 Wis. 2d 673; 882 N.W.2d 422; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 161


January 25, 2016, Oral Argument 
July 1, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2012CF147). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Outagamie. JUDGE: Mark J. McGinnis.
State v. Jackson, 2015 WI App 49, 363 Wis. 2d 554, 866 N.W.2d 768, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 353 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The inevitable discovery doctrine under U.S. Const. amend. IV applied because untainted portions of the search warrant affidavit established probable cause to search the residence; defendant was an obvious suspect in her husband's murder as she was very angry at him, the officers legally searching defendant's residence had actively engaged in searching the premises before her arrival, and those officers would have continued the search and discovered the physical evidence without defendant's involvement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. McKellips


No. 2014AP827-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 51; 369 Wis. 2d 437; 881 N.W.2d 258; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 158


April 7, 2016, Argued 
June 28, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. McKellips, 2016 WI 81, 371 Wis. 2d 614, 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 321 (2016)
Petition for certiorari filed at, 09/23/2016


PRIOR HISTORY: (L.C. No. 2011CF645).
State v. McKellips, 2015 WI App 31, 361 Wis. 2d 773, 864 N.W.2d 106, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 204 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The State satisfied its burden of proving the element, use of a "computerized communications system," because defendant used his cellphone as a computer to send communications to the victim over the computer system used by their cellphones so that he could have sexual contact with her; [2]-Wis. Stat. § 948.075 (2013-14) was not unconstitutionally vague because a person of ordinary intelligence would understand that using a cellphone to text or picture-message a child to entice sexual encounters violated the statute; [3]-The court of appeals erred in exercising its discretionary reversal authority under Wis. Stat. § 752.35 when it determined the interest of justice required a new trial on the ground that the real controversy was not fully tried; the court of appeals did not decide the issues defendant raised, and took a shortcut directly to § 752.35.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Black v. City of Milwaukee


No. 2014AP400


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 47; 369 Wis. 2d 272; 882 N.W.2d 333; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 155


February 24, 2016, Argued 
June 23, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Milwaukee Police Ass'n v. City of Milwaukee, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 7225 (U.S., Nov. 28, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2013CV5977). COURT:Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Paul R. Van Grunsven.
Black v. City of Milwaukee, 2015 WI App 60, 364 Wis. 2d 626, 869 N.W.2d 522, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 536 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Wis. Stat. § 66.0502 (2013-14) precluded the city from enforcing its residency requirement for city employees because Wis. Stat. § 66.0502 uniformly affected every city or village and satisfied the uniformity requirement of the home rule amendment, Wis. Const. art. XI, § 3(1); [2]-Police association was not entitled to relief or damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because the association had not shown a deprivation of rights, privileges or immunities protected by the Constitution or laws of the United States.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

10 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Moustakis v. State DOJ


No. 2014AP1853


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 42; 368 Wis. 2d 677; 880 N.W.2d 142; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 150


February 4, 2016, Argued 
May 20, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2014CV41). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Lincoln. JUDGE: Jay R. Tlusty.
Moustakis v. State DOJ, 2015 WI App 63, 364 Wis. 2d 740, 869 N.W.2d 788, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 580 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A district attorney, as a holder of a state public office under Wis. Const. art. VI, § 4 and Wis. Stat. §§ 19.32(4) (2013-2014), 19.42(13) (2013-2014), 20.923(2) (2013-2014), was not an employee within the meaning of Wis. Stat. §§ 19.32(1bg) (2013-2014), 19.356(2)(a)1. (2013-2014), and thus could not maintain an action under § 19.356(4) to restrain the Wisconsin Department of Justice from providing access to requested records that pertained to him; [2]-Although the State of Wisconsin was not specifically identified as an authority under § 19.32(1), the district attorney could not qualify under the second part of the definition of an employee in § 19.32(1bg) as employed by an employer other than an authority because drawing a distinction between holding a state public office and being employed by a state public office was contrary to any reasonable reading of the statutes.


OUTCOME: Affirmed and remanded.

 

11 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Coyne v. Walker


No. 2013AP416


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 38; 368 Wis. 2d 444; 879 N.W.2d 520; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 148


November 17, 2015, Oral Argument 
May 18, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Amy R. Smith. (L.C. No. 2011CV4573).
Coyne v. Walker, 2015 WI App 21, 361 Wis. 2d 225, 862 N.W.2d 606, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 127 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because 2011 Wisconsin Act 21 did not allow the Wisconsin Superintendent of Public Instruction (SPI) and the Wisconsin Department of Public Instruction (DPI) to proceed with their duties of supervision without the Wisconsin Governor's and, in some circumstances, the Wisconsin Secretary of Administration's approval, Act 21 unconstitutionally vested the Governor and Secretary of Administration with the supervision of public instruction in violation of Wis. Const. art. X, § 1; hence, Act 21 was void as applied to the SPI and his subordinates.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

12 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


S.A.M. v. Meister (In re Meister)


No. 2014AP1283


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 22; 367 Wis. 2d 447; 876 N.W.2d 746; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 123


October 6, 2015, Argued 
April 7, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2011FA335). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Jefferson. JUDGE: William F. Hue.
Weber v. Meister (In re Meister), 2015 WI App 28, 361 Wis. 2d 286, 862 N.W.2d 619, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 88 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Wis. Stat. § 767.43(1) did not require a grandparent, greatgrandparent, or stepparent who filed a motion for visitation rights to prove that he or she maintained a relationship similar to a parent-child relationship with the child; rather, the parent-child relationship element applied only to a "person" seeking visitation rights who was not a grandparent, greatgrandparent, or stepparent; [2]-Visitation rights to grandparents, greatgrandparents, and stepparents under Wis. Stat. § 767.43(1) were allowed when visitation was in the best interest of the child, and it did not unconstitutionally infringe on parents' constitutional rights because any best interest determination gave special weight to a fit parent's decisions regarding the child's best interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

State v. Parisi


No. 2014AP1267-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 10; 367 Wis. 2d 1; 875 N.W.2d 619; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 10


October 5, 2015, Oral Argument 
February 24, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for certiorari filed at, 05/23/2016


PRIOR HISTORY: (L.C. No. 2013CF242). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Winnebago. JUDGE: Daniel J. Bissett.
State v. Parisi, 2015 WI App 20, 360 Wis. 2d 491, 864 N.W.2d 121, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 36 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The blood draw was constitutional because it was supported by exigent circumstances; given the rapid dissipation of heroin in the blood, the time needed to obtain a warrant, and defendant's unstable condition at the hospital, the officer might reasonably have believed that he was confronted with an emergency, in which the delay necessary to obtain a warrant, under the circumstances, threatened the destruction of evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Matalonis


No. 2014AP108-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 7; 366 Wis. 2d 443; 875 N.W.2d 567; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 7


September 18, 2015, Argued 
February 10, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Abrahamson, 2016 WI 78, 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 466 (2016)
Reconsideration denied by State v. Matalonis, 2016 WI 78, 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 469 (2016)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Matalonis v. Wisconsin, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 6080 (U.S., Oct. 11, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2012CF81). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Kenosha. JUDGE: Wilber W. Warren, III.
State v. Matalonis, 2015 WI App 13, 359 Wis. 2d 675, 859 N.W.2d 628, 2014 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1046 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The warrantless search by the police of defendant's home, importantly the room secured by the locked, blood-spattered door, was reasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11 because the police were exercising a bona fide community caretaker function when they searched the home; in light of all the facts that an officer had to consider, the blood outside the house, inside the house, and on the door itself, the fact that the door was locked, the conflicting stories, and the noises the officers had heard, the fact that the officer heard a fan inside the locked room and smelled marijuana did not negate the bona fide community caretaking function.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

15 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Hoffer Props., LLC v. DOT


No. 2012AP2520


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 5; 366 Wis. 2d 372; 874 N.W.2d 533; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 5


September 8, 2015, Argued 
February 4, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Jefferson. JUDGE: William F. Hue.
Hoffer Props., LLC v. State, 2014 WI App 71, 354 Wis. 2d 621, 848 N.W.2d 903, 2014 Wisc. App. LEXIS 357 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Wis. Stat. § 84.25(3) (2007-08) authorized the Wisconsin DOT to change the abutting property owner's access to the controlled-access highway in whatever way it deemed necessary or desirable; such changes, including elimination of direct access points, were duly authorized exercises of the police power and were not compensable under Wis. Stat. § 32.09 as long as alternate access was given that did not deprive the owner of all or substantially all beneficial use of the property; [2]-When the DOT changed a property owner's access to a controlled-access highway but other access was given or existed, the owner was precluded from compensation pursuant to § 32.09(6)(b) as a matter of law and no jury determination of reasonableness was required; hence, the owner was precluded from compensation under § 32.09(6)(b) because alternate access to the property was provided.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Winnebago Cnty. v. Christopher S. (In re Christopher S.)


No. 2014AP1048


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2016 WI 1; 366 Wis. 2d 1; 878 N.W.2d 109; 2016 Wisc. LEXIS 1


September 18, 2015, Oral Argument 
January 5, 2016, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Christopher S. v. Winnebago Cnty., 136 S. Ct. 2464, 195 L. Ed. 2d 805, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 3827 (U.S., June 13, 2016)
Appeal dismissed by Winnebago Cty. v. C.S. (In re C.S.), 2017 Wisc. App. LEXIS 602 (Wis. Ct. App., Aug. 16, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders issued by the Circuit Court for Winnebago County, Scott C. Woldt, Judge. (L.C. No. 2012ME5572).
Winnebago Cnty. v. Christopher S. (In re Christopher S.), 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 269 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 1, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Court properly granted the County's petition for the involuntary commitment of the inmate for mental health care; Wis. Stat. § 51.20(1)(ar) (2013-14) is facially constitutional under the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 1 because it is reasonably related to the State's legitimate interest in providing care and assistance to inmates suffering from mental illness; [2]-Court did not err when it found that the County established by clear and convincing evidence that the inmate was incompetent to refuse psychotropic medication because the medical expert's undisputed testimony sufficiently addressed and met the requirements outlined in Wis. Stat. § 51.61(1)(g)4.b. (2013-14).


OUTCOME: Orders affirmed.

State ex rel. Three Unnamed Petitioners v. Peterson


Nos. 2013AP2504-W, 2013AP2505-W, 2013AP2506-W, 2013AP2507-W, 2013AP2508-W, 2014AP296-OA, 2014AP417-W, 2014AP418-W, 2014AP419-W, 2014AP420-W, 2014AP421-W.


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2015 WI 103; 365 Wis. 2d 351; 875 N.W.2d 49; 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 710



December 2, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee, Iowa, Dodge, Dane and Columbia. JUDGE: Gregory A. Peterson (Reserve). (L.C. Nos. 2013JD11 & 2013JD9 & 2013JD6 & 2013JD1 & 2012JD23).
State ex rel. Two Unnamed Petitioners v. Peterson, 2015 WI 85, 363 Wis. 2d 1, 866 N.W.2d 165, 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 490 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Motion for reconsideration and motion for stay denied; mandate clarified.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-On a motion for reconsideration of the denial of a petition for a supervisory writ, the court clarified its decision that the special prosecutor in a John Doe investigation of campaign finance violations had been improperly appointed because none of the nine conditions set forth in Wis. Stat. § 978.045(1r) applied; [2]-The court concluded that the prosecutor could no longer act as special prosecutor, but that his acts taken to this point were not void; [3]-The court rejected the prosecutor's motion for reconsideration based on his contention that the investigation could be continued to determine whether there was coordination related to express advocacy because this argument had not been presented to or ruled upon by the lower court; [4]-The court made explicit its requirements for returning all documents and items seized in the investigation.


OUTCOME: Prosecutor's motion for reconsideration denied; motion for stay denied; mandate clarified to require the prosecutor to cease acting other than to return all documents and files obtained in the investigation.

 

19 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Iverson


No. 2014AP515-FT


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2015 WI 101; 365 Wis. 2d 302; 871 N.W.2d 661; 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 709


September 8, 2015, Oral Argument 
November 25, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. Nos. 2013TR4032 & 2013TR4033).
State v. Iverson, 2014 WI App 120, 358 Wis. 2d 712, 856 N.W.2d 346, 2014 Wisc. App. LEXIS 833 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A state traffic patrol officer was authorized to stop a vehicle when he saw the passenger throw a cigarette butt out the passenger-side window because the cigarette butt constituted "other discarded materials" within the definition of "solid waste" in the littering statute, Wis. Stat. §§ 287.81 and 289.01(33); [2]-The state patrol officer was authorized to enforce this law pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 345.22, Wis. Stat. § 110.07, Wis. Stat. § 968.07, and Wis. Stat. § 23.58; [3]-The trooper had probable cause to believe that an occupant of the vehicle had violated § 287.81 by throwing the cigarette butt, Wis. Stat. § 968.24, and evidence gathered from the driver during the stop should not have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: Reversed and cause remanded.

 

20 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



State ex rel. Two Unnamed Petitioners v. Peterson


No. 2014AP296-OA & 2014AP417-W through 2014AP421-W & 2013AP2504-W through 2013AP2508-W (L.C. No. 2013JD11 & 2013JD9 & 2013JD6 & 2013JD1 & 2012JD23)


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2015 WI 85; 363 Wis. 2d 1; 866 N.W.2d 165; 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 490



July 16, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by, Stay denied by State ex rel. Three Unnamed Petitioners v. Peterson, 2015 WI 103, 365 Wis. 2d 351, 875 N.W.2d 49, 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 710 (2015)
Motion granted by Chisholm v. Two Unnamed Petitioners, 136 S. Ct. 2459, 195 L. Ed. 2d 263, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 3371 (U.S., 2016)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Chisholm v. Two Unnamed, 137 S. Ct. 77, 196 L. Ed. 2d 198, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 4657 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: PETITION for supervisory writ and appeal from an order of a John Doe Judge for Milwaukee County, Iowa County, Dodge County, Dane County, and Columbia County, Gregory A, Peterson, Reserve Judge.

PETITION for supervisory writ and review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.
Three Unnamed Petitioners v. Peterson, 360 Wis. 2d 171, 857 N.W.2d 616, 2014 Wisc. LEXIS 1076 (Wis., 2014)



DISPOSITION: Declaration of rights; relief granted; John Doe investigation ordered closed. Petition for supervisory writ denied and order affirmed. Petition for supervisory writ denied and decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In the first case, the special prosecutor's theory of the case was invalidated because the definition of "political purposes" in Wis. Stat. § 11.01(16) (2011-12) was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague under U.S. Const. amend. I and Wis. Const. art. I, § 3; [2]-In the second case, the special prosecutor failed to prove that the reserve judge violated a plain legal duty when he quashed the subpoenas and search warrants and ordered the return of all property seized by the special prosecutor; the reserve judge exercised his discretion under the John Doe statute, Wis. Stat. § 968.26 (2011-12), to determine the extent of the investigation; [3]-In the third case, the unnamed movants failed to prove that the reserve judges violated a plain legal duty by accepting an appointment as a reserve judge, convening a multi-county John Doe proceeding, or appointing a special prosecutor.


OUTCOME: Relief granted in part, petition denied in part, judgment affirmed in part.

State v. Houghton


No. 2013AP1581-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2015 WI 79; 364 Wis. 2d 234; 868 N.W.2d 143; 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 484


April 22, 2015, Oral Argument 
July 14, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Walworth. JUDGE: John R. Race. (L.C. No. 2012CF187). (Reported at 2014 WI App 71, 354 Wis. 2d 623, 848 N.W.2d 904). (Ct. App. 2014 -- Unpublished).
State v. Houghton, 2014 WI App 71, 354 Wis. 2d 623, 848 N.W.2d 904, 2014 Wisc. App. LEXIS 373 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11, an objectively reasonable mistake of law by a police officer could form the basis for reasonable suspicion to conduct a traffic stop; all Wisconsin cases holding otherwise were overruled to the extent they conflicted with that holding; [2]-Wis. Stat. § 346.88, which required that an object "obstruct" a driver's clear view to be a violation did not mean that every object in a driver's clear view was a violation; rather, § 346.88 required a material obstruction--even if minor--in order to be considered a violation of the statute; [3]-The officer's mistake of law as to whether an air freshener and GPS on defendant's windshield violated § 346.88 was objectively reasonable, and therefore, the stop of defendant's vehicle was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

State v. Hogan


No. 2013AP430-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2015 WI 76; 364 Wis. 2d 167; 868 N.W.2d 124; 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 348


March 4, 2015, Oral Argument 
July 10, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. (Reported at 2014 WI App 71, 354 Wis. 2d 622, 848 N.W.2d 903). (Ct. App. 2014 -- Unpublished). REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Grant. JUDGE: Craig R. Day. (L.C. No. 2012CF147).
State v. Hogan, 2014 WI App 71, 354 Wis. 2d 622, 848 N.W.2d 903, 2014 Wisc. App. LEXIS 398 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An extension of a traffic stop for field sobriety tests was not a lawful investigatory stop under the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV, because a deputy's observations that defendant was shaking and appeared to be very nervous did not suffice to establish reasonable suspicion; [2]-After defendant passed the field sobriety tests and the deputy told defendant that he was free to leave, the traffic stop had ended and defendant was not constructively seized when the deputy then requested and obtained consent to search defendant's vehicle; [3]-There was no need to determine whether defendant's consent was sufficiently attenuated because the unlawful extension of the stop was not a but-for cause of the consent and thus did not taint the search; [4]-Accordingly, the circuit court did not err in denying motions to suppress evidence of drugs and weapons found in the vehicle.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN

April 21, 2015, Oral Argument 
July 10, 2015, Filed

Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Williams v. Eckstein, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 19904 (E.D. Wis., Feb. 13, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Jeffrey A. Wagner, Judge. (L.C. No. 2013CF30).
State v. Williams, 2014 Wisc. App. LEXIS 922 (Wis. Ct. App., Nov. 6, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Convictions under erroneous jury instructions were subject to harmless error review; when an erroneous instruction was given but it was clear beyond a reasonable doubt that the jury would have convicted defendant had the proper instruction been given, the jury verdict could be affirmed; [2]-The erroneous jury instruction was harmless error and there was sufficient evidence to convict defendant of felony murder; [3]-The probative value of photographs of the crime scene and the victims' fatal wounds was not substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice under Wis. Stat. § 904.03 because they were useful in helping the jury garner a more thorough understanding of the events on the night of the killings; they were neither overly gruesome nor unfairly prejudicial, and the purpose of the photographs was to prove an element of the crimes charged.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Wilson

SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2015 WI 48; 362 Wis. 2d 193; 864 N.W.2d 52; 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 312


September 4, 2014, Argued 
May 12, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition denied by State v. Wilson, 2015 WI 91, 364 Wis. 2d 543, 870 N.W.2d 465, 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 510 (2015)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wilson v. Wis., 2016 U.S. LEXIS 1727 (U.S., Mar. 7, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Victor Manian. (L.C. No. 1993CF931541).
State v. Wilson, 2014 Wisc. LEXIS 714 (Wis., Sept. 4, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The reversal of defendant's first-degree intentional homicide conviction was improper because, the although the Denny test was the appropriate test for circuit courts to use to determine the admissibility of third-party perpetrator evidence, for a defendant to show that a third party had the "opportunity" to commit a crime by employing a gunman or gunmen to kill the victim, defendant was required to provide some evidence that the third party had the realistic ability to engineer such a scenario; [2]-Defendant failed to show that the third party had the opportunity to kill the victim, directly or indirectly and thus, it was not error for the circuit court to exclude defendant's proffered evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Schwegel v. Milwaukee County


No. 2012AP2490


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2015 WI 12; 360 Wis. 2d 654; 859 N.W.2d 78; 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 13; 165 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P61,565


October 1, 2014, Oral Argument 
February 12, 2015, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.

(L.C. No. 2012CV1528). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Christopher R. Foley.
Wis. Fedn. & Health Professionals v. Milwaukee County, 2013 WI App 134, 351 Wis. 2d 421, 839 N.W.2d 869, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 819 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; cause remanded to the circuit court to dismiss the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The county did not abrogate a vested contract right when, through Milwaukee Co., Wis., General Ordinance § 17.14(7)(ee)(1) (2011), it prospectively modified a health insurance benefit it offered for employees who had not yet retired; [2]-County employees had a vested contract right to Medicare Part B premium reimbursement when they fulfilled all three criteria for its payment: (1) reaching retirement age; (2) providing 15 or more years of credited county service; and (3) retiring before the dates established by the county; employees who did not meet all three criteria did not fulfill the requirements necessary to establish a vested contract right to reimbursement.


OUTCOME: Affirmed and remanded.

State v. Alger (In re Alger)


Nos. 2013AP225 & 2013AP578


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2015 WI 3; 360 Wis. 2d 193; 858 N.W.2d 346; 2015 Wisc. LEXIS 2


October 2, 2014, Oral Argument 
January 20, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit/Circuit. COUNTY: Outagamie/Dane. JUDGE: John A. Des Jardins/Nicholas McNamara. (L.C. Nos. 2004CV654 & 2002CI3).
State v. Alger (In re Alger), 2013 WI App 148, 352 Wis. 2d 145, 841 N.W.2d 329, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 976 (2013)
State v. Knipfer (In re Knipfer), 2014 WI App 9, 352 Wis. 2d 563, 842 N.W.2d 526, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1073 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Daubert evidentiary standard under Wis. Stat. § 907.02(1) (2011-12) did not apply to expert testimony in trials on appellants inmates' petitions for discharge from their Wis. Stat. ch. 980 commitments because the petitions were continuations of their original commitments to which Daubert did not apply, instead of commencing new "actions" or "special proceedings," and this was not an absurd result the legislature did not intend; [2]-Not applying Daubert did not offend equal protection or substantive due process because no fundamental right was implicated, and the legislature had a rational basis for applying the same evidentiary standard to expert testimony in all proceedings on the inmates' commitments.


OUTCOME: Judgments affirmed.

State v. Kennedy


No. 2012AP523-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2014 WI 132; 359 Wis. 2d 454; 856 N.W.2d 834; 2014 Wisc. LEXIS 954


September 9, 2014, Oral Argument 
December 26, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Jeffrey A. Wagner. (L.C. No. 2006CF4053).
State v. Kennedy, 2013 WI App 73, 348 Wis. 2d 263, 831 N.W.2d 824, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 309 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Police had probable cause to believe that defendant committed a drunk driving offense because an officer observed block-long skid marks leading to defendant's car, the results of a high speed impact, and that defendant's eyes were bloodshot and glassy, he was slurring his speech, he was swaying, and he smelled of alcohol; [2]-Although no exigent circumstances were argued to justify a warrantless blood draw under U.S. Const. amend. IV, the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule applied because police acted in objectively reasonable accord with the clear and settled Wisconsin precedent holding that the natural dissipation of alcohol in the bloodstream of a suspect created a sufficient exigency to justify a warrantless investigatory blood draw.


OUTCOME: Decision of the court of appeals affirmed.

State v. Gonzalez

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:

League of Women Voters v. Walker


No. 2012AP584


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2014 WI 97; 357 Wis. 2d 360; 851 N.W.2d 302; 2014 Wisc. LEXIS 535



July 31, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2011CV4669). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Richard G. Niess.
League of Women Voters of Wis. Educ. Network, Inc. v. Walker, 2013 WI App 77, 348 Wis. 2d 714, 834 N.W.2d 393, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 459 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Modified and as modified, affirmed; injunction vacated; cause remanded to circuit court to dismiss the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether portions of a voter ID law, 2011 Wis. Sess. Laws 23 (Act 23), were unconstitutional. HOLDINGS: [1]-The legislature did not exceed its authority under Wisc. Const. art. III, § 1 by requiring electors to present Act 23-acceptable photo ID, as it was within its province to require any prospective voter to furnish such proof as it deemed requisite that he was a qualified elector, and requiring photo ID did not impose an elector qualification in addition to those set out in § 1; [2]-Act 23 was within the legislature's authority to enact laws regarding voter registration under Wisc. Const. art. III, § 2 because Act 23-acceptable photo ID was the mode for verifying that a potential voter was the elector listed on the registration list; [3]-Act 23 was a reasonable regulation that could improve and modernize election procedures, safeguard voter confidence, and deter voter fraud.


OUTCOME: The decision of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed as modified and the matter was remanded to the trial court to dismiss the voters group's lawsuit.

Appling v. Walker


No. 2011AP1572


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2014 WI 96; 358 Wis. 2d 132; 853 N.W.2d 888; 2014 Wisc. LEXIS 533



July 31, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2010CV4434). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Daniel R. Moeser.
Appling v. Doyle, 2013 WI App 3, 345 Wis. 2d 762, 826 N.W.2d 666, 2012 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1016 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether Wis. Stat. ch. 770, by which the legislature created the legal status of domestic partnership for same-sex couples, violated Wis. Const. art. XIII, § 13. HOLDINGS: [1]-The court of appeals' holding that ch. 770 was constitutional was proper, based on the presumption of constitutionality, plaintiffs' failure to meet the burden of proof, and the evidence reviewed in accord with the Dairyland framework used to interpret constitutional provisions; [2]-Evidence from the drafting and ratification process demonstrated that the framers of the amendment intended specifically to allow legislation that provided a set of rights and benefits to same-sex couples, and during the constitutional ratification process, proponents explicitly mentioned same-sex intimate relationships when voters raised questions about what kind of relationship might legally be recognized if it passed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Madison Teachers, Inc. v. Walker


No. 2012AP2067


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN

DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:

HOLDINGS: [1]-A decision invalidating portions the Act was improper, as the constitutional right to freedom of association of "general employees" was not infringed upon by the Act; collective bargaining remained a creation of legislative grace and not constitutional obligation, and the First Amendment could not be used as a vehicle to expand the parameters of a benefit that it did not itself protect; [2]-Wis. Stat. § 62.623 did not violate the home rule amendment, Wis. Const. art. XI, § 3(1), because § 62.623 primarily concerned a matter of statewide concern; [3]-Plaintiffs' Contract Clause claim failed, as the City of Milwaukee was not contractually obligated to pay the employee share of contributions to the Milwaukee Employee Retirement System.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

Milwaukee Branch of NAACP v. Walker

SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2014 WI 98; 357 Wis. 2d 469; 851 N.W.2d 262; 2014 Wisc. LEXIS 534



July 31, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration dismissed by, As moot, Motion denied by Milwaukee Branch of NAACP v. Walker, 2014 WI 117, 856 N.W.2d 177, 2014 Wisc. LEXIS 731 (2014)

DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; permanent and temporary injunctions vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Wisconsin's voter photo identification act, 2011 Wis. Act 23, does not violate Wis. Const. art. III, § 1 because the burdens of time and inconvenience associated with obtaining acceptable photo identification are not undue burdens on the right to vote; [2]-In order to resolve a conflict between Act 23 (prohibiting a fee) and its implementing rules (requiring documents for which fees are charged), the court held that Department of Transportation photo identification cards for voting must be issued without requiring documents for which an elector must pay a fee to a government agency, and the court explained the procedure for an elector to follow; [3]-Act 23 is reasonably related to the State's significant interests.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed and the permanent and temporary injunctions were vacated.

State v. Brown


No. 2011AP2907-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2014 WI 69; 355 Wis. 2d 668; 850 N.W.2d 66; 2014 Wisc. LEXIS 483


January 15, 2014, Argued 
July 16, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Rebecca F. Dallet. (L.C. No. 2010CF3318).
State v. Brown, 2013 WI App 17, 346 Wis. 2d 98, 827 N.W.2d 903, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 36 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where officers stopped a vehicle based on an unlit light bulb in the vehicle's tail lamp and found a gun during a search, suppression was warranted under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11 because there was no probable cause or reasonable suspicion to stop the vehicle since having one unlit bulb on the back of the vehicle did not on its own violate the statutory requirements for tail lamps, and an officer's mistake of law was not sufficient grounds for a stop; [2]-Wis. OUTCOME: Court of appeals' decision affirmed.

53 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Bostco LLC v. Milwaukee Metro. Sewerage Dist.


No. 2007AP221 & 2007AP1440


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 78; 350 Wis. 2d 554; 835 N.W.2d 160; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 290


September 6, 2012, Argued 
July 18, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2003CV5040). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Jean A. DiMotto & Jeffrey A. Kremers.
Bostco LLC v. Milwaukee Metro. Sewerage Dist., 2011 WI App 76, 334 Wis. 2d 620, 800 N.W.2d 518, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 411 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed in part and reversed in part the circuit court's decision in favor of defendant Milwaukee Metropolitan Sewerage District (MMSD) on plaintiff landowner's allegation that MMSD's negligent operation and maintenance of a sewerage tunnel (Deep Tunnel) beneath the landowner's property resulted in excessive groundwater seepage, causing damage to the landowner's buildings. The landowner petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the landowner proved that MMSD negligently caused a continuing private nuisance due to the manner in which MMSD chose to maintain the Deep Tunnel. MMSD had notice that excessively siphoning groundwater from around the landowner's building was interfering with the landowner's use and enjoyment of its property by damaging the foundation of the building. The circuit court properly concluded that MMSD was required to abate the private nuisance caused by MMSD's negligence maintenance of the Deep Tunnel. The supreme court concluded that the plain meaning of Wis. Stat. § 893.80(3) (2011-12) was to limit the dollar amount of recovery to be paid for damages, injuries or death to $50,000 per claimant, but the provision had no bearing on the availability of equitable relief such as abatement. A municipal entity may be subjected to claims for equitable relief to abate a negligently maintained nuisance that was a cause of significant harm and of which the municipal entity had notice. A rational basis existed for the damage limitations in § 893.80(3). The landowner substantially complied with the notice of claim requirements of Wis. Stat. § 893.80(1) (2011-12).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed at that decision that the landowner was not entitled to equitable relief in the form of an order for abatement and remanded to the circuit court; the judgment was affirmed on all other issues.

 

54 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Rock-Koshkonong Lake District v. State Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 2008AP1523


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 74; 350 Wis. 2d 45; 833 N.W.2d 800; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 285


September 5, 2012, Argued 
July 16, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. (L.C. No. 2006CV1846). COUNTY: Rock. JUDGE: Daniel T. Dillon.
Rock-Koshkonong Lake Dist. v. State Dep't of Natural Res., 2011 WI App 115, 336 Wis. 2d 677, 803 N.W.2d 853, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 569 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners filed a petition to raise the Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources-designated water levels of a lake. Respondent, the Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources (DNR), rejected the petition, and its denial was affirmed by an administrative law judge, by the county circuit court, and by the Wisconsin Court of Appeals. Petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The DNR properly considered the impact of the petition's proposed water levels on public and private wetlands in and adjacent to the lake. However, the DNR inappropriately relied on the public trust doctrine for its authority to protect non-navigable land and non-navigable water above the ordinary high water mark. But, the DNR had broad statutory authority grounded in the state's police power to protect non-navigable wetlands and other non-navigable water resources. Thus, contrary to petitioners' contentions, the DNR could consider the water level impact on all adjacent property under Wis. Stat. § 31.02(1) (2009-10). In addition, under Wis. Stat. § 31.02(1) (2009-10), the DNR rightly considered the direct impact of lower water levels on riparian properties, but wrongly excluded the cumulative economic effect of the lower water levels on those properties. The DNR had to consider the economic impacts of the lower water levels. Thus, the DNR erred when it excluded testimony on economic impacts of lower water levels when making a water level determination under Wis. Stat. § 31.02(1) (2009-10).


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and remanded the case to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Dane County v. Sheila W. (In re Interest of Sheila W.)


No. 2012AP500


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 63; 348 Wis. 2d 674; 835 N.W.2d 148; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 272


April 11, 2013, Argued 
July 10, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2012JC55). COURT: Dane. COUNTY: Circuit. JUDGE: William C. Foust.
Dane County v. Sheila W., 2013 WI 22, 346 Wis. 2d 282, 827 N.W.2d 373, 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 40 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court appointed a temporary guardian under Wis. Stat. § 54.50 to decide whether to consent to medical treatment for petitioner minor, who had been diagnosed with aplastic anemia and opposed life-saving blood transfusions on religious grounds. The order expired while the minor's appeal was pending, and the Court of Appeals, Wisconsin, dismissed the appeal as moot. The minor sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Wisconsin agreed with the determination that the appeal was moot because no determination of the court would have any practical legal effect upon an existing controversy, given that the order being appealed had expired. There was no request to extend the order and no indication that respondent county sought any additional order. Further, although the case presented issues of great public importance, the court deemed it unwise to decide such substantial social policy issues with far-ranging implications based on a singular fact situation in a case that is moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals.

 

56 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Neumann


No. 2011AP1044-CR & 2011AP1105-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 58; 348 Wis. 2d 455; 832 N.W.2d 560; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 269


December 4, 2012, Argued 
July 3, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Neumann v. Wisconsin, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 7800 (U.S., Nov. 4, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from judgments and orders of the Circuit Court for Marathon County, Vincent K. Howard, Judge. (L.C. No. 2008CF324 & 2008CF323). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Marathon. JUDGE: Vincent K. Howard.
State v. Neumann, 2012 Wisc. App. LEXIS 448 (Wis. Ct. App., May 1, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were separately convicted, in the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin) of their child's second-degree reckless homicide, under Wis. Stat. § 940.06(1) (2009-10), and their requests for postconviction relief, under Wis. Stat. §§ 809.30 and 974.02 (2009-10), were denied. The case was certified to the Wisconsin Supreme Court to determine the scope of the prayer treatment exception in Wis. Stat. § 948.03(6) (2009-10).


OVERVIEW: Defendants tried prayer treatment. They said their prosecutions were unconstitutional because Wis. Stat. § 948.03(6) (2009-10) protected prayer treatment but Wis. Stat. § 940.06(1) (2009-10) criminalized it. The supreme court disagreed because (1) the reckless homicide statute differed from Wis. Stat. § 948.03(a) and (c) (2009-10), the criminal child abuse statute to which the prayer provision applied, in the reckless nature of conduct, the mental state required, and the harm caused, so each gave fair notice of when actors might be liable or protected, and (2) juries could reasonably find defendants created a substantial risk of death, subjectively knew the risk, and caused the death. Wis. Stat. § 751.06 (2009-10) did not require reversal because (1) the jury was properly instructed on their duty to provide medical care and the crime's subjective awareness element, and (2) counsel was not ineffective. Nothing showed being told of the mother's conviction biased the father's jurors because, (1) to convict him, the jury had to find he subjectively knew his conduct created a substantial risk to the child, and (2) the jury was told the trials' results could differ.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions and orders denying postconviction relief were affirmed.

 

57 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sobczak


No. 2010AP3034-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 52; 347 Wis. 2d 724; 833 N.W.2d 59; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 264


December 4, 2012, Oral Argument 
June 20, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sobczak v. Wisconsin, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 8142 (U.S., Nov. 12, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2009CF297). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Washington. JUDGE: Patrick J. Faragher.
State v. Sobczak, 2012 WI App 6, 338 Wis. 2d 410, 808 N.W.2d 730, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1016 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a trial for possession of child pornography, the circuit court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence from a warrantless entry of his home search of his computer, finding that his girlfriend, who was staying with defendant for the weekend, had authority to consent to the search. The Court of Appeals, Wisconsin, affirmed, and defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's girlfriend, who was staying in defendant's home for the weekend, was alone while defendant was at work and using his laptop with his permission. She observed what appeared to be child pornography, arranged for the police to be called, and consented to an officer's entry into the home and inspection of the material on the computer. The Wisconsin Supreme Court found no Fourth Amendment violation. The girlfriend had a sufficient relationship to the premises to establish actual authority to consent to the officer's entry. Significant factors included the three-month duration of her relationship with defendant, the fact the he encouraged her to spend an evening alone in the home, and the fact that he placed no apparent restrictions on her use of the house. The court believed society would have expected a girlfriend of three months, left alone in a home and given unrestricted access to the common areas of the home, to enjoy the authority to invite guests in to those common areas, even with potentially deleterious consequences to her boyfriend. The girlfriend also had authority to consent to the search of the laptop, which she had permission to use.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Court of Appeals.

 

58 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sahs


No. 2009AP2916-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 51; 347 Wis. 2d 641; 832 N.W.2d 80; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 262


February 25, 2013, Oral Argument 
June 18, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2008CF3217). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Jeffrey A. Conen.
State v. Sahs, 2010 WI App 159, 330 Wis. 2d 498, 792 N.W.2d 240, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 853 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of child pornography under Wis. Stat. § 948.12(1m) (2007-2008).


OVERVIEW: While on probation for a previous child pornography conviction, defendant was required to participate in sex offender group therapy. Defendant told his probation agent that he had used a computer he kept at a friend's house to access child pornography. The police investigated and found the computer, which led to a revocation of defendant's probation and additional criminal charges. Defendant asserted that he had signed a Wisconsin Department of Corrections form advising him that statements he made to his probation agent could not be used against him in criminal proceedings. He further asserted that he had been scheduled to take a mandatory polygraph test the day after his conversation with the probation agent. The court concluded that defendant had not met his burden of proving that his statements to his probation agent were compelled for Fifth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. V, self-incrimination purposes because the record lacked sufficient evidence regarding his conditions of probation. Defendant's probation rules were not in the record. The record did not contain the form defendant described, nor did it show that defendant had been scheduled to take a mandatory polygraph test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

59 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Masters


No. 2011AP1240


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 43; 347 Wis. 2d 238; 830 N.W.2d 647; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 179


September 7, 2012, Oral Argument 
May 17, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Kathryn W. Foster, Judge. (L.C. No. 1988FA73).
Johnson v. Masters, 2012 WI 77, 342 Wis. 2d 160, 816 N.W.2d 324, 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 435 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife moved to compel respondent ex-husband to provide pension information so that a qualified domestic relations order (QDRO) could be prepared and his Wisconsin Retirement System (WRS) pension could be divided in accordance with their 1989 divorce judgment. The Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Wisconsin, denied the motion on the grounds that the motion was barred by Wis. Stat. § 893.40, a statute of repose. The ex-wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: Divorce judgment, which had been filed more than 20 years before, had awarded the ex-wife half of the value accrued during the span of the marriage and stated that a QDRO "shall be submitted to secure these rights." The appellate court held that the motion was not barred by the operation of § 893.40, a 20-year statute of repose because, at the time of the divorce judgment, Wis. Stat. § 40.08(1) (1987-88) precluded assigning the WRS pension; the divorce judgment contained a provision that required the filing of a QDRO with the WRS; and it was not until 1998 that 1997 Wis. Sess. Laws 125, § 5 authorized WRS to accept such orders for marriages, such as between the parties, that were terminated in 1989.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the circuit court and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Travis


No. 2011AP685-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 38; 347 Wis. 2d 142; 832 N.W.2d 491; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 173


January 10, 2013, Oral Argument 
May 2, 2013, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
Court: Circuit. County: Kenosha. Judge: Wilbur Warren III.
State v. Travis, 2012 WI App 46, 340 Wis. 2d 639, 813 N.W.2d 702, 2012 Wisc. App. LEXIS 211 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Court of Appeals modified the judgment of conviction entered by the trial court after defendant was convicted following a guilty plea of attempted first-degree sexual assault of a child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1)(d) (2010) and an agreement was reached that the provision violated was actually Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1)(e) (2010). It then ordered that he be resentenced. The state supreme court granted review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with one count of attempted first-degree sexual assault of a child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1)(d) (2010). The complaint and information charged a violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1)(d) (2010), but did not contain any allegations supporting the "use or threat of force or violence" element. Defendant was convicted on his plea of guilty to a violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1)(d) (2010). The appellate court ordered the judgment of conviction to be amended according to the agreement of the prosecuting attorney, defense counsel, defendant, and the trial court to list the correct crime, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1)(e) (2010). It also directed that defendant be resentenced accordingly. The state supreme court found that the trial court's error in incorrectly concluding that the five-year mandatory minimum sentence of the incorrect statutory provision applied did not belong to the class of cases involving structural error. Nevertheless, it determined that the State had not met its burden of showing that the error in not applying the correct statutory provision, which had no minimum, did not affect the eight-year sentence the trial court imposed.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment and order that the case be remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

 

61 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brereton


No. 2010AP1366-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 17; 345 Wis. 2d 563; 826 N.W.2d 369; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 15



February 6, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Brereton v. Wis., 2013 U.S. LEXIS 6283 (U.S., Oct. 7, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Walworth. JUDGE: Michael S. Gibbs.
State v. Brereton, 2011 WI App 127, 337 Wis. 2d 145, 804 N.W.2d 243, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 647 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to suppress evidence was denied, defendant pleaded guilty to several counts related to burglaries. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the court of appeals erred by upholding the denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained through monitoring by a global positioning system (GPS) device installed on defendant's vehicle. The supreme court disagreed. The three-hour seizure of defendant's vehicle, whereby officers were able to install the GPS device, did not constitute an unreasonable seizure under U.S. Const. amend. IV, as applied to automobiles. The officers' decision to obtain a warrant prior to conducting the GPS search was proper. The seizure of defendant's vehicle was supported by probable cause that the vehicle was, or contained, evidence of a crime, and was therefore permissible. The seizure was supported by witnesses' reports that a car matching the make, model, and license plate number of that particular vehicle had been seen at the locations of recent burglaries in the area. That the device provided officers with real-time updates of movements did not alter the kind of information to be obtained under the warrant, or the nature of the intrusion allowed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Gracia


No. 2011AP813-CR & 2011AP814


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2013 WI 15; 345 Wis. 2d 488; 826 N.W.2d 87; 2013 Wisc. LEXIS 13



January 31, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.
State v. Gracia, 2012 WI App 11, 338 Wis. 2d 486, 808 N.W.2d 743, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1040 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which upheld an order convicting him of operating with a prohibited alcohol content, fourth offense, with an alcohol fine enhancer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled no contest to operating with a prohibited alcohol content, fourth offense, with an alcohol fine enhancer. The court of appeals affirmed the judgment. On review, the court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress. The police were following up on a major single-vehicle accident that left the front end of the car driven by defendant extensively damaged and a traffic pole completely knocked down. They validly entered the home where he resided on consent of his brother and after the brother broke open his bedroom door, without any prompting by the police, reasonably exercised their community caretaker function when they crossed the threshold into the bedroom. The police acted on their concern that he might have sustained a significant injury in the automobile accident. Further, the trial court properly denied defendant's collateral attack of his 1998 operating a motor vehicle under the influence conviction and thus considered the conviction in determining that he had three prior relevant convictions. Despite a technically deficient plea colloquy, he knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his right to counsel in the 1998 case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Brenner v. New Richmond Reg'l Airport Comm'n & New Richmond


No. 2010AP342


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 98; 343 Wis. 2d 320; 816 N.W.2d 291; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 392


February 7, 2012, Argued 
July 17, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, On remand at Brenner v. City of New Richmond, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 394 (Wis. Ct. App., May 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2007CV1153). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: St. Croix. JUDGE: Howard W. Cameron, Jr.
Brenner v. City of New Richmond, 2011 WI App 99, 334 Wis. 2d 807, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 749 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court dismissed the inverse condemnation claims of plaintiff landowners whose property was close or immediately adjacent to defendant airport. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin reversed. The state supreme court accepted the airport's petition for review.


OVERVIEW: The landowners alleged that an extension of the airport's runway amounted to the compensable taking of an easement because the resulting overflights had adverse effects on their properties, including diminished use and enjoyment and decrease of value. In the inverse condemnation case filed under Wis. Stat. § 32.10, the circuit court erred by applying the standard for a regulatory taking. The Supreme Court of Wisconsin held that the standard for a taking in an airplane overflight case was whether the overflights were low enough and frequent enough to have a direct and immediate effect on the use and enjoyment of the person's property. If this standard could be satisfied, the government had taken an easement without paying compensation for it.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed. The case was remanded to the circuit court to make factual findings and apply the correct standard to determine whether there were takings of plaintiffs' properties.

 

64 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 2010AP1192-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 91; 342 Wis. 2d 710; 817 N.W.2d 410; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 384


March 13, 2012, Argued 
July 12, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smith v. Wisconsin, 133 S. Ct. 635, 184 L. Ed. 2d 405, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 8854 (U.S., 2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Motion denied by, As moot, Dismissed by Smith v. Schwochert, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 91998 (E.D. Wis., July 15, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Brown. (L.C. No. 2007CF875). JUDGE: Sue E. Bischel.
State v. Smith, 2011 WI App 99, 334 Wis. 2d 808, 800 N.W.2d 958, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 422 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a case in which defendant was convicted of being a party to the crime of possession with intent to deliver more than 10,000 grams of tetrahydrocannabinol, the Wisconsin Court of Appeals found the evidence sufficient to support defendant's conviction but remanded the cause for a determination of the proper remedy after finding he did not waive his right to a jury determination of the drug quantity. Both defendant and the State sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stipulated to the fact that the packages seized by the police contained more than 10,000 grams of tetrahydrocannabinol. The court held that appellate courts had to defer to reasonable inferences drawn by the jury from the evidence and had to consider the totality of the evidence when conducting a sufficiency of the evidence inquiry. Because a reasonable inference of defendant's guilt could have been drawn by the jury from the evidence presented at trial, viewed in its entirety, the evidence was sufficient to sustain his conviction. Defendant had a constitutional right to a jury determination of the drug quantity involved in his offense because the fact in question exposed him to a higher penalty. The trial court thus erred in determining the question without eliciting from defendant a proper waiver of his jury trial right. He was never informed he had a constitutional right to a jury determination of the drug quantity, nor was he ever given the opportunity to waive or invoke the right. However, the error was harmless because it was clear beyond a reasonable doubt that a properly instructed, rational jury would have found him guilty of the charged offense absent the error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and reinstated defendant's guilty verdict and judgment of conviction.

Kroner v. Oneida Seven Generations Corp.


No. 2010AP2533


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 88; 342 Wis. 2d 626; 819 N.W.2d 264; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 378


March 7, 2012, Argued 
July 11, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2008CV2234). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Brown. JUDGE: Donald R. Zuidmulder.
Kroner v. Oneida Seven Generations Corp., 2011 WI App 114, 336 Wis. 2d 476, 801 N.W.2d 350, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 429 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner filed a petition for review of the judgment of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which affirmed the decision of the circuit court, granting the motion to transfer the case to the Oneida Tribal Court filed by respondent tribally chartered corporate entity.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was terminated from his job as chief executive officer of the tribally chartered corporate entity. After his termination, the petitioner filed suit. The reviewing court held that the order to transfer was an erroneous exercise of the circuit court's discretion, because the facts and the applicable law were not fully stated and considered together in making both the determinations that Wis. Stat. § 801.54 (2009-10) required. A court that was considering transferring a case to a tribal court under the tribal transfer statute must conduct a two-part analysis. It must make a clear record of its findings and conclusions regarding concurrent jurisdiction, as well as an analysis of all of the rule's relevant factors on the facts presented. The record did not show that the facts of record and law relied upon were stated and were considered together in reaching the conclusion that the transfer to tribal court was warranted. Also, analysis was needed on the question of whether Wis. Stat. § 801.54 was retroactively applicable where the case was filed before the rule took effect but where the circuit court ruled on a transfer motion brought after the rule took effect.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Wisconsin v. Gilbert (In re Gilbert)

SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 72; 342 Wis. 2d 82; 816 N.W.2d 215; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 365


January 10, 2012, Argued 
June 29, 2012, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gilbert v. Wisconsin, 133 S. Ct. 560, 184 L. Ed. 2d 364, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 8361 (U.S., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2006CI12 & 2007CI9). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Jeffrey A. Wagner (In case 10AP594). Jeffrey A. Conen (In case 10AP1155).
State v. Gilbert (In re Commitment of Gilbert), 2011 WI App 61, 333 Wis. 2d 157, 798 N.W.2d 889, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 283 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Trial courts denied petitioners' postconviction motions to dismiss commitment petitions filed by the State pursuant to Wis. Stat. ch. 980. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin affirmed, holding that dismissal of a ch. 980 proceeding was not required when the subject of the petition was transferred to the custody of the Department of Corrections before a ch. 990 commitment order was entered. Petitioners sought review.


OVERVIEW: Both petitioners were found to be sexually violent persons and ordered to be committed under Wis. Stat. ch. 980, and then had their parole and extended supervision revoked and were incarcerated. On appeal, the court held that ch. 980 did not require the dismissal of a pending commitment petition when the individual subject to the petition was incarcerated because of the revocation of either parole or extended supervision, and therefore both petitioners were properly committed under ch. 980 after their parole and extended supervision, respectively, were revoked. The court held that ch. 980 did not require a dismissal because it: (1) did not contain language allowing for dismissal in the instant case; (2) did not set a time period for execution of a commitment order; and (3) stated that an individual could be simultaneously committed under ch. 980 and incarcerated at a Department of Corrections facility.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Anagnos (In re Anagnos)


NO. 2010AP1812


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 64; 341 Wis. 2d 576; 815 N.W.2d 675; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 360


April 24, 2012, Oral Argument 
June 26, 2012, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No.2010TR334). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Walworth. JUDGE: Robert J. Kennedy.
State v. Anagnos (In re Anagnos), 2011 WI App 118, 337 Wis. 2d 57, 805 N.W.2d 722, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 594 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the circuit court's determination that the traffic stop of defendant's vehicle was unconstitutional and that his operating privileges should not have been revoked on account of his refusal to take a chemical test to determine the presence or quantity of alcohol in his blood or breath.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed the determination that the traffic stop of defendant's vehicle was unconstitutional and that his operating privileges should not have been revoked on account of his refusal to take a chemical test to determine the presence or quantity of alcohol in his blood or breath and the supreme court reversed. The arresting officer pointed to specific and articulable facts, which taken together with rational inferences from those facts, gave rise to the reasonable suspicion necessary for an investigative stop. Because the stop of defendant's vehicle was supported by reasonable suspicion, the circuit court erred in concluding that the stop was unconstitutional and that he was not lawfully placed under arrest. The case was further remanded to the circuit court to revoke defendant's operating privilege under Wis. Stat. § 343.305(9)(d) (2009-10). The facts, as articulated by the deputy, led to a reasonable suspicion that the driver of the vehicle made a series of unusual and impulsive driving choices, suggestive of impairment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the circuit court to revoke defendant's operating privilege.

 

68 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 2010AP1551-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 59; 341 Wis. 2d 191; 814 N.W.2d 460; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 353


December 1, 2011, Oral Argument 
May 30, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County, James P. Daley, Judge. COURT: CIRCUIT. COUNTY: ROCK. JUDGE: JAMES P. DALEY. (L.C. No. 2008CF3468).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest to a charge of manufacturing tetrahydrocannabinol (THC), in violation of Wis. Stat. § 961.41(1)(h)(3). The Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) sentenced defendant to four years probation with six months conditional jail time. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the search warrant that was issued for his home by a circuit court commissioner was invalid as beyond the lawful authority of court commissioners, and that the evidence obtained upon the execution of the warrant should have been suppressed. Wis. Stat. § 757.69(1)(b), which granted circuit court commissioners the power to issue search warrants, was constitutional. The issuance of a search warrant was not an exercise of "the judicial power," as that phrase was employed in Wis. Const. art. VII, § 2. Instead, it required that the individual be authorized by law to issue the warrant, that he or she be neutral and detached, and that the warrant be issued only upon a showing of probable cause. Furthermore, Wis. Stat. § 757.69(1)(b) did not impermissibly intrude upon the judicial power granted to the courts by Wis. Const. art. VII, § 2. Because no challenge was made to the warrant except the constitutional challenge, the circuit court commissioner's search warrant was validly issued and the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

69 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Felix


NO.: 2010AP346-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 36; 339 Wis. 2d 670; 811 N.W.2d 775; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 29


November 9, 2011, Argued 
April 3, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2007CF659). COURT: CIRCUIT. COUNTY: MARATHON. JUDGE: CONRAD A. RICHARDS.
State v. Felix, 2011 WI App 58, 332 Wis. 2d 804, 798 N.W.2d 319, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 244 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court denied in part defendant's motions to suppress statements and physical evidence obtained after police arrested him at his home without an arrest warrant. Defendant pled guilty to second degree intentional homicide. The Court of Appeals, Wisconsin, reversed in part, and the State sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Adopting the U.S. Supreme Court's Harris exception to the exclusionary rule, the Wisconsin Supreme Court held that under Wis. Const. art. I, § 11, where police had probable cause to arrest before an unlawful entry and warrantless arrest from a defendant's home, this violation of Payton did not require the suppression of evidence obtained from a defendant outside of the home, such as statements obtained after the defendant was given and waived his Miranda rights. In the current case, the court found that police had probable cause to arrest defendant and assumed without deciding that defendant's warrantless arrest from his home was in violation of Payton. The court concluded that, pursuant to the Harris rule, the following evidence that police obtained outside of defendant's home was admissible: defendant's signed statement, made after defendant was given and waived his Miranda rights, a buccal swab obtained at the police station, and defendant's clothing seized at the jail, as well as any derivative evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and affirmed the circuit court's judgment of conviction.
