Heritage Farms, Inc. v. Markel Ins. Co.


No. 2010AP355


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 26; 339 Wis. 2d 125; 810 N.W.2d 465; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 21


November 1, 2011, Argued 
March 16, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Waushara. JUDGE: John V. Finn.
Heritage Farms, Inc. v. Markel Ins. Co., 2011 WI App 12, 331 Wis. 2d 64, 793 N.W.2d 896, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 980 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded to the circuit court with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, landowners, sought review of the decision of the court of appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the circuit court's order granting in part and denying in part the landowners' motion for payment of double damages and reasonable costs for legal representation under Wis. Stat. § 26.21(1) (2003-04) and for 12 percent interest in an action against defendants, individual, campground, and insurers, stemming from a fire.


OVERVIEW: The landowners' properties were damaged as a result of a forest fire and the appeal was a review of the appellate court's decision affirming an order by the circuit court that granted in part, and denied in part, the landowners' motion for payment of double damages and reasonable costs for legal representation under Wis. Stat. § 26.21(1) (2003-04) and for 12 percent interest thereon. The supreme court reversed, concluding that if it was determined that the owner's property was injured or destroyed by a forest fire that occurred through willfulness, malice, or negligence, then the property owner was entitled to double damages as a matter of course. Because the jury determined that the property was damaged by a forest fire caused by the individual's negligence, the property owners were entitled to double damages. Further, under Wis. Stat. § 814.04(4) (2003-04), the property owners were entitled to 12 percent interest on its double damages award from the date of the jury's verdict. The property owners were entitled to 12 percent interest on their award of attorney fees and costs only from the date of that award, not from the date of the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's decision was reversed and the case was remanded to the circuit court with instructions to enter judgment in accordance with the supreme court's opinion.

State v. Dinkins


No. 2009AP1643-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 24; 339 Wis. 2d 78; 810 N.W.2d 787; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 20


September 6, 2011, Argued 
March 13, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2008CF233). COURT: CIRCUIT. COUNTY: DODGE. JUDGE: ANDREW P. BISSONNETTE.
State v. Dinkins, 2010 WI App 163, 330 Wis. 2d 591, 794 N.W.2d 236, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 944 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State seeks review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed a finding that defendant was guilty of knowingly failing to comply with the sex offender registration statute, Wis. Stat. § 301.45(6) (2009-10).


OVERVIEW: The State sought review of the appellate court decision reversing defnedant's conviction for knowingly failing to comply with the sex offender registration statute. A registrant could not be convicted of violating Wis. Stat. § 301.45(6) for failing to report the address at which he would be residing when he was unable to provide that information. A registrant was unable to provide the required information when that information did not exist, despite the registrant's reasonable attempt to provide it. The supreme court agreed with the State that homeless registrants were not exempt from registration requirements and that homelessness was not a defense to failing to comply with the registration requirements. However, the supreme court disagreed that defendant was capable of complying with the statute by listing a park bench or other on-the-street location. The legislature set forth an alternative procedure for monitoring the whereabouts of registrants who were unable to provide an address without imposing criminal liability. Defendant attempted to comply with the statute, he was unable to find housing on his own, and the DOC would have to find housing for him.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed.

 

72 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Zwiefelhofer v. Town of Cooks Valley


No. 2010AP2398


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2012 WI 7; 338 Wis. 2d 488; 809 N.W.2d 362; 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 5


December 2, 2011, Argued 
February 8, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Chippewa County, James M. Isaacson, Judge. (L.C. No. 2009CV738).
Zwiefelhofer v. Town of Cooks Valley, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 525 (Wis. Ct. App., June 28, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chippewa County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) granted plaintiff town residents' summary judgment motion that they filed after they had filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant town seeking a declaration that the town's Nonmetallic Mining Ordinance was invalid. The town appealed and the appellate court certified the appeal to the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The town residents filed a complaint for declaratory judgment that alleged that each of them owned land in the town, had engaged in nonmetallic mining in the past, and may wish to do so on their land in the future. They contended that the Nonmetallic Mining Ordinance (Ordinance) was a zoning ordinance that was invalid because it did not have county board approval. If the Ordinance was not a zoning ordinance, county board approval was not required. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the town residents. The town's appeal presented one issue: "Is the town's Nonmetallic Mining Ordinance a zoning ordinance?" The state supreme court found that it was not a zoning ordinance. It scrutinized the Ordinance in light of the characteristics and purposes of traditional zoning ordinances, and concluded that, despite having some similarities to traditional zoning ordinances, the Ordinance was not to be classified as a zoning ordinance. It held that the Ordinance was a non-zoning ordinance adopted under the town's police power. Accordingly, it found that the ordinance did not need county board approval, and that the trial court's judgment could not stand.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

73 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. West (In re West)


No. 2009AP1579


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 83; 336 Wis. 2d 578; 800 N.W.2d 929; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 372


May 3, 2011, Argued 
July 26, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 1997CI970001). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: M. Joseph Donald.
State v. West (In re West), 2010 WI App 135, 329 Wis. 2d 710, 790 N.W.2d 543, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 634 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an individual committed as a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980, appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed a circuit court order denying his petition for supervised release.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was found to be a sexually violent person and placed under the custody of the Department of Health and Family Services (DHFS) for control, care, and treatment. He petitioned for release, but his petition was denied. On review, the court rejected petitioner's contention that the State bore the burden of proof to establish that his continued confinement was appropriate and held that Wis. Stat. § 980.08(4)(cg) (2005) unambiguously places the burden of proof with the committed individual. While the statute did not set forth the burden of proof required, the court held that, because the concerns for the public safety that justified restricting petitioner's liberty in the initial commitment were perhaps even more strongly implicated in the decision to release him back into the community because the initial determination involved a finding that the individual is likely to reoffend, in the absence of a statutory directive to the contrary, it was appropriate to require petitioner to bear the burden of proof by clear and convincing evidence that he was entitled to supervised release.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

 

74 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Dawson v. Town of Jackson


No. 2009AP120


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 77; 336 Wis. 2d 318; 801 N.W.2d 316; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 366



July 19, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
L.C. No. 2008CV682.
Dawson v. Town of Jackson, 2010 WI App 24, 323 Wis. 2d 477, 780 N.W.2d 222, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 7 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed the trial court's summary judgment ruling in favor of respondent property owners after they filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a determination that the joint action of the town boards of defendant two towns resulted in discontinuance of a road. The state supreme court granted the one town's petition for review.


OVERVIEW: The property owners sought a declaratory judgment under Wis. Stat. § 806.04 (2008) that the joint action of the two town boards resulted in discontinuance of a road surrounded by land that they owned. The trial court granted summary judgment to the property owners upon concluding that under Wis. Stat. § 82.21(2) (2008), "acting together" required that all votes at the joint meeting be counted in the aggregate, resulting in discontinuance. On appeal, the appellate court affirmed. On the one town's request for further review, the state supreme court found that "acting together" in the context of Wis. Stat. § 82.21(2) (2008) did not require an aggregate counting of votes and that statute did not mandate the creation of a new, combined board. Rather, it found that approval of both town boards, after they came together to resolve a joint application, was necessary to approve that application. It also found that since Wis. Stat. § 82.15 (2008) contemplated certiorari review under Wis. Stat. § 68.13 (2008) as the prescribed method for review of "a highway order, or a refusal to issue such an order," the trial court should have denied the property owners' declaratory judgment request.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment.

Northern Air Servs. v. Link


No. 2008AP2897


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 75; 336 Wis. 2d 1; 804 N.W.2d 458; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 363


October 6, 2010, Argued 
July 14, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Decision reached on appeal by Northern Air Servs. v. Link, 2012 Wisc. App. LEXIS 32 (Wis. Ct. App., Jan. 18, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2005CV127). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Washburn. JUDGE: Eugene D. Harrington.
N. Air Servs., Inc. v. Link, 2010 WI App 1, 322 Wis. 2d 735, 778 N.W.2d 172, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 882 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Court of Appeals found that (1) considering plaintiff father's postverdict motion to lower punitive damages was error; (2) defendant first son waived an appeal of the denial of his statutory oppression claim; and (3) he waived an appeal of the limit as to damages he could present on breach of fiduciary duty claims against the father and plaintiff second son. The state supreme court granted the father and first son's review requests.


OVERVIEW: A family owned companies. The first son's employment ended after conflicts arose. The father and second son sued seeking specific performance of an agreement requiring the first son to surrender his shares in plaintiff company. The first son counterclaimed alleging that they had "squeezed" him out of it. A jury found, inter alia, that they had breached fiduciary duties owed to him. The jury ordered the father to pay, inter alia, punitive damages to him. The trial court granted specific performance, and found that the first son had not shown Wis. Stat. § 180.1430(2)(b) (2006) oppression. It then allowed the father to file a post-verdict motion a day late. The appellate court found the trial court should not have considered the tardy postverdict motion, the first son waived an appeal as to the statutory oppression claim, and he waived a claim about limiting the evidence he could present. The state supreme court found the postverdict motion was untimely under Wis. Stat. § 805.16 (2006), the first son, no longer a shareholder, lacked standing as to the oppression claim, and the limit on evidence was error since he was trying to show he was owed "fair market value" for his shares.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the finding of error in the trial court considering the father's postverdict motion to reduce punitive damages and the rejection of the first son's statutory oppression claim. It reversed the finding that the first son waived his right to appeal a limit on evidence he could present as to damages on his breach of fiduciary duty claims against the father and second son, and remanded the case to the appellate court.

State v. Rhodes


No. 2009AP25-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 73; 336 Wis. 2d 64; 799 N.W.2d 850; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 362



July 14, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Rhodes, 2012 WI App 1, 338 Wis. 2d 210, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 882 (Nov. 22, 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied Rhodes v. Meisner, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 81997 (E.D. Wis., May 30, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2006CF1848). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Patricia D. McMahon.
State v. Rhodes, 2010 WI App 120, 329 Wis. 2d 268, 789 N.W.2d 753, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 507 (July 7, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree intentional homicide and first-degree recklessly endangering safety, both as party to a crime. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals reversed. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his right to confrontation under U.S. Const. amend. VI was violated because he should have been allowed to cross-examine his sister to rebut the State's theory of motive--namely, that defendant and the co-defendant gunned down the victim in an attempt to avenge the beating his sister had incurred at the victim's alleged direction. The supreme court disagreed. The case already involved two defendants, only one of whom testified. Over the course of the four-day trial, testimony was taken from sixteen witnesses, including the surviving victim of the crime. The jury was already presented with the difficult task of taking the often-conflicting testimony it heard and weighing it on two charges against two separate defendants. The trial court was concerned that the jury would be misled into an improper focus on questions about motive and the alleged history of abuse between the victim and the sister. Both were legitimate concerns, and therefore, defendant's right to cross-examination was not violated when the trial court limited his cross-examination of his sister.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the court of appeals for further proceedings.

State v. Gonzalez

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed a circuit court judgment convicting him of exposing a child to harmful materials under Wis. Stat. § 948.11(2)(a) (2005-06) and that affirmed a circuit court order denying his petition for post-conviction relief, arguing that the jury instructions were erroneous.

Affeldt v. Green Lake County


No. 2009AP2315


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 56; 335 Wis. 2d 104; 803 N.W.2d 56; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 345



July 6, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2008CV92). COURT: CIRCUIT COURT. COUNTY: GREEN LAKE. JUDGE: WILLIAM M. MCMONIGAL.
Affeldt v. Green Lake County, 2010 WI App 120, 329 Wis. 2d 271, 789 N.W.2d 755, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 588 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed the trial court's summary judgment grant in favor of defendant county after plaintiff property owners objected to the county's removal of trees and fences along their farm property on a county highway. They had filed a declaratory judgment action claiming that the trees and fences were not within the county's right-of-way. The state supreme court granted the property owners' request for review.


OVERVIEW: The county undertook a county highway reconstruction and maintenance project. To complete the project, it determined that it would need to remove trees and fences along the farm property of the property owners on the county highway. It figured it could do so because those items were within its right-of-way. The property owners filed a declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration that the county was incorrect. The trial court granted the county's summary judgment motion. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court found that the property owners introduced sufficient evidence to rebut the presumption under Wis. Stat. § 82.31 (2008) that the county highway was 66 feet, or four rods, wide. It cited a survey map that the property owners' licensed land surveyor provided, as well as affidavits from each of the property owners, that indicated the county had never maintained the trees or fence line along the county highway in the several decades that they had existed in the same location. That, the state supreme court found, was sufficient to find that a genuine issue of material fact existed about the width of the highway and right to remove the trees and fences.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Buchanan


No. 2009AP2934-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 49; 334 Wis. 2d 379; 799 N.W.2d 775; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 339


April 19, 2011, Argued 
June 29, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2009CF13). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Trempealeau. JUDGE: John A. Damon.
State v. Buchanan, 2010 WI App 135, 329 Wis. 2d 712, 790 N.W.2d 543, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 648 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed his conviction of possessing marijuana with the intent to deliver under Wis. Stat. § 961.41(1m)(h)(3) (2007-08), arguing that the trial court erred in denying his suppression motion because the evidence at issue was seized in violation of the federal and state constitutional provisions barring unreasonable searches and seizures.


OVERVIEW: A police officer effected a traffic stop. As he approached the vehicle, he observed defendant make furtive movements that indicated that he might be hiding something beneath the driver's seat. When the officer spoke to defendant, he noticed that defendant's hands were shaking as if he were very nervous. The officer called for backup; when backup arrived, he frisked defendant and searched the area inside the car within his reach and discovered drugs. On review, the court held that under the totality of the circumstances, the officer's observation of defendant's furtive movements and visible nervousness, a record of arrests for violent crimes, and a drug delivery arrest that had occurred nearby a short time before the stop constituted specific and articulable facts that, taken together with the rational inferences from those facts, created reasonable suspicion and justified a protective search for the officer's safety.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of possessing marijuana with intent to deliver was affirmed.

State ex rel. Ozanne v. Fitzgerald


No. 2011AP613-LV & 2011AP765-W


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 43; 334 Wis. 2d 70; 798 N.W.2d 436; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 332


June 6, 2011, Argued 
June 14, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Ozanne v. Fitzgerald, 2012 Wisc. LEXIS 614 (Wis., Jan. 20, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:
(L.C. No. 2011CV1244).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was a petition for leave to appeal a non-final order and accompanying motion for temporary relief. The petition and accompanying motion arose out of a case originating in the Dane County Circuit Court, Wisconsin, in which plaintiff district attorney alleged violations of Wisconsin's Open Meetings Law, Wis. Stat. § 19.81 et seq., in connection with the enactment of a budget repair bill.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the circuit court usurped the legislative power which the Wisconsin Constitution granted exclusively to the legislature. The circuit court exceeded its jurisdiction, invaded the legislature's constitutional powers under Wis. Const. art. IV, §§ 1 and 17, and erred in enjoining the publication and further implementation of the budget repair bill. The legislature did not violate the Wisconsin Constitution by the process it used to enact the bill. The doors of the senate and assembly were kept open to the press and members of the public during the enactment of the bill. The doors of the senate parlor, where the joint committee on conference met, were open to the press and members of the public. Regarding the argument that the bill was invalid because the legislature did not follow certain notice provisions of the Open Meetings Law for the meeting of the joint committee on conference, the court noted the legislature relied on its interpretation of its own rules of proceeding. The court declined to review the validity of the procedure used to give notice of the joint committee on conference.


OUTCOME: All orders and judgments of the circuit court in this case were vacated and declared to be void ab initio.

State v. Ninham


No. 2008AP1139


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 33; 333 Wis. 2d 335; 797 N.W.2d 451; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 324


January 5, 2011, Argued 
May 20, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ninham v. Wis., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 4920 (U.S., June 29, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 1999CF523). Court: Circuit. County: Brown. Judge: John D. McKay.
State v. Ninham, 2009 WI App 64, 316 Wis. 2d 776, 767 N.W.2d 326, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 143 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant, who was 14 years old at the time of the offense, of first-degree intentional homicide and physical abuse of a 13-year-old victim as a party, under Wis. Stat. §§ 940.01(1), 948.03(2)(b), 939.05 (1997-98). The circuit court denied his post-conviction motion for relief from a sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The Court of Appeals, Wisconsin, affirmed, and defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The Wisconsin Supreme Court held that sentencing a 14-year-old defendant to life imprisonment without parole was not categorically cruel and unusual under the Eighth Amendment or Wis. Const. art. I, § 6. The court found no national consensus against sentencing a 14-year-old to life imprisonment without parole when the crime was intentional homicide and also concluded, in the exercise of it own independent judgment, that the punishment is not categorically unconstitutional. The court also rejected defendant's alternative arguments. First, the sentence was not excessive under the circumstances. The manner in which defendant took the victim's life was horrific and senseless, and defendant refused to take responsibility. That he was just 14 years old and suffered an indisputably difficult childhood did not automatically make his punishment disproportionate. Second, defendant did not demonstrate that new scientific research regarding adolescent brain development constituted a new factor that frustrated the purpose of the sentence. Finally, defendant did not demonstrate that the circuit court relied on the religious beliefs of the victim's family when imposing the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Court of Appeals.

Tammy W-G. v. Jacob T. (In re Gwenevere T.)


No. 2009AP2973


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 30; 333 Wis. 2d 273; 797 N.W.2d 854; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 161



May 17, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Grant County, Michael Kirchman, Judge. (L.C. No. 09-TP-6). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Grant. JUDGE: Michael Kirchman.
Tammy W-G. v. Jacob T. (In re Gwenevere T.), 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 439 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 22, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Grant County, Wisconsin, that terminated his parental rights. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals certified the appeal for higher review in order to resolve the ambiguities and uncertainties regarding the use of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6) (2007-08) as a ground to terminate parental rights.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that, when applying Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6) in proceedings for the termination of parental rights, the fact-finder should consider the involvement of the parent over the entirety of the child's life, including the time when the child was in-utero. Although a parent's lack of opportunity to establish a substantial relationship was not a defense to the failure to assume parental responsibility, the reasons for a parent's lack of involvement could still be considered in the totality-of-the-circumstances analysis. The fact-finder could also consider whether the parent, while caring for the child, exposed the child to a hazardous living environment. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's finding that the father failed to assume responsibility for his daughter because, in the four years of her life leading up to the termination proceeding, the father had actual custody for only the child's first four months of life. He never had legal custody of her, and after four months, he provided no financial or material support. In addition, the father moved to Illinois and had little to no contact with his daughter since she was approximately five months old.


OUTCOME: The order terminating the father's parental rights was affirmed.

State v. Burris


No. 2009AP956-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 32; 333 Wis. 2d 87; 797 N.W.2d 430; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 162



May 17, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Burris, 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 868 (Wis. Ct. App., Nov. 22, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.
State v. Burris, 2010 WI App 33, 323 Wis. 2d 823, 781 N.W.2d 551, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 59 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that reversed a judgment convicting defendant of first-degree reckless injury while armed contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.23(1)(a) and § 939.63 (2007-08) and being a felon in possession of a firearm contrary to Wis. Stat. § 941.29(2)(a) (2007-08) and that reversed the denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief and awarded him a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the mother of his two children became involved in an argument that escalated into the shooting of the mother's brother, leaving him paralyzed. At trial, the central focus was whether defendant acted with utter disregard for human life, an element of Wis. Stat. § 940.23(1)(a). The court of appeals reversed defendant's conviction, concluding that the trial court's supplemental jury instruction on utter disregard was erroneous. On review, the court rejected the State's argument that defendant's after-the-fact mitigating conduct did not have the same evidentiary weight as his actions before and during the crime and held that, in an utter disregard analysis, defendant's conduct was not, as a matter of law, assigned more or less weight whether the conduct occurred before, during, or after the crime. When evaluating whether defendant acted with utter disregard for human life, the fact-finder was to consider any relevant evidence in regard to the totality of the circumstances. There was no bright-line rule regarding the evidentiary weight of a particular category of defendant's conduct depending on when that conduct occurred relative to the crime.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was reversed, and the case was remanded to that court to decide the other claims raised by defendant.

State v. Beauchamp


No. 2009AP806-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 27; 333 Wis. 2d 1; 796 N.W.2d 780; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 159


January 4, 2011, Argued 
May 3, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Beauchamp v. Wis., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8824 (U.S., Dec. 5, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: Jeffrey A. Wagner. L.C. No. 06-CF-3184.
State v. Beauchamp, 2010 WI App 42, 324 Wis. 2d 162, 781 N.W.2d 254, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 89 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree intentional homicide while using a dangerous weapon. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the statements made by the dying victim to a paramedic and an officer were improperly admitted and violated defendant's confrontation rights under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Wis. Const. art. I, § 7. The supreme court disagreed. Defendant conceded that the dying declaration exception was an established hearsay exception at common law. Allowing that hearsay exception comported with the protections of the Confrontation Clause. While the United States Supreme Court had yet to give its explicit blessing to the dying declaration exception, it had given no reason to abandon a principle that was so deeply rooted in the common law. The fairest way to resolve the tension between the State's interest in presenting a dying declaration and a defendant's concerns about unreliability was not to prohibit such evidence, but to continue to freely permit the aggressive impeachment of a dying declaration on any grounds that might be relevant. In other words, if there was evidence the declarant had a motive to accuse falsely, introduce it. If there was evidence that the declarant was cognitively impaired and incapable of perceiving events accurately, introduce it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Forbush


No. 2008AP3007-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 25; 332 Wis. 2d 620; 796 N.W.2d 741; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 157


September 14, 2010, Argued 
April 29, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit Court. COUNTY: Sheboygan. Judge: Terence T. Bourke. L.C. No. 2008CF292.
State v. Forbush, 2010 WI App 11, 323 Wis. 2d 258, 779 N.W.2d 476, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1011 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded to the circuit court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that reversed the trial court's order granting defendant's motion to suppress statements that he made during a police interrogation.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the U.S. Supreme Court's decision in Montejo v. Louisiana, 129 S. Ct. 2079 (2009), required the court to overrule Wisconsin precedent that established the parameters of a charged defendant's right to counsel in Wisconsin when the defendant, who had affirmatively invoked his constitutional right to counsel by retaining and receiving the services of counsel on pending charges, was subjected to questioning by law enforcement. Because defendant's right to counsel had attached and was affirmatively invoked before questioning was initiated and because the trial court's finding that the investigator knew that defendant had secured legal counsel for the pending charge was not clearly erroneous, defendant was not required to re-invoke his right to counsel when the investigator initiated interrogation, and his statements had to be suppressed.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court.

Metro. Assocs. v. City of Milwaukee


No. 2009AP524


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 20; 332 Wis. 2d 85; 796 N.W.2d 717; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 154


October 7, 2010, Argued 
March 25, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2008CV9866). COURT: Circuit COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Jean W. DiMotto.
Metro. Assocs. v. City of Milwaukee, 2009 WI App 157, 321 Wis. 2d 632, 774 N.W.2d 821, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 705 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Court of Appeals reversed the trial court's summary judgment grant to respondent taxpayer after the taxpayer filed a complaint against appellant city on its own behalf and on behalf of others similarly situated to challenge the procedures taxpayers had to follow to dispute municipal property tax assessments. The state supreme court then granted the taxpayer's request to allow an appeal challenging the appellate court's ruling.


OVERVIEW: The Legislature passed 2007 Wis. Sess. Laws 86, which allowed municipalities to pass an ordinance opting out of de novo review as a method of challenging property tax assessments. Taxpayers in those "opt out" municipalities were restricted to a new form of trial court review. That review was broader in scope than traditional certiorari review but narrower in scope than de novo review. The taxpayer, who owned property in the city, filed a lawsuit to challenge that law. The trial court found that the law unconstitutionally denied taxpayers residing in opt out municipalities equal protection of the laws by depriving those taxpayers of access to de novo review without a rational basis for doing so. The appellate court reversed. The state supreme court found that the process for reviewing property tax assessments dictated by 2007 Wis. Sess. Laws 86 made treatment for those taxpayers subject to it significantly different for all other taxpayers without a rational basis for doing so and, accordingly, that law violated the equal protection provisions of Wis. Stat. art. I, § 1 and the Fourteenth Amendment. The state supreme court also found that the offending provisions were severable.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment that had reversed the trial court's summary judgment grant to the taxpayer.

Ottman v. Town of Primrose


No. 2008AP3182


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2011 WI 18; 332 Wis. 2d 3; 796 N.W.2d 411; 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 152



March 22, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
(L.C. No. 2005CV1158).
Ottman v. Town of Primrose, 2010 WI App 46, 324 Wis. 2d 306, 784 N.W.2d 182, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 136 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent town board denied a permit application filed by appellants, petitioners. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed a circuit court order dismissing the petition for certiorari review of the board's decision. The petitioners sought review.


OVERVIEW: The board denied the petitioner's application for a permit to build a residential driveway. In the instant appeal, the petitioners were not challenging the validity of the ordinance, but simply asserted that Wis. Stat. ch. 68 (2009-2010) review should be augmented by the standards for certiorari review set forth in Wis. Stat. § 62.23 (2009-2010). The reviewing court held that the petitioners had not demonstrated how review would differ if the reviewing court proceeded under the standards set forth in Wis. Stat. § 62.23(7)(e)10. The petitioners failed to provide a persuasive rationale for upsetting the longstanding jurisprudence and the reviewing court declined to alter the established scope of statutory certiorari. Also, the board's interpretation of the farm income requirement was entitled to a presumption of correctness, and the reviewing court would accord it deference. The petitioners had not met their burden of showing that the board's interpretation was unreasonable. The board made a finding of fact that the farm income requirement was not met, and the petitioners had failed to demonstrate that no reasonable view of the evidence supported that finding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

89 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Wisc. Judicial Comm'n v. Zodrow (In re Judicial Disciplinary Proceedings)


No. 2009AP2904-J


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 107; 329 Wis. 2d 53; 787 N.W.2d 815; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 185



August 26, 2010, Filed


DISPOSITION: Reprimand imposed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant Wisconsin Judicial Commission (Commission) filed a complaint against respondent municipal judge alleging that he engaged in misconduct by failing to dispose of judicial matters promptly, efficiently, and fairly and by willfully or persistently failing to perform official duties. The panel recommended that the judge be reprimanded.


OVERVIEW: The judge believed he would have been encouraged to process cases in a more timely manner if there had been additional clerk support so he would not have been required to spend time performing tasks that he believed to be more properly the work of a clerk. The Commission alleged that, by allowing a backlog to accumulate, the judge violated Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 60.04(1)(h). The panel concluded that the judge's failure to decide cases in a timely fashion constituted judicial misconduct under Wis. Stat. § 757.81(4)(a) (2007-08). The panel found that the judge also violated Wis. Stat. § 757.81(4)(b) (2007-08) by refusing to adjudicate virtually all parking ticket stipulation cases for nearly a year. The supreme court agreed with the panel that a reprimand was the appropriate discipline for the judge's misconduct. There was no conceivable reason that might justify a backlog of 3,500 cases, some of which were more than seven years old. The likelihood of similar conduct by the judge was minimal.


OUTCOME: The judge was reprimanded for judicial misconduct.

State v. Henley


No. 2008AP697-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 97; 328 Wis. 2d 544; 787 N.W.2d 350; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 175


October 20, 2009, Oral Argument 
July 21, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Henley, 2011 WI 67, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 353 (2011)
Later proceeding at State v. Henley, 2011 WI 68, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 357 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County, Jacqueline R. Erwin, Judge. (L.C. No. 1998CF486).
State v. Henley, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 412 (Wis. Ct. App., Jan. 8, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County, Wisconsin, that granted defendant's motion for a new trial eight years after he was convicted of second-degree sexual assault. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals certified five questions regarding the authority of Wisconsin courts to order a new trial in the interests of justice.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of sexual assault, his conviction had been affirmed on appeal, and he exhausted his postconviction remedies in state and federal court, the conviction of one of his co-defendant was vacated. Thereafter, defendant sought a new trial under Wis. Stat. §§ 805.15 and 806.07, and the circuit court granted the requested relief, even though it had previously rejected defendant's identical argument. On review, the court held that neither Wis. Stat. § 805.15(1) nor Wis. Stat. § 806.07(1)(g) or (h) was an available procedural mechanism for a convicted criminal defendant to challenge his or her conviction or sentence, and Wisconsin circuit courts lacked the inherent authority to order a new trial in the interest of justice when a case was not before the court under a proper procedural mechanism. While the circuit court did have inherent powers, a broad, inherent power to order a new trial in the interest of justice at any time, unbound by concerns for finality and proper procedural mechanisms, was not one of them.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was reversed, and the case was remanded for entry of an order denying defendant's motion.

State v. McGuire


No. 2007AP2711-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 91; 328 Wis. 2d 289; 786 N.W.2d 227; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 168


January 5, 2010, Argued 
July 20, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McGuire v. Wisconsin, 178 L. Ed. 2d 558, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 9715 (U.S., Dec. 13, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2005CF80). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Walworth. JUDGE: James L. Carlson.
Wis. v. McGuire, 2009 WI App 95, 320 Wis. 2d 482, 769 N.W.2d 877, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 378 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed the denial of his petition for postconviction relief following his conviction of indecent behavior with a child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 944.11(2) (1965-66), arguing that the tolling provision of Wis. Stat. § 939.74(3) (2007-08) was unconstitutional and that the charges were barred by due process where 36 years passed between the offenses and the charges.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a Jesuit priest who taught at a school and molested two young teenaged boys in the late 1960's. A criminal complaint was not filed until 2005, after the priest's victims met each other and learned of their similar abuse. On review, the court held that the fact that defendant had not been in hiding and did not flee justice did not render Wis. Stat. § 939.74(3) unconstitutional as applied to him. Further, the statute did not violate the Privileges and Immunities, Due Process, or Equal Protection provisions of the United States Constitution, and Wis. Stat. § 939.74(3) did not burden a fundamental right and was rationally related to the legitimate governmental interests of detecting crimes and apprehending criminals. In addition, that a significant amount of time had elapsed since the commission of the offenses and the filing of charges did not warrant postconviction relief because petitioned failed to show a violation of his due process rights. Because petitioner could not demonstrate an improper motive on the part of the State, he failed to allege a necessary prerequisite for dismissal based on pre-indictment delay.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

State v. Sveum

SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 92; 328 Wis. 2d 369; 787 N.W.2d 317; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 171


March 2, 2010, Argued

PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2003CF1783).
State v. Sveum, 2009 WI App 81, 319 Wis. 2d 498, 769 N.W.2d 53, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 343 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed a circuit court judgment convicting defendant of aggravated stalking and that denied defendant's post-conviction motion for a new trial, arguing that the circuit court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of stalking and harassing his former girlfriend. After he was released from prison, the victim reported to the police that she believed defendant was following her again. The police received circuit court authority to install a GPS device in defendant's vehicle and to monitor defendant's travels. Based upon information that the police obtained through tracking defendant, defendant was again charged with and convicted of stalking. Further, execution of the warrant was reasonable under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11, because there was no indication that law enforcement's intrusion went beyond what was necessary to install and remove the device.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

Wis. Med. Soc'y, Inc. v. Morgan


No. 2009AP728


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 94; 328 Wis. 2d 469; 787 N.W.2d 22; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 169



July 20, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Michael Nowakowski, Judge. (L.C. No. 2007CV4035).
Wis. Med. Soc'y, Inc. v. Morgan, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1027 (Wis. Ct. App., Dec. 10, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a suit alleging an unconstitutional taking, plaintiff health care providers appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, that dismissed their suit against defendant, the Wisconsin Secretary of State, on the ground that they lacked a property interest in the Injured Patients and Families Compensation Fund, the property at issue.


OVERVIEW: As part of the state budget, the Wisconsin Legislature authorized the transfer of $ 200 million from the Injured Patients and Families Compensation Fund (the Fund) to the Medical Assistance Trust Fund through 2007 Wis. Act 20, § 9225. To implement the Act, the Secretary of State transferred the funds. The health care providers challenged the transfer as an unconstitutional taking. On review of the order of dismissal, the court held that the health care providers had a constitutionally protected property interest in the Fund. Wis. Stat. § 655.27(6) (2007-08) defined the Fund as an irrevocable trust, and the structure and purpose of the Fund satisfied all of the elements necessary to establish a formal trust. Because the health care providers were specifically named as beneficiaries of the trust, they had equitable title to the assets of the Fund. Because the health care providers had protected property interests in the Fund, § 9225 of 2007 Wis. Act 20 was unconstitutional because it authorized an unconstitutional taking of private property without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was reversed, and the case was remanded to the circuit court.

State v. Artic


No. 2008AP880-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 83; 327 Wis. 2d 392; 768 N.W.2d 430; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 108


September 11, 2009, Oral Argument 
July 15, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Artic v. Wisconsin, 131 S. Ct. 671, 178 L. Ed. 2d 500, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 9126 (U.S., 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Artic, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 658 (Wis. Ct. App., Aug. 13, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: Timothy M. Witkowiak. (L.C. No. 2006CF685).
State v. Artic, 2009 WI App 12, 316 Wis. 2d 133, 762 N.W.2d 436, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 964 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed the denial of his motion seeking post-conviction relief, arguing that counsel was ineffective in failing to preserve the argument that the police obtained evidence in violation of the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that it was unnecessary to address whether defense counsel was deficient because petitioner was not prejudiced by any alleged deficiencies. The trial court would have properly denied petitioner's motion to suppress even if defense counsel had raised the argument that the police created their own exigent circumstances because petitioner's consent to permit the police to search was given freely and voluntarily and not merely in acquiescence to police authority. Petitioner's consent was voluntary despite the fact that a police officer had his gun drawn when petitioner answered the door because the officer holstered his gun before asking petitioner for consent to search and he did not demand entry or use a threat or physical force. Further, petitioner orally consented to a search and reaffirmed his giving of consent. The fact that he subsequently refused to sign a consent form did not vitiate his consent, render his oral consent involuntary, or render the search unlawful.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court was affirmed.

State v. Robinson


No. 2008AP266-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 80; 327 Wis. 2d 302; 786 N.W.2d 463; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 112


April 13, 2010, Oral Argument 
July 15, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: Joseph R. Wall. (L.C. No. 2006CF5998).
State v. Robinson, 2009 WI App 97, 320 Wis. 2d 689, 770 N.W.2d 721, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 467 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed a judgment of conviction entered upon a guilty plea, arguing that the circuit court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence because the warrantless entry into his apartment by police officers and their subsequent search violated his constitutional rights against unreasonable searches and seizures under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the police officers' "knock and talk" entry into defendant's apartment was lawful and reasonable because it was supported by probable cause and justified by exigent circumstances. The police officers' warrantless entry into the apartment was supported by probable cause because, once the officers corroborated each of the three preliminary details provided by their anonymous informant who told them that defendant was selling drugs from his apartment, it was reasonable for the officers to then believe, as the informant had alleged, that evidence of illegal drug activity would probably be found in defendant's apartment. Further, the police officers' warrantless entry into defendant's apartment was justified by exigent circumstances. The officers knocked and announced their presence and immediately heard footsteps running away from the door. Therefore, the officers reasonably believed that defendant would destroy evidence of his illegal drug activity, and exigent circumstances permitted them to enter to prevent the destruction of evidence. Once inside the apartment, the officers lawfully seized the evidence in plain view and arrested Robinson.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

State v. Pinkard


No. 2008AP1204-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 81; 327 Wis. 2d 346; 785 N.W.2d 592; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 167


January 7, 2010, Oral Argument 
July 15, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Pinkard v. Wis., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 750 (U.S., Jan. 18, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: M. Joseph Donald. (L.C. No. 2006CF4557).
State v. Pinkard, 2009 WI App 77, 319 Wis. 2d 234, 769 N.W.2d 573, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 286 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed a circuit court's amended judgment convicting him of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, arguing that the circuit court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence seized from his bedroom following the warrantless entry of the police into his home.


OVERVIEW: The police received an anonymous tip that two individuals at a home appeared to be sleeping next to drugs and drug paraphernalia and that the door to the residence was standing open. Police officers proceeded to the home and entered to ensure that the occupants were not the victims of any type of crime such as robbery and were uninjured. The officers awaking defendant and the female occupant, arrested defendant, and seized the drugs that were in plain view. On review, the court held that the officers' warrantless entry into the home to ensure the health and safety of the occupants was undertaken as a bona fide community caretaker function. The officer could reasonably have been concerned that defendant and his companion had overdosed on drugs. The open doors to defendant's house and bedroom, along with defendant's unresponsiveness to the officers' repeated efforts to rouse him and his companion by knocking on the door, also could indicate a drug overdose. Accordingly, the police officers had an objectively reasonable basis for deciding that entry was necessary to ensure the health and safety of the occupants, and the officers lawfully seized drugs that were in plain view.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court was affirmed.

State v. Dearborn


NO. 2007AP1894-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 84; 327 Wis. 2d 252; 786 N.W.2d 97; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 110


April 13, 2010, Oral Argument 
July 15, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Dearborn v. Wis., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 4858 (U.S., June 27, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Grant. Judge: George S. Curry. (L.C. No. 2006CM116).
State v. Dearborn, 2008 WI App 131, 313 Wis. 2d 767, 758 N.W.2d 463, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 570 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed a judgment convicting him of assaulting. obstructing, or resisting a conservation warden in violation of Wis. Stat. § 29.951 (2005-06) and of possession of tetrahydrocannabinols (THC) in violation of Wis. Stat. § 961.41(3g)(e) (2005-06), arguing that the circuit court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained from a search of his locked vehicle.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the circuit court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained from a search of the passenger compartment of his locked vehicle because the search that occurred after he was placed under arrest and secured in the back of a squad car. On review, the court held that the good faith exception precluded application of the exclusionary rule under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11, where the officers conducted a search in objectively reasonable reliance upon clear and settled Wisconsin precedent that was later deemed unconstitutional by the United States Supreme Court. Under the Supreme Court's ruling in Arizona v. Gant, the search at issue violated defendant's constitutional right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. However, because the search was lawful under Wisconsin law as it existed before Gant, the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule applied. The exclusionary rule was inappropriate when the police reasonably relied on clear and settled precedent.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

State v. Hess


No. 2008AP2231-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 82; 327 Wis. 2d 524; 785 N.W.2d 568; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 109


March 2, 2010, Oral Argument 
July 15, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Walworth. JUDGE: James L. Carlson. (L.C. No. 2007CF000110).
State v. Hess, 2009 WI App 105, 320 Wis. 2d 600, 770 N.W.2d 769, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 436 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that reversed defendant's conviction and remanded to the circuit court with instructions to retry defendant but to grant defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained through an invalid arrest warrant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of an alcohol-related offense. When he left a meeting with the agent assigned to complete his pre-sentence investigation (PSI), a civil warrant for his arrest was issued based upon his failure to appear in court. A deputy sheriff executed the warrant and found defendant intoxicated in violation of the conditions of his release. As a result, defendant was charged with bail jumping. Although the State conceded that the arrest warrant was invalid, it nevertheless argued that the good faith exception applied to permit evidence of defendant's intoxication into evidence. On review, the court held that the arrest warrant was ab initio, and the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule did not apply when a warrant was void. The warrant was void because the circuit court did not have statutory authority to issue a warrant for failure to meet with the PSI agent and because failure to cooperate with the PSI agent was not a crime. Further, walking out on a meeting with a PSI agent did not constitute failing to appear in court. In addition, the civil arrest warrant was void because the matter pending before the circuit court was criminal in nature, not civil.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

Soc'y Ins. v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n


No. 2008AP3135


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 68; 326 Wis. 2d 444; 786 N.W.2d 385; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 60



July 8, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County, Dale L. English, judge. L.C. No. 2008CV449. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Fond du Lac. JUDGE: Dale L. English.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Wisconsin Labor & Industry Review Commission, appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County, Wisconsin, that declared the retroactive application of Wis. Stat. § 102.17(4) and Wis. Stat. § 102.66(1) (2005-06) to be unconstitutional. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals certified the question for resolution.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the retroactive application of Wis. Stat. §§ 102.17(4) and 102.66(1) (2005-06) violated plaintiff worker's compensation insurer's due process rights under Wis. Const. art. I, § 1, and U.S. Const. amend. XIV because the insurer had a vested property right in the prior statute of limitations, which limited its liability to pay for an injured employee's benefits or treatment once 12 years from the day of the last payment of compensation had passed. Further, retroactive application impaired the insurer's contractual rights because it contracted to provide insurance in reliance upon the established liability limit and based its pricing and premiums on the law as it existed under Wis. Stat. §§ 102.17(4) and 102.66(1) (2003-04), including the 12-year statute of limitations applicable to traumatic injury claims. Retroactive application altered the contractual expectations of the insurer by renewing its liability on an injured employee's claim after its original liability expired on the date the statute of limitations ran; as such, the legislation impaired the obligation of contract in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and Wis. Const. art. I, § 12.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was affirmed.

State v. Jones


No. 2008AP2342-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 72; 326 Wis. 2d 380; 797 N.W.2d 378; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 64


April 12, 2010, Oral Argument 
July 8, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Elsa C. Lamelas. (L.C. No. 2005CF2432).
State v. Jones, 2009 WI App 141, 321 Wis. 2d 477, 774 N.W.2d 476, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 600 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed a circuit court's judgment of conviction and order denying defendant's post-conviction motion for a new trial, arguing that the circuit court erred in denying his request to substitute counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the circuit court erred in failing to appoint new counsel because, due to a profound hearing impairment, he was unable to communicate with his attorney. On review, the court held that the record amply supported the circuit court's conclusion that defendant and his trial counsel communicated effectively without a sign language interpreter, including letters from defense counsel to defendant, testimony that defendant did not dispute that counsel met with him and reviewed discovery with him, the circuit court's observation of defendant's communications with counsel, testimony that defendant read lips, and testimony of defendant's mother that she did not know sign language and never used it to communicate with her son. Even if defendant was dissatisfied with counsel and took offense at counsel's assessment of the strength of the State's case, it was clear from the record that the two communicated and that an adequate defense was presented. There was therefore no violation of defendant's right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Wis. Const. art. I, § 7, and the circuit court properly denied defendant's motion for a new trial on that basis.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

State v. Conger


No. 2008AP755-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 56; 325 Wis. 2d 664; 797 N.W.2d 341; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 50


December 1, 2009, Argued 
June 30, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from orders of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County, Peter L. Grimm, Judge. (L.C. No. 2007CF324).
State v. Conger, 2009 WI 98, 321 Wis. 2d 50, 775 N.W.2d 256, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 332 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Order denying motion to amend affirmed; order denying motion to recuse affirmed; order of the court of appeals designating the circuit court an intervenor-respondent remanded to the court of appeals for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant had been charged with various drug crimes and he and the prosecutor negotiated a plea agreement, which respondent judge of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County, Wisconsin, rejected. Appellant's motion for recusal was also rejected. Appellant petitioned for an interlocutory appeal and co-appellant state joined the petition. A Wisconsin court of appeals certified the appeal to the Supreme Court of Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: The plea agreement involved a felony charge that was to be amended to three misdemeanors, another charge to be dismissed, and a recommendation by the prosecutor for specific sentencing. Appellant and the state argued that deference to the prosecutor's recommendation was warranted because it was made after consideration of all of the relevant facts and constituted a reasonable exercise of the prosecutor's inherent power and discretion. The court held that a circuit court must review a plea agreement independently and could, in an appropriate exercise of discretion, reject any plea agreement that did not serve the public interest. The public interest was a consideration that was not capable of precise outlines and the factors that the circuit court could weigh when defining the public interest involved would vary from case to case. The court also concluded that the circuit court's rejection of a plea did not in and of itself become a personal interest in the outcome of the matter and Wis. Stat. § 757.19(2)(f) was not implicated here. However, because the record was undeveloped as to whether the judge had become a party to the case, the matter was remanded on this issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court denying the motion to amend the information pursuant to the plea agreement and the order denying appellant's initial motion seeking the judge's recusal. However, the court remanded the issue of whether the judge had become a party or amicus and whether recusal was now required.

Wis. Judicial Comm'n v. Gableman (In re Judicial Disciplinary Proceedings Against Gableman)


No. 2008AP2458-J


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 61; 325 Wis. 2d 579; 784 N.W.2d 605; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 51



June 30, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Supplemented by Wis. Judicial Comm'n v. Gableman (In re Judicial Disciplinary Proceedings Against Gableman), 2010 WI 62, 325 Wis. 2d 631, 784 N.W.2d 631, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 179 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant, the Wisconsin Judicial Commission, filed a complaint against respondent justice based upon a television advertisement run by his re-election campaign, alleging that the advertisement contained a misrepresentation of fact about his opponent. The justice moved for summary judgment, and the Judicial Conduct Panel designated to hear the matter recommended that the motion be granted and the complaint be dismissed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court found itself equally divided with respect to the panel's recommendation, with only three of the six justices finding that the advertisement constituted a misrepresentation. Because no majority agreed with the Panel's recommendation, the Judicial Commission's complaint survived summary judgment. Further, because no four justices voted either to accept or to reject the Judicial Conduct Panel's recommendations and no four justices agreed on the motion for summary judgment or any disposition of the Judicial Commission's complaint, no action could be taken on the Panel's recommendation. Because the Judicial Commission failed to obtain a majority of justices to reject the recommendation of the Panel, the Panel was relieved of any further responsibility in the matter, and the case was remanded to the Judicial Commission with directions to request a jury hearing. The justices who supported a finding that the advertisement violated the Judicial Code set forth an opinion advocating their position, which was not binding in that it lacked majority support, and the three justices reaching a contradictory conclusion issued a written opinion in a separate opinion.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the Judicial Commission with instructions to request a jury hearing with a jury of 12 persons on the question of whether the campaign advertisement violated the Wisconsin Judicial Code.

 

103 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Wis. Judicial Comm'n v. Gableman (In re Judicial Disciplinary Proceedings Against Gableman)


No. 2008AP2458-J


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 62; 325 Wis. 2d 631; 784 N.W.2d 631; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 179



June 30, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Wis. Judicial Comm'n v. Gableman (In re Judicial Disciplinary Proceedings Against Gableman), 2010 WI 61, 325 Wis. 2d 579, 784 N.W.2d 605, 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 51 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant, the Wisconsin Judicial Commission, filed a complaint against respondent justice based upon a television advertisement run by his re-election campaign, alleging that the advertisement contained a misrepresentation of fact about his opponent. The justice moved for summary judgment, and the Judicial Conduct Panel designated to hear the matter recommended that the motion be granted and the complaint be dismissed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court found itself equally divided with respect to the panel's recommendation, with only three of the six justices finding that the advertisement constituted a misrepresentation. Because no majority agreed with the Panel's recommendation, the Judicial Commission's complaint survived summary judgment. Further, because no four justices voted either to accept or to reject the Judicial Conduct Panel's recommendations and no four justices agreed on the motion for summary judgment or any disposition of the Judicial Commission's complaint, no action could be taken on the Panel's recommendation. Because the Judicial Commission failed to obtain a majority of justices to reject the recommendation of the Panel, the Panel was relieved of any further responsibility in the matter, and the case was remanded to the Judicial Commission with directions to request a jury hearing. The justices who did not support a finding that the advertisement violated the Judicial Code set forth an opinion advocating their position, which was not binding in that it lacked majority support, and the three justices reaching a contradictory conclusion issued a written opinion at 2010 Wisc. Lexis 51.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the Judicial Commission with instructions to request a jury hearing with a jury of 12 persons on the question of whether the campaign advertisement violated the Wisconsin Judicial Code.

In re Disciplinary Proceeding Against Boyd


No. 2009AP774-D


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 41; 324 Wis. 2d 688; 782 N.W.2d 718; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 37



May 27, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Office of Lawyer Regulation v. Boyd ( In re Boyd), 2006 WI 28, 289 Wis. 2d 351, 711 N.W.2d 268, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 210 (2006)


DISPOSITION: Attorney's license suspended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Office of Lawyer Regulation (OLR) filed a disciplinary complaint alleging that respondent attorney committed 11 separate acts of misconduct in four client matters. Pursuant to a stipulation the attorney entered a no contest plea. A referee recommended, among other things, suspension of the attorney's license to practice law for 12 months consecutive to disciplinary suspensions already imposed. The attorney did not appeal.


OVERVIEW: The attorney had been subject to discipline on several previous occasions and was suspended at the time of this proceeding. The four client matters at issue involved criminal proceedings in which the attorney did not timely file motions, did not inform her clients as to the status of their cases, did not follow the clients' directions, and failed to provide services that were necessary to preserve her clients' rights. The court agreed with the referee's recommendations and suspended the attorney's license to practice law in Wisconsin for 12 months consecutive to disciplinary suspensions already imposed, directed her to pay restitution to three of the clients, with interest until paid, as well as the costs of the proceeding, and to secure 20 credits of Wisconsin-approved continuing legal education ethics courses. Although the fourth client also argued that he should have received restitution, the court found that although the client might have had a civil action against the attorney, it appeared that the fee he paid did not meet the criteria the OLR used to assess whether restitution was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court accepted the referee's recommendations.

 

105 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carter


No. 2008AP1185--CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 40; 324 Wis. 2d 640; 782 N.W.2d 695; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 35


November 3, 2009, Argued 
May 25, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2005CF4726).
State v. Carter, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1028 (Wis. Ct. App., Mar. 12, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of one count of first-degree sexual assault of a child. The circuit court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals remanded the matter to the circuit court for further proceedings. The State petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the court of appeals improperly remanded the case to the circuit court for further proceedings on defendant's claim that his trial counsel was ineffective. The supreme court agreed. Defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim failed under the two-part inquiry of Strickland. First, his trial counsel's performance was not deficient. His counsel's strategic decision not to introduce evidence that the child victim was previously sexually assaulted was reasonable considering all the circumstances. Second, even assuming that his counsel's performance was deficient, the deficiency did not prejudice defendant's defense. Evidence that the child was previously sexually assaulted would have been inadmissible under Wisconsin's rape shield law, Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2), and the narrow exception. Counsel informed the circuit court that he had made the strategic decision not to present evidence that the child might have been previously sexually assaulted by a third party. He gave three reasons for his decision: (1) he thought the State would likely object; (2) he did not see it as relevant; and (3) he thought he would--if anything, build up sympathy for the child.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was reversed. The judgment of the circuit court denying defendant's post-conviction motion for a new trial was affirmed.

State v. Jensen


No. 2008AP552-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 38; 324 Wis. 2d 586; 782 N.W.2d 415; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 33


November 10, 2009, Argued 
May 20, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended May 24, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the court of appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: David T. Flanagan, III. (L.C. No. 2002CF2453).
State v. Jensen, 2009 WI App 26, 316 Wis. 2d 377, 762 N.W.2d 833, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 24 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following remand for a new trial, appellant filed a motion to transfer his case from the Dane County Circuit Court, Wisconsin, where the misconduct was alleged to have occurred and where his first jury trial had taken place, to Waukesha County Circuit Court, Wisconsin, where appellant resided, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 971.19(12) (2007-08). The denial of the motion was affirmed by the Wisconsin Court of Appeals. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of three counts of felony misconduct in public office as party to the crime, Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3), and one misdemeanor count of intentional misuse of public positions for private benefit as party to the crime, Wis. Stat. § 19.45(2). During the pendency of an appeal, Wis. Stat. § 971.19(12) (2007-08) was passed, which provided that defendants charged with certain violations of, and violations arising from or in relation to, the elections, ethics, and lobbying regulation laws were to be tried in the county where the defendant resided. The State contended that § 971.19(12) did not apply to the charges against appellant. The court disagreed and concluded that Wis. Stat. § 971.19(12) established Waukesha County Circuit Court as the proper venue for appellant's trial because the allegations against him came within two categories of actions described in § 971.19(12). First, the State alleged that appellant violated a law arising from or in relation to the official functions of the subject of the investigation. Second, the State alleged that appellant violated a law arising from or in relation to any matter that involved elections under chapters 5 to 12.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Wood


No. 2007AP2767-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 17; 323 Wis. 2d 321; 780 N.W.2d 63; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 16


November 3, 2009, Oral Argument 
March 19, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for La Crosse County, Michael J. Mulroy, Judge. (L.C. No. 1998CF59).
State v. Wood, 2008 WI 124, 314 Wis. 2d 284, 758 N.W.2d 928, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 1058 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a paranoid schizophrenic, was found not guilty of crimes by reason of mental disease or defect (NGI). A circuit court (Wisconsin) authorized a mental health facility to administer psychotropic medication to defendant without his consent pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 971.17(3)(c) (2005-06) and denied his motion for relief. The court of appeals (Wisconsin) certified two questions concerning due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found NGI of a brutal murder and subsequently found NGI of a sexual assault of another patient in an institutional setting. Except for a period of seven years, defendant had been institutionalized for 30 years. Wis. Stat. § 971.17(3)(c) authorized the involuntary medication of committed persons who were found NGI of a crime and who were found to be incompetent to refuse treatment or medication. In a case of first impression in Wisconsin, the court held that § 971.17(3)(c) and the administrative directive implementing it comported with the substantive and procedural due process provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 1, facially and as applied. First, due process did not require a finding of dangerousness to issue an order compelling involuntary medication of a person committed under Wis. Stat. ch. 971. Nevertheless, § 971.17(3)(c) and the directive effectively provided for such a finding. Second, due process required periodic review of the compelled involuntary medication order. Section 971.17(3)(c) and the directive satisfied that requirement as well. Finally, defendant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's orders compelling involuntary medication and denying defendant's motion for relief from the involuntary medication order.

State v. Smith


No. 2008AP1011-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 16; 323 Wis. 2d 377; 780 N.W.2d 90; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 18


September 15, 2009, Argued 
March 19, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smith v. Wisconsin, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 6488 (U.S., Oct. 4, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2005CF1266). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Brown. JUDGE: Richard J. Dietz.
State v. Smith, 2009 WI App 16, 316 Wis. 2d 165, 762 N.W.2d 856, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 996 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was charged with failure to comply with sex offender registration. The Brown County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) concluded that Wis. Stat. § 301.45 (2005-06), the sex offender registration statute, was constitutional as applied to appellant, who had been convicted of false imprisonment of a minor, Wis. Stat. § 940.30 (1999-2000), and denied his motion to dismiss the charge. The court of appeals affirmed and appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that Wis. Stat. § 301.45 was unconstitutional as applied to him because it required him to register as a sex offender even though his underlying conviction for false imprisonment of a minor was not of a sexual nature. Appellant acknowledged that § 301.45 served a legitimate state interest, but argued that § 301.45 was unconstitutional as applied to him because requiring him to register was irrational, arbitrary, and could not have been rationally related to any legitimate government interest. The court held that § 301.45 was constitutional as applied to appellant because § 301.45 was rationally related to a legitimate governmental interest and he failed to prove that the registration requirements as applied to him were unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt. The legislature chose to require registration by those, like appellant, who committed the crime of falsely imprisoning a minor, regardless of whether that crime was of a sexual nature. The court must afford deference to the words chosen by the legislature and could not conclude that there was no legitimate government interest in requiring registration of such offenders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.
