110 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carroll


No. 2007AP1378-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 8; 322 Wis. 2d 299; 778 N.W.2d 1; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 8


September 15, 2009, Oral Argument 
February 3, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 2008 WI App 161, 314 Wis. 2d 690, 762 N.W.2d 404. (Ct. App. 2008-Published). Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: Charles F. Kahn, Jr. (L.C. No. 2006CF6568).
State v. Carroll, 2008 WI App 161, 314 Wis. 2d 690, 762 N.W.2d 404, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 840 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of a firearm by a felon. The trial court suppressed evidence obtained from defendant's cell phone pursuant to a warrant. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals reversed the suppression order. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the court of appeals erred in reversing the suppression order. The supreme court disagreed. An officer who had observed defendant speeding confronted defendant outside of his vehicle and ordered him to drop an unknown object that he held in his hand, and upon retrieving that object, the officer recognized it as an open cell phone and observed on the display screen an image of defendant smoking what appeared to be a marijuana blunt. The officer was justified in seizing defendant's cell phone and in viewing the marijuana image, which was in plain view. However, the evidence that the officer gleaned from searching other images was tainted and could not form the basis for a search warrant. However, based on exigent circumstances, the officer was justified in answering the incoming call to defendant's phone during which the caller ordered illegal drugs. That evidence was an untainted independent source that formed a valid basis for the search warrant when combined with the officer's knowledge of drug traffickers and defendant's juvenile record, along with the plain view of the image of the marijuana blunt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

State v. Fischer


No. 2007AP1898-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2010 WI 6; 322 Wis. 2d 265; 778 N.W.2d 629; 2010 Wisc. LEXIS 5


October 13, 2009, Argued 
February 2, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Fischer v. Wisconsin, 130 S. Ct. 3480, 177 L. Ed. 2d 1058, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 5024 (U.S., 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus granted Fischer v. Ozaukee County Circuit Court, 741 F. Supp. 2d 944, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 108264 (E.D. Wis., Sept. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2005CM123). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Ozaukee. JUDGE: Thomas R. Wolfgram.
State v. Fischer, 2008 WI App 152, 314 Wis. 2d 324, 761 N.W.2d 7, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 717 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Ozaukee County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), appellant was found guilty of operating while intoxicated (OWI), Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) and (b) (2005-06). The Court of Appeals affirmed the circuit court's judgment and ruling that excluded an expert's report and opinion testimony based in part on the results of a preliminary breath test (PBT) appellant took just prior to arrest. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The expert's opinion was that appellant had a BAC below the legal limit at the time he was pulled over by police and that his BAC level only later rose above the limit as his body continued to absorb the alcohol. At issue was whether Wis. Stat. § 343.303 created an absolute bar on the admission of PBT results in OWI prosecutions, even when used as the basis for an expert's opinion offered under Wis. Stat. § 907.03, and, if so, whether such an application of the statute violated a defendant's constitutional right to present a defense. The court reached the same result under different analysis than in the courts below. The court held that in an OWI prosecution, even if the defendant established a constitutional right to present an expert opinion that was based in part on PBT results, the right to do so was outweighed by the State's compelling interest to exclude that evidence. Permitting the use of that evidence as the basis for an expert opinion would render meaningless the legislature's act forbidding such evidence in OWI prosecutions, an act that promoted efficient investigations of suspected drunk driving and furthered the State's compelling interest in public safety.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Coulee Catholic Sch. v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n


No. 2007AP496


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI 88; 320 Wis. 2d 275; 768 N.W.2d 868; 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 297; 106 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1514


March 3, 2009, Argued 
July 21, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2006CV193). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: La Crosse. JUDGE: Dale T. Pasell.
Coulee Catholic Sch. v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n, 2008 WI App 68, 312 Wis. 2d 331, 752 N.W.2d 342, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 430 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent teacher brought a claim alleging that she was terminated from her first-grade teaching position at a Catholic school on the basis of her age in violation of the Wisconsin Fair Employment Act (WFEA). Petitioner employer argued that the suit was barred by the First Amendment because respondent's position was "ministerial," but the trial court determined otherwise. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed. The employer sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that both the Free Exercise Clause of the First Amendment and the Freedom of Conscience Clauses in Wis. Const. art. I, § 18, preclude employment discrimination claims under the WFEA for employees whose positions are important and closely linked to the religious mission of a religious organization. In the case at bar, respondent's school was committed to a religious mission - the inculcation of the Catholic faith and worldview - and her teaching position was important and closely linked to that mission. Respondent led prayer with her students, incorporated religious examples, symbols, and stories into other subjects, and helped celebrate school-wide celebrations of religious holidays. Significantly, respondent was a catechist for four days per week; that is, she taught Catholic doctrine and practice to her students. Respondent was not simply a public school teacher with an added obligation to teach religion. She was an important instrument in a faith-based organization's efforts to pass on its faith to the next generation. Therefore, respondent's age discrimination claim under the WFEA unconstitutionally impinged upon her employer's right to religious freedom.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court to dismiss respondent's claim.

City of Milwaukee Post No. 2874 VFW v. Redevelopment Auth.


No. 2006AP2866


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI 84; 319 Wis. 2d 553; 768 N.W.2d 749; 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 294



July 17, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by City of Milwaukee Post No. 2874 v. Redevelopment Auth. of Milwaukee, 2010 WI 5, 322 Wis. 2d 130, 779 N.W.2d 181, 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 793 (2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by City of Milwaukee Post No. 2874 VFW of the U.S. v. Redevelopment Auth., 2010 U.S. LEXIS 5007 (U.S., June 21, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2005CV365). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Elsa Lamelas.
City of Milwaukee Post No. 2874 VFW v. Redevelopment Auth., 2008 WI App 24, 307 Wis. 2d 518, 746 N.W.2d 536, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 53 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant redevelopment authority sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the circuit court's judgment that the redevelopment authority was not obligated under Wis. Const. art. I, § 13 to pay any sum to plaintiff lessee as just compensation for the taking of the real property in which the lessee held a leasehold interest.


OVERVIEW: The lessee conveyed the real property in exchange for a long-term leasehold interest, with a nominal rent obligation, in a portion of a building that the buyer constructed. After the building and the surrounding neighborhood deteriorated, the redevelopment authority created a redevelopment district and issued a relocation order. The redevelopment authority presented evidence that the building would cost more to renovate than the improvements would be worth and that it would cost more to demolish than the vacant land would be worth. A jury accordingly found that the undivided interest in the property had no value at the time of the taking. The court held that the unit rule, under which a condemnor paid the value of an undivided interest in a property rather than paying the value of each partial interest, was the applicable method of determining just compensation and did not allow the lessee to obtain a recovery based on equitable principles of fairness. Departure from the unit rule could be made only in rare and exceptional circumstances, and the lessee's failure to protect the value of its leasehold interest by means of contract law was not such a circumstance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Milwaukee Journal Sentinel v. Wis. Dep't of Admin.


No. 2007AP1160


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI 79; 319 Wis. 2d 439; 768 N.W.2d 700; 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 288; 186 L.R.R.M. 3255; 37 Media L. Rep. 2061


April 15, 2009, Oral Argument 
July 15, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County, C. William Foust, Judge. (L.C. Nos. 2005CV3569 & 2005CV3923). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: William C. Foust.
Milwaukee Journal Sentinel v. Wis. Dep't of Admin., 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 461 (Wis. Ct. App., June 17, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and cause remanded to the circuit court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a dispute concerning whether a provision in the State's ratified collective bargaining agreement with intervenor Wisconsin State Employees Union (WSEU), which purported to prohibit the disclosure to the press of the names of WSEU-represented employees, modified the Public Records Law, Wis. Stat. § 19.31 et seq., a circuit court issued mandamus ordering disclosure of the employees' names. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals certified WSEU's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that courts had jurisdiction to review whether the legislature's ratification of a collective bargaining agreement under Wis. Stat. § 111.92(1)(a) (2005-06), without introducing a companion bill to specifically amend the Public Records Law, was sufficient to effect a change in that law because courts had jurisdiction to determine the meaning of statutes and of constitutional provisions. Ratification of the collective bargaining agreement was insufficient to amend the Public Records Law because Article 2/4/4, the provision of the agreement at issue, was not introduced in a bill or companion bills within the meaning of § 111.92(1)(a), as that meaning was driven by the requirements of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 17(2). Thus, the ratification of the agreement did not create an exception to the Public Records Law. Wis. Stat. § 111.93(3) (2005-06) did not support WSEU's assertion that Article 2/4/4 superseded the disclosure provision of the Public Records Law. The court affirmed the circuit court's application of the balancing test, which it appeared the circuit court applied to the WSEU members as a group because that was how the issue was argued to the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court and remanded the cause to that court.

Phelps v. Physicians Ins. Co. of Wis., Inc.


No. 2006AP2599


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI 74; 319 Wis. 2d 1; 768 N.W.2d 615; 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 284


March 5, 2009, Oral Argument 
July 10, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 1999CV7971). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: John A. Franke.
Phelps v. Physicians Ins. Co. of Wis., Inc., 2008 WI App 6, 307 Wis. 2d 184, 744 N.W.2d 880, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1058 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded to the circuit court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a doctor and his insurer (doctor), sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which found in favor of plaintiffs, a mother, father, and their surviving children, and affirmed the circuit court's decision reinstating the father's award for bystander negligent infliction of emotional distress. The appellate court also reversed the circuit court's ruling that the doctor was a borrowed employee.


OVERVIEW: After one of the parents' twins was unable to be resuscitated and died during birth, a subsequent malpractice action was instituted. The two questions presented for supreme court review were whether the doctor was a borrow employee of the hospital and whether the father was permitted to recover damages caused by the doctor's negligence on a theory of the negligent infliction of emotional distress to a bystander. The supreme court concluded that the doctor was a borrowed employee and accordingly, the doctor was an employee of a health care provider subject to Wis. Stat. ch. 655 and Wis. Stat. § 893.55(4) (1997-98). As a result, the father's claim for bystander negligent infliction of emotional distress was subject to those statutory provisions. Because the father's claim was one for bystander negligent infliction of emotional distress and Wis. Stat. ch. 655 did not permit such claims, his claim was not recognized by Wisconsin law and therefore, the appellate court's decision was reversed.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the appellate court's decision and remanded to the circuit court to issue an order dismissing the father's claim.

 

116 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Luckett v. Bodner


No. 2007AP308


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI 68; 318 Wis. 2d 423; 769 N.W.2d 504; 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 277


January 7, 2009, Argued 
July 7, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2003CV7355). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Christopher R. Foley.
Luckett v. Bodner, 2008 WI App 83, 312 Wis. 2d 480, 751 N.W.2d 902, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 307 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the patient's family and the estate administrator (family), sued appellants, physicians, hospitals, and insurers, alleging the doctors' negligence caused the patient's brain damage (and eventual death). The family's motion to withdraw admissions they made in response to requests made by the physicians, hospitals, and insurers was granted. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed. The physicians, hospitals, and insurers appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the physicians, hospitals, and insurers, contended it was error to allow the family to withdraw their admissions. The supreme court disagreed, concluding that withdrawal of the admissions would subserve the presentation of the merits because if, as the newly-discovered entries in the medical records arguably indicated, the patient was capable of and did experience pain and suffering for the extended period between the time she lapsed into a coma to the time of her death, it was appropriate for the jury to consider that fact and, if liability was established, award damages to compensate that loss. Further, the physicians, hospitals, and insurers would not be prejudiced by the withdrawal of the admissions in maintaining their defense on the merits, and their increased exposure was not a pertinent consideration on the prejudice prong of Wis. Stat. § 804.11(2) (2005-06). The family's admissions, if allowed to stand, would have effectively eliminated a determination on the merits of the issues of the patient's pain and suffering. Thus, granting the plaintiffs' motion to withdraw the admissions would aid in the ascertainment of the truth and the development of the merits.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals' decision affirming the circuit court's order allowing the family to withdraw the admissions was affirmed, and the cause was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

117 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baron


No. 2007AP1289-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI 58; 318 Wis. 2d 60; 769 N.W.2d 34; 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 268; 37 Media L. Rep. 1929


March 6, 2009, Argued 
June 23, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2006CF496). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Jefferson. JUDGE: Randy R. Koschnick.
State v. Baron, 2008 WI App 90, 312 Wis. 2d 789, 754 N.W.2d 175, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 410 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that reversed a decision of the Jefferson County Circuit Court that held that Wis. Stat. § 943.201(2)(c) (2005-06), which punished the unauthorized use of another individual's personal identifying information in order to harm that individual reputation, violated the right to freedom of speech under U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, without authorization, accessed his supervisor's e-mail account, reviewed messages between his supervisor and the woman with whom he was having an affair, and sent portions of their messages from the supervisor's account to various acquaintances; his supervisor committed suicide the next day. Defendant was charged with a violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.201(2)(c). On review of the appellate court opinion upholding the statute as constitutional, the court held that the statute, as applied to the facts of this specific case, was content based and regulated speech in addition to conduct because whether defendant's conduct was prohibited depended entirely upon whether defendant's speech--the content of the e-mails--was intended to be reputation-harming speech. As a result, the statute was to be analyzed under strict scrutiny. However, because the statute, as applied to defendant, was narrowly tailored to achieve a compelling government interest, it was constitutional. The statute survived strict scrutiny in that it was narrowly tailored and applied only when a defendant intentionally used another individual's personal information to harm that individual's reputation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

 

118 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ferguson


No. 2007AP2095-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI 50; 317 Wis. 2d 586; 767 N.W.2d 187; 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 141


December 16, 2008, Argued 
June 16, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2006CF233). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Marathon. JUDGE: Gregory B. Huber.
State v. Ferguson, 2008 WI App 36, 308 Wis. 2d 397, 746 N.W.2d 606, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 74 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of misdemeanor obstructing an officer. Determining that the jury instruction given by the circuit court for the lawful authority element of obstruction was an incorrect statement of the law, the Wisconsin Court of Appeals reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State argued that the officers acted in accordance with the law because they complied with Wis. Stat. § 968.07(1)(d) (2005-06). The appellate court agreed, finding that the police had probable cause to arrest defendant for disorderly conduct; once she was removed from her house, the police were not required to re-arrest her for disorderly conduct in order to make her continued custody lawful. Therefore, her continuing struggles outside of her home occurred when the police were lawfully transporting her to the station house. Although the jury was not instructed about exigent circumstances, it did receive an instruction on lawful authority. The jury necessarily found that there were reasonable grounds to believe defendant was committing or had committed a crime because it convicted defendant of obstruction. Under the instruction given, the jury must have found that the officers acted pursuant to their lawful authority if it found that the officers had reasonable grounds to believe defendant was committing a crime. As the jury convicted defendant, it found this fact. Thus, if the failure to instruct the jury on exigent circumstances was error, it was harmless.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's decision was reversed, and the circuit court's judgment of conviction was affirmed.

State v. Welda


No. 2007AP2024-CR

DISPOSITION: Dismissed.

Defendant's motion to dismiss the hate-crime penalty enhancer was granted by the circuit court, and the State appealed. Furthermore, it was uncertain whether defendant would be convicted of disorderly conduct. If he was not convicted, the issues relating to the penalty enhancer would be moot. Review in the case was improvidently granted.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed its review of the decision of the court of appeals.

State v. Ndina


No. 2007AP005-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI 21; 315 Wis. 2d 653; 761 N.W.2d 612; 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 14


February 26, 2009, Argued 
February 26, 2009, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Dennis P. Moroney. (L.C. No.2002CF006623).
State v. Ndina, 2007 WI App 268, 306 Wis. 2d 706, 743 N.W.2d 722, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1018 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the circuit court's order granting defendant a new trial following his conviction for attempted first-degree intentional homicide while using a dangerous weapon.


OVERVIEW: The victim, who was defendant's nephew, was stabbed during a family gathering. The circuit court issued a sequestration order requiring witnesses to stay outside the courtroom until they testified and not to discuss their testimony. Two disturbances occurred among defendant's family members in the courtroom during testimony. The prosecutor suggested that persons entering and leaving the courtroom might have been violating the sequestration order by conveying information to prospective witnesses. Without objection, the circuit court excluded all of defendant's family members except his mother from the courtroom until testimony ended. Noting that the State did not raise the issue of forfeiture or waiver during the postconviction hearing, the court declined to address that issue. The court concluded that although the exclusion order implicated defendant's Sixth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VI, right to a public trial, the order was justified under the circumstances. Violations of the sequestration order seemed likely, the closure was not overbroad, the circuit court implicitly determined that no less restrictive alternatives existed, and the findings on the record were sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals, reversed the new trial order, reinstated the judgment rendered by the jury, and remanded the matter to the circuit court for additional postconviction remedies and proceedings required by law.

 

121 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


De La Trinidad v. Capitol Indem. Corp.


No. 2007AP45


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2009 WI 8; 315 Wis. 2d 324; 759 N.W.2d 586; 2009 Wisc. LEXIS 3


November 4, 2008, Argued 
January 23, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Kenosha. JUDGE: David M. Bastianelli. (L.C. No. 2005CV145).
De La Trinidad v. Capitol Indem. Corp., 2008 WI App 36, 308 Wis. 2d 394, 746 N.W.2d 604, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 50 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death suit, appellants, the parents of two children who drowned in a pond, challenged a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that affirmed a circuit court order dismissing their lawsuit against appellees, a recreational facility, its employee, and its insurer, on the ground that the recreational immunity statute, Wis. Stat. § 895.52 (2005-06), applied and barred their cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The recreational facility described itself in its articles of incorporation as a hunt and sportsman club with the purpose of promoting wetlands preservation and environmental education. Its regulations allow dues-paying members to invite guests to events held on the its grounds, and it collected extra fees from member who hosted events to which guests were invited. At one such event, the two children drowned. Their parents filed a negligence action, but the recreational facility was deemed immune under Wis. Stat. § 895.52. On review, the court held that the recreational facility was a nonprofit organization under the recreational immunity statute and was immune from liability. The facility's articles of incorporation, tax returns, and financial statements established that it was organized and conducted as a nonprofit organization, a fact recognized by both Wisconsin and the federal government. That the recreational facility might have earned a profit did render it ineligible for classification as a nonprofit organization because nonprofit entities were barred from distributing profits to directors, officers, and members but were not barred from earning a profit.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

State v. Denk


No. 2006AP1744-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 130; 315 Wis. 2d 5; 758 N.W.2d 775; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 1063



December 30, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Pepin County, Dane F. Morey, Judge, and James J. Duvall, Judge. (L.C. No. 2004CF31).
State v. Denk, 2008 WI 40, 308 Wis. 2d 613, 749 N.W.2d 664, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 221 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed orders from the Circuit Court for Pepin County (Wisconsin) denying his motions to suppress evidence and to withdraw his guilty plea. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin certified a question under Wis. Stat. § 809.61 (2005-06): whether the police may search the personal belongings of a passenger that were are found outside a motor vehicle incident to the arrest of the driver.


OVERVIEW: After pulling over the vehicle defendant was a passenger in and arresting the driver, the officer searched an eyeglasses case lying on the ground next to the passenger door that defendant admitted belonged to him and found a glass methamphetamine pipe and some cleaning tools. On review, the court held that the search of the eyeglass case was a permissible search incident to the arrest of the driver because the officer was outnumbered at a late night arrest involving two men and he knew that narcotics were present. The proximity of the eyeglass case to the car, to defendant, and to the driver, as well as its unexplained location at defendant's feet, raised questions about the danger defendant posed acting alone or in concert with the driver. Because the warrantless search of the eyeglass case was lawful, the search of defendant was also lawful. Defendant's admitted ownership of the case containing a methamphetamine pipe gave the officer probable cause to arrest him and to search incident to that arrest. Defendant was not entitled to withdraw his guilty plea because he received the benefits of his plea bargain by avoiding a substantial period of incarceration.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed and the certified question was answered in the affirmative.

Office of Lawyer Regulation v. Crandall (In re Crandall)


No. 2008AP570-D


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 112; 314 Wis. 2d 33; 754 N.W.2d 501; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 357



July 31, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Office of Lawyer Regulation v. Crandall (In re Disciplinary Proceedings Crandall), 2011 WI 21, 332 Wis. 2d 698, 798 N.W.2d 183, 2011 Wisc. LEXIS 156 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Office of Lawyer Regulation v. Crandall (In re Crandall), 2006 WI 6, 287 Wis. 2d 102, 708 N.W.2d 690, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 5 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant, the Wisconsin Office of Lawyer Regulation, filed a complaint against respondent attorney to initiate a disciplinary proceeding in this court. One of the 9 counts was a request under Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 22.22 for the imposition of discipline in Wisconsin reciprocal to a 30-day suspension imposed by the Supreme Court of Minnesota. The attorney filed a response to the court's order to show cause.


OVERVIEW: The attorney argued that the counts for new misconduct should not have been included with the count for reciprocal discipline. The court agreed, holding that in cases of separate misconduct and reciprocal discipline, the counts should be brought in separate proceedings. The court rejected the attorney's argument that the copies of the other jurisdiction's orders were not certified. Although Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 22.22(2)(a) provided for a certified copy of the disciplinary judgment or order issued by the other jurisdiction to be attached to the complaint, the attachment of non-certified copies did not require the dismissal of the reciprocal discipline counts because any error was technical and did not prejudice the attorney. The court's imposition of discipline for professional misconduct that allegedly occurred in another state did not accord extraterritorial effect to Wisconsin's Rules of Professional Conduct for Attorneys. Rather, imposing reciprocal discipline was a means to ensure that Wisconsin attorneys comport themselves in a manner that promotes the efficient administration of the law and to protect the citizens of Wisconsin who needed competent and trustworthy attorneys.


OUTCOME: The court imposed a 30-day suspension on the attorney.

 

124 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arias


No. 2006AP974-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 84; 311 Wis. 2d 358; 752 N.W.2d 748; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 335



July 9, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Clark County, Jon M. Counsell, judge. (L.C. No. 2005CF131).
State v. Arias, 2007 WI 114, 302 Wis. 2d 109, 737 N.W.2d 435, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 557 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Clark County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of defendant and suppressed evidence. The appellate court certified two issues to the supreme court concerning whether a dog sniff of a stopped vehicle was a search and whether the vehicle stop was unreasonably prolonged.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court granted defendant's motion to suppress the weapon and the drugs obtained pursuant to the search conducted following a police dog's sniff of the exterior of the vehicle in which defendant was a passenger. The appellate court certified two issues to the supreme court: 1) Whether, under the Wisconsin Constitution, a dog sniff of a stopped vehicle was a search; and 2) whether the vehicle stop was unreasonably prolonged in duration by the officer's controlled substance investigation. The supreme court answered both questions in the negative. A dog sniff of the exterior of a vehicle located in a public place did not constitute a search under the Wis. Const. art. I, § 11. Secondly, the officer who performed a controlled substance investigation did not unreasonably prolong his seizure of defendant. The circuit court's finding that the dog sniff prolonged the detention by approximately 38 minutes was clearly erroneous. The dog sniff prolonged the detention by no more than 78 seconds. That 78 seconds was not an unreasonable incremental intrusion upon defendant's liberty. Thus, the dog sniff did not unreasonably prolong in duration the controlled substance investigation.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was reversed, and the cause was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings. Following remand, if a party moved the circuit court to determine whether the dog sniff was sufficient to establish probable cause to conduct a search of the vehicle, the supreme court's decision did not preclude the circuit court from holding a hearing on such a motion, if the circuit court chose to do so.

State v. Sanders


No. 2006AP2060-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 85; 311 Wis. 2d 257; 752 N.W.2d 713; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 336



July 9, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Racine. JUDGE: Dennis J. Barry. (L.C. No. 2005CF600).
State v. Sanders, 2007 WI App 174, 304 Wis. 2d 159, 737 N.W.2d 44, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 526 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that reversed a circuit court ruling denying defendant's motion to suppress physical evidence and statements that law enforcement officers obtained following a warrantless entry into defendant's home and two subsequent warrantless searches of defendant's bedroom.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court determined that the issue turned on whether the law enforcement officers' two warrantless searches of defendant's bedroom were justified under the protective sweep and search incident to arrest exceptions to the Fourth Amendment's warrant requirement, not the issue decided by the court of appeal, which was whether the law enforcement officers' warrantless entry into defendant's home to make a warrantless arrest was justified under the Fourth Amendment. In ruling that the circuit court erred in denying defendant's suppression motions, the court concluded that, where officers entered defendant home to arrest him for obstructing officers investigating an animal cruelty complaint, the officers did not have the right to search a canister in defendant's bedroom and seize its contents. Although the officer claimed to be conducting a protective sweep for individuals who might be armed, the canister was too small an object in which a person could hide. Further, the second search of defendant's bedroom likewise violated the Fourth Amendment; it was not a search incident to an arrest because defendant had already been removed from the home when the search was conducted.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed but on different grounds.

Town of Rhine v. Bizzell


No. 2006AP450


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 76; 311 Wis. 2d 1; 751 N.W.2d 780; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 328



July 1, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County, Gary Langhoff, Judge. L.C. No. 2004CV898.
Town of Rhine v. Bizzell, 2007 WI 134, 305 Wis. 2d 131, 742 N.W.2d 528, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 837 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded to the circuit court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Town brought actions against respondents, a recreation club and club members, alleging the members violated public nuisance laws and the club violated Rhine, Wis., Municipal Code § 4.08. The actions were dismissed, and the Wisconsin Court of Appeals certified two issues for review: whether the nuisance claims were properly dismissed, and whether the ordinance in question was facially unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: On review, the Town contended the circuit court erred in ruling that Rhine, Wis., Municipal Code § 4.08(2)(a) was unconstitutional on its face and in dismissing the nuisance ordinance violations against the members. The supreme court held that § 4.08(2)(a), the B-2 District (the district in question), was unconstitutional on its face because it was arbitrary and unreasonable in that it precluded any use as of right (a "no-permitted uses" zone) in the B-2 District, and such a limitation had no substantial relation to the public health, safety, morals or general welfare. No justification existed for precluding all uses in the B-2 District and only providing the club with the possibility of obtaining a conditional use permit. However, the supreme court agreed that the circuit court erred by applying a common-law definition of "nuisance" rather than the definition of "public nuisance" articulated in Rhine, Wis., Municipal Code § 2.02.


OUTCOME: That portion of the judgment holding Rhine, Wis., Municipal Code § 4.08(2)(a) unconstitutional on its face was affirmed; that portion of the judgment dismissing the nuisance complaints was reversed and remanded to the circuit court to apply the proper definition of public nuisance.

State v. Jorgensen


No. 2006AP1847-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 60; 310 Wis. 2d 138; 754 N.W.2d 77; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 311



June 13, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Shawano. JUDGE: James R. Habeck. (L.C. No. 2005CF37).
State v. Jorgensen, 2007 WI App 130, 301 Wis. 2d 750, 731 N.W.2d 384, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 227 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a Wisconsin circuit court, defendant was convicted of bail jumping, operating while intoxicated, operating with a prohibited alcohol concentration, and operating a motor vehicle after revocation. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that as a result of a hearing transcript being read to the jury and the State's closing argument, defendant was denied basic constitutional rights at critical junctures of his trial. The errors included: (1) the admission of other acts such as prior convictions and pending charges for operating while intoxicated; (2) the admission of the fact that a preliminary breath test was conducted and the results of that test; (3) the admission of inadmissible hearsay including "testimony" from the judge and the prosecutor; (4) the admission of information before the jury that was not subject to confrontation, such as the judge's remarks and the prosecutor's commentary regarding the preliminary breath test, their personal observations of defendant, and their conclusions about his guilt; and (5) the prosecutor's assertion of personal knowledge of the facts. The supreme court concluded that the unobjected to errors of the judge and the prosecutor were fundamental, obvious, and substantial, and that the State had failed to meet its burden of proof that these errors were harmless. Thus, these errors constituted plain error under Wis. Stat. § 901.03(4) (2003-04).


OUTCOME: The decision of the intermediate court of appeals was reversed, and the cause was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Olson v. Town of Cottage Grove


No. 2005AP2257


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 51; 309 Wis. 2d 365; 749 N.W.2d 211; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 301



May 30, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit County: Dane. Judge: Angela B. Bartell. (L.C. No. 2004CV2821).
Olson v. Town of Cottage Grove, 2007 WI App 19, 298 Wis. 2d 548, 727 N.W.2d 373, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1271 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant town, challenging the constitutionality of Cottage Grove, Wis., Land Division and Planning Code § 15.15, and, inter alia, seeking approval of a final subdivision plat. The circuit court granted summary judgment to the town on the ground that the suit was not ripe. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin reversed. The town's petition for review of the decision was granted.


OVERVIEW: Since this was an appeal of a decision regarding a declaratory judgment action, the first issue was what standard of review to apply. Although a discretionary standard usually applied under Wisconsin's Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act, Wis. Stat. § 806.04 (2003-2004), the appellate court applied a de novo review to the ripeness determination. The landowner's claim for declaratory relief was ripe for review because, contrary to the circuit court's conclusion, the county board had extended the delayed effective date of conditional approval of the landowner's second zoning petition for one year. That fact demonstrated that the landowner was subject to compliance with § 15.15 when he filed suit against the town because he was required to file a final plat with the town to receive ultimate rezoning approval from the county. The town required the landowner to first comply with § 15.15 by acquiring 10 transfer of development rights before it allowed him to file his final plat. Thus, the landowner's efforts to rezone, subdivide, and develop his property were directly impacted by application of § 15.15 when he filed the suit. As a result, his action for declaratory relief was ripe.


OUTCOME: The lower court's decision was affirmed. The cause was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Walworth County HHS v. Andrea L.O. (In re Lyle D.E.)


No. 2007AP8


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 46; 309 Wis. 2d 161; 749 N.W.2d 168; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 296



May 28, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Walworth County, Robert J. Kennedy, Judge. (L.C. No. 2005TP29).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which terminated the mother's parental rights to her minor son on the ground that he had been adjudged a child in continuing need of protection or services, under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2) (2005-06), by petitioner Walworth County Department of Health & Human Services.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated to the first ground terminating the mother's parental rights, namely that the child had been adjudged a child in need of protection or services (CHIPS). The mother contended that the stipulation constituted an invalid withdrawal of her demand for a jury trial on the CHIPS element. The court found that the stipulation addressed a single, undisputed, paper element where another element was the focus of the controversy, whether there was a substantial likelihood that the mother would not meet the conditions for return within a year. Regardless of the stipulation, the mother received a jury trial because the jury was presented with ample evidence and instructed on the CHIPS element. The circuit court did not err in failing to engage the mother in a personal colloquy to determine that the withdrawal was knowing and voluntary. The mother agreed to the stipulation in open court, and there was ample uncontroverted evidence to support the stipulated element. However, the court urged circuit courts in termination proceedings to consider engaging a parent in a colloquy to explain that a stipulation to an element withdrew that element from the jury's consideration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order terminating the mother's parental rights.

 

130 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Quintana


No. 2006AP499-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 33; 308 Wis. 2d 615; 748 N.W.2d 447; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 176



May 1, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Marathon. JUDGE: Vincent K. Howard. (L.C. No. 2004CF733).
State v. Quintana, 2007 WI App 29, 299 Wis. 2d 234, 729 N.W.2d 776, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 14 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A circuit court held that the forehead did not qualify as an "other bodily member" under Wis. Stat. § 940.21 (2003-04) and that the violent crime in a school zone penalty enhancer under Wis. Stat. § 939.632 was unconstitutional as applied to defendant. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin reversed and remanded the case. Defendant petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for striking his sleeping wife in the head with a hammer. On appeal, the court held that the forehead qualified as an "other bodily member" under Wis. Stat. § 940.21. Because the legislature intended the phrase to construed broadly rather than narrowly, the phrase encompassed all body parts, including a person's forehead. The application of the mayhem statute was limited by the need to prove that a person specifically intended to disable or disfigure. The court further held that the violent crime in a school zone penalty enhancement of Wis. Stat. § 939.632 was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant because the legislature sought to deter violent crime near schools in an effort to create a safety zone around schools, and the 1,000-foot perimeter was a reasonable distance to try to accomplish the legislative goal. The legislature had clearly concluded that children congregated on or near school premises and were more likely to live near school premises. Under § 939.632, the crime of mayhem was specifically included in the definition of "violent crime."


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court reversing and remanded the case was affirmed.

State v. Harenda Enters.


No. 2005AP1829


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 16; 307 Wis. 2d 604; 746 N.W.2d 25; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 11



March 13, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Harenda Enters., 2008 WI 115, 310 Wis. 2d 711, 754 N.W.2d 853, 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 496 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Harenda Enters. v. Wisconsin, 129 S. Ct. 573, 172 L. Ed. 2d 431, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8240 (U.S., Nov. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Kitty Brennan. (L.C. No. 2003CV6540).
State v. Harenda Enters., 2006 WI App 230, 297 Wis. 2d 571, 724 N.W.2d 434, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1014 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State instituted proceedings to impose environmental penalties and ancillary charges against defendant company in connection with the company's testing for asbestos contamination. A Wisconsin trial court awarded summary judgment to the State. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin reversed the trial court's judgment, and the State sought review.


OVERVIEW: The case centered on the question of the proper method for testing whether material constituted asbestos-containing material (ACM) under Wis. Admin. Code NR § 447.02 2 and 40 C.F.R. pt. 763, subpt. E, app. E, § 1.7.2.1. According to clarifications by the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA), separate layers in multi-layered systems were to be analyzed separately, such that no averaging or dilution by combining layers of ACM with nonasbestos-containing material was allowed. The supreme court determined that: (1) the language of § 1.7.2.1 was ambiguous; (2) giving deference to an agency's interpretation of its own rule, the EPA's interpretation was controlling because it was neither inconsistent with § 1.7.2.1 nor clearly erroneous; (3) the EPA's clarifications did not constitute impermissible rule making, but were valid interpretive rules; and (4) the circuit court's judgment did not violate the company's substantive due process rights because there was nothing arbitrary in the circuit court's conclusion that tests showed that material from a disputed area was ACM.


OUTCOME: The decision of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.

 

132 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Helgeland v. Wis. Municipalities


No. 2005AP2540


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2008 WI 9; 307 Wis. 2d 1; 745 N.W.2d 1; 2008 Wisc. LEXIS 6



February 7, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Dane. Judge: David T. Flanagan. (L.C. No. 2005CV1265).
Helgeland v. Wis. Municipalities, 2006 WI App 216, 296 Wis. 2d 880, 724 N.W.2d 208, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 912 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employees and their same-sex domestic partners sued defendant state entities, alleging that Wis. Stat. § 40.02(2) (2003-2004) violated Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. Petitioner municipalities' motion to intervene or for joinder was denied. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin affirmed the circuit court's order denying intervention and joinder. The municipalities appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The municipalities did not have a right to intervene under Wis. Stat. § 803.09(1) (2003-2004) because even though their motion was timely and a judgment in the state employees' favor might have exposed them to the adverse effect of stare decisis, they only claimed a generalized interest in the subject of the action. The municipalities failed to demonstrate how their interests related to the subject of the action in a direct and immediate fashion. Moreover, their interests were adequately represented by the state entities. The municipalities were properly denied permissive intervention under Wis. Stat. § 803.09(2) (2003-2004) as the circuit court's decision was based on reasonable consideration of delay. The circuit court also did not err in refusing to join the municipalities sua sponte under Wis. Stat. § 803.03(1)(b)(1) (2003-2004) because if a person had no right of intervention under Wis. Stat. § 803.09(1) (2003-2004), the courts had no duty to join that person sua sponte as a necessary party. Joinder under Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11) (2003-2004) was properly denied as the municipalities were not public officers charged with enforcing Wis. Stat. § 40.02(2) (2003-2004).


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

133 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



City of Janesville v. CC Midwest, Inc.


No. 2004AP267


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI 93; 302 Wis. 2d 599; 734 N.W.2d 428; 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 422


October 11, 2006, Oral Argument 
July 11, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Rock-Janesville. JUDGE: John W. Roethe. (L.C. No. 2003CV1288).
City of Janesville v. CC Midwest, Inc., 2006 WI App 21, 289 Wis. 2d 453, 710 N.W.2d 713, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 69 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court entered a judgment granting plaintiff city a writ of assistance to remove defendant corporation from property that the city previously acquired by exercising its power of eminent domain. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals reversed the judgment. Review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The intermediate appellate court deemed that the city was not entitled to a writ of assistance, and it certified a question with respect to "comparable replacement business." The city had acquired ownership of the property through condemnation proceedings. The corporation informed the city that none of the identified relocation sites was a comparable replacement business because none satisfied its interpretation of the statutory criteria. Relocation assistance benefits did not have a direct relationship to the fair market value of a tenant's interest, and therefore, incidental or consequential damages were not considered in the constitutional requirement for just compensation. In satisfying its statutory obligation to make available a comparable replacement property pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 32.05(8)(b), (c) (2003-04), prior to being entitled to a writ of assistance, the city was required to proceed to identify one or more properties that met the parameters of Wis. Stat. § 32.19(2)(c) (2003-04) to serve as a comparable replacement business. The supreme court concluded that the city had done so, and it had made no contrary concession in this regard.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the decision of the intermediate appellate court.

HSBC Realty Credit Corp. v. City of Glendale (In re City of Glendale Cmty. Dev. Auth. Condemnation Award)


No. 2005AP1042


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI 94; 303 Wis. 2d 1; 735 N.W.2d 77; 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 423


January 4, 2007, Oral Argument 
July 11, 2007, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the 2006 WI App 160. Reported at: Court of Appeals. 2006 WI App 160, 295 Wis. 2d 493, 721 N.W.2d 489 (Ct. App. 2006-Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Richard J. Sankovitz. (L.C. No. 2004CV10624).
HSBC Realty Credit Corp. v. Glendale (In re City of Glendale Cmty. Dev. Auth. Condemnation Award), 2006 WI App 160, 295 Wis. 2d 493, 721 N.W.2d 489, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 591 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, petitioner, filed a petition for review of a decision entered by the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, reversing an order of the Milwaukee County Circuit Court, which transferred a condemnation award from the control of appellant, county clerk of court, to a money market account at a private bank, in the eminent domain case involving respondent, city.


OVERVIEW: The city deposited the condemnation award of $ 14,439,294.84 with the clerk of court. The clerk of court invested the award in the county's general fund with the interest to go to the fund. The award would earn about 2 percent interest annually, producing about $ 24,000 a month for the county. The petitioner requested the award be placed into an interest bearing account for the benefit of the ultimate recipients of the award. The petitioner's motion was granted by a circuit judge and support by the circuit court. The court of appeals reversed, finding that the circuit court did not have statutory authority to order the clerk of court to transfer the award into a private money market account. The reviewing court held that Wis. Stat. § 59.40(3)(c) (2003-2004) empowered the circuit judge not only to veto the clerk of court's authority to invest "certain funds" and pay all interest on those funds into the county general fund, but also to direct the clerk of court to transfer "certain funds" from the his control into a secure private account for the benefit of persons ultimately entitled to the funds.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was reversed and the cause was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Lornson v. Siddiqui


No. 2005AP2315


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI 92; 302 Wis. 2d 519; 735 N.W.2d 55; 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 421


October 11, 2006, Oral Argument  
July 10, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County, Robert A. Hawley, Judge. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Winnebago. JUDGE: Robert Hawley. (L.C. No. 2003CV1094).
Lornson v. Siddiqui, 2006 WI 108, 292 Wis. 2d 415, 718 N.W.2d 728, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 571 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff daughters sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), dismissing their wrongful death claims against defendants doctors, medical group, hospital, and insurance company based on lack of standing. The case was certified by the Court of Appeals of Wisconsin under Wis. Stat. § 809.61 (2005-06).


OVERVIEW: The patient died from complications of a large paraesophageal hiatal hernia. Her husband alleged that defendants acted negligently by failing to timely diagnose and treat the patient's hernia. Before trial the husband died, and the daughters of the patient and the husband were substituted as plaintiffs. On appeal of the trial court's decision dismissing the action for lack of standing, the court held that because in wrongful death actions, an eligible claimant's cause of action did not survive the death of the claimant, the husband's wrong death claim did not survive. The court further affirmed the dismissal with prejudice of the daughters' claim in their capacity as personal representatives of the husband's estate, as well as their claim in their capacity as adult children of the patient, because in a medical malpractice wrongful death case, adult children of the deceased were not listed as eligible claimants and therefore were not eligible because of the exclusivity of Wis. Stat. § 655.007 as interpreted in the Czapinski case.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the daughters' wrongful death claims was affirmed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

136 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Rouse v. Theda Clark Med. Ctr.


No. 2005AP2743


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI 87; 302 Wis. 2d 358; 735 N.W.2d 30; 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 416


April 25, 2007, Oral Argument 
July 6, 2007, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER EDITING AND MODIFICATION. THE FINAL VERSION WILL APPEAR IN THE BOUND VOLUME OF THE OFFICIAL REPORTS.


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2004CV162). Reported at: 297 Wis. 2d 584, 724 N.W.2d 703 (Ct. App. 2006-Unpublished). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Calument. JUDGE: Donald A. Poppy.
Rouse v. Theda Clark Med. Ctr., 2006 WI App 244, 297 Wis. 2d 584, 724 N.W.2d 703, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 913 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed a judgment of the circuit court dismissing with prejudice plaintiff patient's medical malpractice action against defendant, the University of Wisconsin Hospital & Clinics Authority (UWHCA), because plaintiff failed to provide notice pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 893.80 (2003-04). Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sole question on appeal was whether the UWHCA, as a statutorily-created, public body corporate and politic, was a "political corporation" for purposes of § 893.80 (2003-04). The UWHCA was a "political corporation" because of the power and structure provided by the legislature in Wis. Stat. ch. 233 (2003-04). Because plaintiff failed to service the notice required by Wis. Stat. § 893.80 on the UWHCA, he could not maintain his medical malpractice action against it. Plaintiff argued that § 893.80 (2003-04) should not have applied to his case because of the exclusivity provisions of Wis. Stat. ch. 655 (2003-04) for bringing a medical malpractice claim. However, the notice statute was a specific statute of limitations which applied in medical malpractice cases against enumerated types of governmental bodies, such as political corporations. The language of Wis. Stat. § 893.80(1m) (2003-04) explicitly anticipated the application of § 893.80 to medical malpractice claims against governmental bodies. The generally exclusive nature of Wis. Stat. ch. 655 (2003-04) did not prevent the application of Wis. Stat. § 893.80 (2003-04) in the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals.

Trinity Petroleum, Inc. v. Scott Oil Co.


No. 2005AP2837


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI 88; 302 Wis. 2d 299; 735 N.W.2d 1; 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 417


April 11, 2007, Argued  
July 6, 2007, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER EDITING AND MODIFICATION. THE FINAL VERSION WILL APPEAR IN THE BOUND VOLUME OF THE OFFICIAL REPORTS.


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. 2006 WI App 219, 296 Wis. 2d 666, 724 N.W.2d 259. Reported at: 2006 WI App 219, 296 Wis. 2d 666, 724 N.W.2d 259 (Ct. App. 2006-Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Waukesha. JUDGE: James R. Kieffer. (L.C. No. 2004CV846).
Trinity Petroleum, Inc. v. Scott Oil Co., 2006 WI App 219, 296 Wis. 2d 666, 724 N.W.2d 259, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 865 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant oil company appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which applied the new Wis. Stat. § 802.05 (2005-06) (new rule) and affirmed the denial of its motion for sanctions against plaintiff delivery company for the alleged frivolous commencement and maintenance of an action for the breach of a contract to deliver the oil company's petroleum products to customers.


OVERVIEW: After the new rule's effective date, the oil company obtained summary judgment and, relying on former Wis. Stat. §§ 802.05 and 814.025 (2003-04) (former rules), filed a motion to impose sanctions against the delivery company for filing a frivolous breach of contract action. The circuit court denied the motion, finding that oil company did not comply with the new rule's safe harbor notice provision. The court of appeals affirmed. The oil company appealed. The court reversed because the circuit court and court of appeals erred as a matter of law in holding that new rule had retroactive application without exception. The court held that the new rule was a procedural rule that generally had retroactive application but was not to be applied retroactively when it diminished a contract, disturbed vested rights, or imposed an unreasonable burden. Although the retroactive application of the new rule did not disturb a contract or substantive vested right, the court remanded the case for a determination of whether the retroactive application imposed an unreasonable burden on a party who was to comply with its procedural requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and the order of the circuit court. The court remanded the cause to the circuit court for whether retroactive application of the new rule imposed an unreasonable burden, whether the former or new rules applied, and whether, under the applicable provision and the unreasonable burden standard, the delivery company engaged in frivolous conduct and what sanctions were to be imposed.

State v. Bobby G. (In re Marquette S.)


No. 2006AP66-NM


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI 77; 301 Wis. 2d 531; 734 N.W.2d 81; 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 406


February 13, 2007, Oral Argument 
June 22, 2007, Decided 
June 22, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Bobby G. (In re Marquette S.), 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 118 (Wis. Ct. App., Feb. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Thomas R. Cooper. (L.C. No. 2004TP285).
State v. Bobby G., 2006 WI 126, 297 Wis. 2d 319, 724 N.W.2d 202, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 752 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the father, sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the circuit court's judgment terminating the father's parental rights to his biological son. The circuit court had granted the State partial summary judgment at the fact-finding phase relating to the grounds for termination.


OVERVIEW: The case involved a review of the appellate court's decision summarily affirming the dispositional order of the circuit court, terminating the father's parental rights. The circuit court granted the State partial summary judgment at the first step of the termination of parental rights proceedings, the fact-finding phase relating to the grounds for termination. The supreme court reversed and remanded, stating that in determining whether a party seeking termination of parental rights had proven by clear and convincing evidence that a biological father failed to assume parental responsibility under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6) (2003-04), the circuit court must consider the biological father's efforts after he discovered that he was the father but before the circuit court adjudicated the grounds of the termination proceeding. The circuit court proceeded under an erroneous interpretation of the statute and the facts were not fully developed. To the extent that facts were developed, those facts and their import were in dispute. The parties disputed whether the father had assumed parental responsibility after he learned of his paternity but before adjudication of the grounds for termination.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the decision of the appellate court and the summary judgment and remanded the cause to the circuit court for a fact-finding hearing to determine whether grounds existed for termination of the father's parental rights and, if necessary, for a dispositional hearing on whether the father's parental rights should be terminated in the best interests of the child.

Kocken v. Wis. Council 40


No. 2005AP2742


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI 72; 301 Wis. 2d 266; 732 N.W.2d 828; 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 400; 182 L.R.R.M. 2592; 154 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,438


January 16, 2007, Oral Argument 
June 14, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Brown. JUDGE: Mark A. Warpinski. APPEAL from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Brown County, Mark A. Warpinski, Judge. (L.C. No. 2004CV1170).
Kocken v. Wis. Council 40 AFSCME, 2006 WI 126, 297 Wis. 2d 324, 724 N.W.2d 207, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 897 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sheriff sought declaratory relief in an labor-related matter. The Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, granted a permanent injunction to the sheriff, against defendants, a union that represented employees of a jail. The injunction prevented the union from pursuing any type of action before the Wisconsin Employment Relations Commission or seeking injunctive relief. The union appealed.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court also ordered the union to withdraw its prohibited practice complaint filed with the Wisconsin Employment Relations Commission. The matter arose as a result of the sheriff's proposal to stop using county employees to prepare meals for the local jail and instead contract with a private food service provider. The issue presented was whether the sheriff's decision fell within the sheriff's constitutional powers, rights, and duties, and was thus not subject to legislative limitations, including a collective bargaining agreement. The supreme court held that the sheriff's hiring and firing of personnel to provide food service was not a "time immemorial" principal and important duty that characterized and distinguished the office of sheriff, and as such, was not within the sheriff's constitutional powers. Rather, the hiring and firing of personnel to provide food service to the county jail fell within the "mundane and commonplace" "internal management and administrative duties" not protected by the constitution. Hiring and firing personnel to provide food to inmates was subject to legislative regulation, including collective bargaining under Wis. Stat. § 111.70 (2003-04).


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, and it remanded the cause to the circuit court to dismiss the sheriff's complaint seeking declaratory relief. The supreme court also vacated the permanent injunction.

County of Milwaukee v. Williams


Nos. 2005AP2686 & 2005AP2687


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI 69; 301 Wis. 2d 134; 732 N.W.2d 770; 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 396


March 6, 2007, Oral Argument 
June 12, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:
REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit Court. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Daniel L. Konkol. (L.C. Nos. 2005FO107 & 2005FO110).
County of Milwaukee v. Williams, 2006 WI App 153, 295 Wis. 2d 389, 720 N.W.2d 177, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 567 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were found guilty of picking up passengers in their taxis at General Mitchell International Airport without an airport permit, in violation of Milwaukee, Wis., County Ord. 4.05. The Court of Appeals, Wisconsin, affirmed the judgments of conviction, and defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: On different dates in January 2005, defendants traveled to the airport to pick up passengers who had made prior arrangements for pickups by the cab company. After ignoring warnings that they could not accept departing taxi fares from the airport, defendants were issued citations for violating the county ordinance, and received fines of $250. The reviewing court addressed the county's ability to enact an ordinance that prohibited taxis without airport permits from making prearranged pickups of customers, where the same ordinance allowed limousines without permits to make such pickups. The reviewing court held that the county ordinance conflicted with the requirement under Wis. Stat. § 114.14 (2005-2006) that the public have equal access to airport services, and to that extent was invalid and unenforceable. The county had provided nothing in the record to support the claim that allowing taxis without permits to make prearranged pickups would create the problems associated with the open system, even though prearranged service by limousines did not cause such problems. Also, the ordinance did not conflict with Wis. Stat. §§ 133.01, 349.24, and 194.02 (2005-2006).


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed and the causes were remanded with instructions to vacate the judgments of conviction.

State v. Post


No. 2005AP2778-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2007 WI 60; 301 Wis. 2d 1; 733 N.W.2d 634; 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 57


February 14, 2007, Oral Argument  
May 23, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reported at: 296 Wis. 2d 420, 722 N.W.2d 401 (Ct. App. 2006-Unpublished). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Sauk. JUDGE: Patrick Taggart. (L.C. No. 2004CF94).
State v. Post, 2006 WI App 194, 296 Wis. 2d 420, 722 N.W.2d 401, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 715 (2006).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversed a judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration, as a fifth offense. The court of appeals concluded that slight deviations within a single travel lane did not give rise to a reasonable suspicion that a driver was intoxicated. Petitioner State sought review.


OVERVIEW: The State, in essence, asked for a bright-line rule that repeated weaving within a single lane provided the reasonable suspicion necessary to justify a traffic stop. What mattered was whether the vehicle's movements, considered with the totality of the circumstances, gave rise to a reasonable suspicion that defendant was driving while intoxicated. The Supreme Court of Wisconsin determined that weaving within a single traffic lane did not alone give rise to the reasonable suspicion necessary to conduct an investigative stop of a vehicle. However, under the totality of the instant circumstances, the police officer had reasonable suspicion and the stop did not violate defendant's constitutional right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. The officer's testimony indicated that defendant's weave was between five feet and nine feet, based on his individual estimates of distances and that the vehicle moved laterally ten feet. The incident also took place at 9:30 at night. While that was not as significant as when poor driving took place at or around "bar time," it did lend some further credence to the suspicion that defendant was driving while intoxicated.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed.

State v. Lord


No. 2005AP1485-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 122; 297 Wis. 2d 592; 723 N.W.2d 425; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 727



November 9, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Remanded by State v. Lord, 2007 WI App 19, 727 N.W.2d 373, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1212 (Wis. Ct. App., Dec. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 2006 WI App 31, 289 Wis. 2d 551, 710 N.W.2d 726 (Ct. App. 2006) - Unpublished. Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: Victor Manian & Michael B. Brennan. (L.C. No. 2003CM4635). State's motion for summary reversal of Court of Appeals decision.
State v. Lord, 2006 WI App 31, 289 Wis. 2d 551, 710 N.W.2d 726, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 88 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Motion granted and cause remanded to the court of appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Wisconsin, the successful party at the circuit court and the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), filed a motion to summarily reverse the decision of the court of appeals. The court of appeals granted defendant's petition for review to address whether law enforcement officers could stop an automobile on the sole ground that the automobile had a temporary license plate.


OVERVIEW: The question before the court was whether a temporary plate on an automobile, without more, created reasonable suspicion to justify law enforcement's stop of that vehicle. The State's motion for summary reversal conceded, as defendant argued all along, that the decision of the court of appeals conflicted with the holding and rationale of United States Supreme Court case law. Although the State conceded the point of law, the court noted that it, not the parties, decided questions of law. The court stated, however, that it readily accepted the State's concession without further briefing or argument because the State's concession was well-settled law requiring no extensive research or explanation. The Supreme Court opinion at issue stated that except in those situations in which there was at least articulable and reasonable suspicion that a motorist was unlicensed or that an automobile was not registered, or that either the vehicle or an occupant was otherwise subject to seizure for violation of law, stopping an automobile and detaining the driver in order to check his driver's license and the registration of the automobile were unreasonable under the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion and remanded the cause to the court of appeals for reconsideration in light of the court's decision and the request of the parties that further proceedings be conducted in the circuit court.

 

144 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Dairyland Greyhound Park, Inc. v. Doyle


No. 2003AP421


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 107; 295 Wis. 2d 1; 719 N.W.2d 408; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 402


September 7, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
July 14, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Richard J. Callaway, Judge. (L.C. No. 01CV2906).
Dairyland Greyhound Park v. Doyle, 2004 WI 34, 270 Wis. 2d 267, 677 N.W.2d 275, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 236 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tribal gambling establishment appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, the governor and former secretary of administration, and concluded that a 1993 amendment to Wis. Const. art. VI, § 24 did not affect tribal gaming compacts. Plaintiff sought to enjoin defendants from renewing the compacts.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act, 25 U.S.C.S. § 2710(d)(3)(c) and Wis. Stat. § 14.035 (2003-04), the State entered into compacts with 11 tribes that permitted the tribes to engage in certain Class III casino gaming. They lasted for seven-year terms, with automatic extensions for five-year terms. The 1993 Amendment limited gaming. The court affirmed and held that the 1993 Amendment's failure to explicitly address the compacts created an ambiguity as to whether the compacts fell within the its reach, and any language in Panzer v. Doyle, 271 Wis. 2d 295, to the contrary was withdrawn. However, because constitutional amendments were presumed to be prospective, it would have been superfluous for the legislature to exempt the compacts. Also, it was shown that the Legislature and the public who voted did not intend the 1993 Amendment to invalidate the compacts. Under the plain terms of the compacts, changes in State law did not impact the compacts, including renewals and extensions. Because the compacts contemplated extending and amending the scope of gaming, the parties' right of renewal was protected by the Contract Clauses of the United States and Wisconsin Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court.

State v. Campbell


No. 2004AP803-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 99; 294 Wis. 2d 100; 718 N.W.2d 649; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 394


January 11, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
July 12, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Walworth County, Robert J. Kennedy, Judge. Affirmed and cause remanded. (L.C. No. 1998CF29).
State v. Campbell, 2005 WI 136, 285 Wis. 2d 631, 703 N.W.2d 381, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 755 (2005).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin) convicted defendant of two counts of interference with legal custody of a child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.31(1)(b) (1997-98) and felony bail jumping in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.49(1)(b) (1997-98). The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin affirmed. The case was before the court on certification by the court of appeals under Wis. Stat. § 809.61 (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for failing to return his children to his ex-wife when his visitation with the children ended. Defendant challenged his conviction as to one of his children, arguing that the child was not legally adopted by his ex-wife because she procured the adoption order by fraud. At the time of the adoption hearing in Missouri, even though defendant and his family lived in Wisconsin, the ex-wife stated that they still lived in Missouri. On appeal, defendant claimed that the circuit court erred by preventing him from collaterally attacking the validity of the custody order. The court held that because the Wisconsin family court had personal jurisdiction over defendant and defendant received adequate notice of the divorce proceedings, there was no jurisdictional fraud, and the custody order was not void. Defendant's ex-wife therefore had legal custody over the child, and evidence of her alleged fraud in the adoption proceedings could not negate an element of interference with custody. Defendant's fraud allegation did not raise an affirmative defense. The circuit court had the authority to impose attorney fees for standby counsel as a condition of defendant's probation.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The case was remanded to the circuit court to determine whether the full amount of attorney fees should have been imposed.
