Kenosha County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Jodie W. (In re Max G. W.)


No. 2005AP2-NM


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 93; 293 Wis. 2d 530; 716 N.W.2d 845; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 391


March 21, 2006, Oral Argument  
July 11, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Kenosha. Judge: Mary Kay Wagner. (L.C. No. 2004TP23).
Kenosha County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Jodie W., 2006 WI 3, 286 Wis. 2d 660, 708 N.W.2d 692, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 965 (2005).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals of Wisconsin affirming an order of a circuit court terminating the mother's parental rights to her son under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2)(a) (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: The trial court terminated the mother's parental rights to her son, finding that she was unfit because she was unable to meet an impossible condition of return, namely to obtain a suitable residence within 12 months, due to the fact that she was incarcerated. On appeal, the court held that the mother did not waive her right to challenge the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 48.415 by entering a plea of no contest because there was insufficient evidence to support a determination that she entered her plea knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently as required by Wis. Stat. § 48.422(7). The plea form and modifications contained inconsistencies, the trial court's colloquy was incomplete with regard to the inconsistencies, and the trial court refused to allow testimony regarding the mother's reasons for entering the plea. The trial court's application of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2) to the mother violated her substantive due process rights because it was not narrowly tailored. The trial court improperly deemed the mother unfit solely by virtue of her status as an incarcerated person without regard for her actual parenting activities or the condition of her son.


OUTCOME: The judgment affirming the termination of the mother's parental rights was reversed.

Bartholomew v. Wis. Patients Comp. Fund


Case No.: 2004AP2592


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 91; 293 Wis. 2d 38; 717 N.W.2d 216; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 386


April 5, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
July 7, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Kenosha. Judge: Wilbur W. Warren, III. (L.C. No. 2001CV1261).
Bartholomew v. Wis. Patients Comp. Fund, 2006 WI 3, 286 Wis. 2d 660, 708 N.W.2d 692, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 964 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff surviving spouse appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) affirming the decision that awards in a wrongful death case against defendant doctor for damages for the decedent's predeath pain, suffering and disability; damages to the spouse for his predeath loss; and damages for the spouse's postdeath loss of his wife's society were collectively limited by the wrongful death cap of Wis. Stat. § 895.04(4) (2003-03).


OVERVIEW: After being treated by the doctor the decedent suffered a heart attack. She was bedridden in a nursing home until her death five years later. The court reversed and held that Maurin v. Hall, 274 Wis. 2d 28, was unsound in principle and was wrongly decided. Maurin erred in conflating a wrongful death and a survival action and subjecting both to the wrongful death cap. Nothing in any of the statutes indicated a legislative intent to conflate noneconomic damages for predeath claims (such as the victim's pain and suffering and a family member's predeath loss of society and companionship) and noneconomic damages for wrongful death claims for postdeath loss of society into a single cause of action or a single statutory cap. The legislature adopted two caps: a medical malpractice cap for noneconomic damages for predeath claims and a wrongful death cap for noneconomic damages for postdeath loss of society and companionship. Furthermore, no cap applied to the noneconomic damages at issue because Wis. Stat. § 893.55(4)(d) had been held unconstitutional. Therefore, the jury's $ 350,000 award for the spouse's postdeath loss of society and companionship was within the wrongful death cap.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals.


 

148 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Northwest Airlines, Inc. v. Wis. Dep't of Revenue


No. 2004AP319


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 88; 293 Wis. 2d 202; 717 N.W.2d 280; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 384


December 13, 2005, Oral Argument  
July 7, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, John Albert, Judge. Court: Circuit. County: Dane. Judge: John C. Albert. (L.C. No. 2002CV3533).
Northwest Airlines, Inc. v. Wis. Dep't of Revenue, 2005 WI 60, 281 Wis. 2d 117, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 382 (2005).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff airline appealed holdings by the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin that the hub exemption of Wis. Stat. § 70.11(42)(b) (2003-04) was severable; Wis. Stat. § 76.08(1) required it to serve defendant state department of revenue (DOR) within 30 days; and the denial of the re-determination claim did not violate its due process right. The DOR cross-appealed the holding that the hub exemption violated the dormant Commerce Clause.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff challenged the hub exemption on the grounds that it offered two in-state airlines a competitive advantage. The court reversed and held that 49 U.S.C.S. § 40116 showed congressional consent to allow states to impose differential taxes among air carriers. The exemption was limited because § 40116(d)(1)(D) defined "commercial and industrial property" to exclude transportation property and property not subject to a property tax levy. Because the property of the two competitors fit both exceptions to the comparison class, the assessment ratio and tax rate at which their property was taxed were irrelevant. Also, as the exemption did not fall within any of the assessment practices prohibited by the statute, the hub exemption was not subject to dormant Commerce Clause review. Further, since the exemption did not implicate a suspect class or fundamental right, the classifications were upheld as the legislature could have reasonably determined that creating the exemption would help retain air carriers, which would bolster economic development, a legitimate governmental purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's decision that the hub exemption violated the dormant Commerce Clause.

 

149 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Hilton v. Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 2003AP3353


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 84; 293 Wis. 2d 1; 717 N.W.2d 166; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 380


November 9, 2005, Oral Argument  
July 6, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Green Lake. Judge: William M. McMonigal. (L.C. No. 2002CV148).
Hilton v. Dep't of Natural Res., 2005 WI 1, 277 Wis. 2d 151, 691 N.W.2d 353, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 1042 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners' association challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that reversed the decision of the circuit court which had modified an order of the Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) that required the homeowners' association to reduce the number of boat slips on its pier. Appellant Department of Natural Resources (DNR) had expressly adopted the order.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners' association challenged the order requiring a reduction in the number of boat slips. The court held that because the DNR did not appeal the decision of the ALJ, and adopted the decision as its own, the decision was entitled to great weight deference, because it was a decision within the DNR's area of expertise. The court found that the ALJ examined environmental impact, natural scenic beauty, historic use, safety, the absence of a permit, and the DNR's delayed enforcement, among other factors, in determining "reasonable use." The court concluded that there was ample evidence that the ALJ weighed the relevant factors in light of the public trust doctrine. Therefore the court concluded that the DNR's decision to limit the number of boat slips was consistent with applicable law and supported by sufficient evidence that showed the homeowners' association's pier had direct and cumulative adverse impacts to the wildlife and fish habitat, and that the association was entitled to no more than reasonable use, without a permit for its pier. The court declined to address the association's claim that the reduction in the number of boat slips was an unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals decision.


 

150 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brockdorf


Case No.: 2004AP1519


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 76; 291 Wis. 2d 635; 717 N.W.2d 657; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 369


October 12, 2005, Argued  
June 28, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Court: Circuit County: Milwaukee. Judge: Frederick C. Rosa. REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. No. 2004AP1519-CR (L.C. No. 2003CM10122). Reported at: 2005 WI App 21, 278 Wis. 2d 814, 691 N.W.2d 928 (Ct. App. 2004-Unpublished).
State v. Brockdorf, 2005 WI App 21, 278 Wis. 2d 814, 691 N.W.2d 928, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1010 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Milwaukee County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) granted defendant's motion to suppress a statement she made to detectives. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin reversed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a police officer, and her partner were charged with various crimes related to an alleged beating of a shoplifting suspect, including obstructing a detective by knowingly giving false information in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.41(1). Defendant argued that a statement she gave to the detectives should be suppressed because it was involuntary and coerced under the Garrity decision. On appeal, the court held that defendant's statement was voluntary and should be admitted into evidence. Under the two-part test adopted by the court, even though defendant subjectively believed that she would be fired if she elected not to talk to the detectives, that belief was objectively unreasonable because: (1) the detectives did not expressly threaten detective with the loss of her job for choosing to exercise her right to remain silent; (2) there was no state law, ordinance, departmental regulation, or longstanding departmental policy that forced an officer to choose between job loss and self-incrimination; (3) defendant was not in custody during the interview; and (4) defendant was questioned pursuant to a criminal investigation, not a personnel investigation.


OUTCOME: The judgment reversing the suppression of defendant's statement was affirmed.

 

151 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tiepelman


No. 2004AP914-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 66; 291 Wis. 2d 179; 717 N.W.2d 1; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 359



June 9, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 9, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Richland. Judge: Edward E. Leineweber. (L.C. No. 1996CF7).
State v. Tiepelman, 2005 WI App 179, 286 Wis. 2d 464, 703 N.W.2d 683, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 620 (2005).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed a circuit court's judgment of conviction and postconviction order that denied defendant's motion for resentencing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion was based on his claim that the circuit court relied on inaccurate information at his sentencing hearing. The supreme court determined that a defendant who requested resentencing due to the circuit court's use of inaccurate information at the sentencing hearing had to show both that the information was inaccurate and that the court actually relied on the inaccurate information in the sentencing. Defendant had to establish that some of the information presented was inaccurate and that the sentencing court actually relied on that misinformation in reaching its determination in regard to the sentence imposed. The State conceded that the information was inaccurate, and the record made clear that the sentencing court specifically considered the inaccurate information in its decision. The issue of harmless error was not developed to the degree necessary to assist the supreme court in resolving that issue, and since the matter should be remanded for resentencing, the supreme court accepted the stipulation.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the circuit court for resentencing.

Mair v. Trollhaugen Ski Resort


No. 2004AP1252


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 61; 291 Wis. 2d 132; 715 N.W.2d 598; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 357


March 14, 2006, Oral Argument  
June 6, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 2005 WI App 116, 283 Wis. 2d 722, 699 N.W.2d 624 (Ct. App. 2005-Published). Court: Circuit. County: Polk. Judge: Molly E. GaleWyrick. L.C. No. 2002CV573.
Mair v. Trollhaugen Ski Resort, 2005 WI App 116, 283 Wis. 2d 722, 699 N.W.2d 624, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 389 (2005).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a patron, sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a summary judgment order of the circuit court dismissing the patron's safe place claim, Wis. Stat. § 101.11 (2003-04), against respondents, a ski resort and insurer.


OVERVIEW: The patron fractured her right femur in a women's bathroom at the ski resort while exiting a bathroom cubicle. She filed a safe place claim against the ski resort and insurer, which was dismissed on summary judgment. The appellate court affirmed the summary judgment and the supreme court further affirmed. The patron contended that the circuit court erred in applying the 10-year statute of repose in Wis. Stat. § 893.89 (2003-04) to bar her claim brought under the safe place statute, Wis. Stat. § 101.11 (2003-04). The supreme court disagreed and concluded that 10 years after a structure was substantially completed, Wis. Stat. § 893.89 barred safe place claims resulting from injuries caused by structural defects, as opposed to safe place claims resulting from injuries caused by unsafe conditions associated with the structure. Because the facts demonstrated that the patron's fall was caused by alleged defects in the location, depth, and slope of the floor drain that existed since the building's construction, her injury was caused by an alleged structural defect and not an unsafe condition associated with the structure.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

153 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fisher


No. 2004AP2989-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 44; 290 Wis. 2d 121; 714 N.W.2d 495; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 229


February 23, 2006, Oral Argument  
May 17, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Jackson County, John A. Damon, Judge. (L.C. No. 2004CM26). Court: Circuit. County: Jackson. Judge: John A. Damon. Dissented: CROOKS, J., dissents (opinion filed). WILCOX and ROGGENSACK, J.J., join in part.
State v. Fisher, 2005 WI 150, 286 Wis. 2d 103, 705 N.W.2d 663, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 925 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certification from the court of appeals, appellant State sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Jackson County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment dismissing a complaint that charged defendant with unlawfully carrying a concealed weapon in violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.23 (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a tavern owner who kept a loaded gun in his car, and he was arrested one afternoon as he was in the process of running errands. He moved to dismiss the complaint, asserting that he kept the gun for security purposes because he routinely transported large amounts of cash generated by his business, and the circuit court granted his motion. On appeal, defendant argued that § 941.23 was unconstitutional as applied to him because it violated his right, under Wis. Const. art. I, § 25, to bear arms. In reversing the judgment, the court disagreed, finding that defendant's interest in exercising his right to keep and bear arms in his vehicle for purposes of security did not substantially outweigh the State's interest in enforcing Wis. Stat. § 941.23 (2003-04). The court concluded that the statute was a reasonable exercise of the State's inherent police power in light of its interest in protecting public safety. The court distinguished defendant's case from those involving concealed weapons kept in homes or private businesses, noting, among other things, the danger presented by the transportation of concealed weapons and the increased threat to law enforcement officers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order dismissing the complaint and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

State v. Shomberg


Case No. 2004AP630-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 9; 288 Wis. 2d 1; 709 N.W.2d 370; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 8


September 30, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
January 31, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Shomberg, 2006 WI 108, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 579 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. (L.C. No. 2002CF846). Court: Circuit. County: Dane. Judge: Patrick J. Fiedler. Reported at: 278 Wis. 2d 813, 691 N.W.2d 927, 2005 WI App 21 (Ct. App. 2004-Unpublished).
State v. Shomberg, 2005 WI App 21, 278 Wis. 2d 813, 691 N.W.2d 927, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1062 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the judgment of the circuit court convicting defendant of second-degree sexual assault, false imprisonment, and two counts of bail jumping, all as a habitual offender pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 940.225(2)(a), 940.30, and 946.49(1)(b) (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: An assailant dragged the victim into an alleyway and began sexually assaulting her. A security guard heard her screams, came upon them and the assailant ran. Both the security guard and the victim identified defendant in a lineup. The court affirmed, and concluded that it was not an erroneous exercise of discretion for the circuit court to deny defendant's motion to admit expert testimony regarding an eyewitness's ability to identify a stranger because the trial court found that the expert would not assist the trier. Also, any error would have been harmless because there was other sufficient evidence support the verdict. The trial court's decision did not deprive defendant of his constitutional right to present a defense. Defendant failed to establish that the expert eyewitness testimony was necessary to his case. Further, the trial court heard all the relevant details of the charged offense from the perspective of the accused, and the exclusion of expert testimony did not preclude him from introducing any factual evidence. Also, the evidence in the record was insufficient to establish that defendant offered to take a polygraph examination, as opposed to agreeing to take one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Fazio v. Dep't of Emple. Trust Funds


No. 2004AP64


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 7; 287 Wis. 2d 106; 708 N.W.2d 326; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 6


November 16, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
January 26, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: PATRICK J. FIEDLER. (L.C. No. 2001CV94).
Fazio v. Dep't of Emple. Trust Funds, 280 Wis. 2d 837, 696 N.W.2d 563, 2005 WI App 87, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 262 (2005).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beneficiary filed suit against defendant Wisconsin Department of Employee Trust Funds (Department), seeking interest on a death benefit. The matter was certified as a class action and the beneficiary was designated class representative. The circuit court granted the beneficiary's motion for summary judgment. The Court of Appeals, Wisconsin, reversed the order of the circuit court, and the beneficiary's petition for review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The beneficiary was the widow of a university professor. The professor was a Wisconsin Retirement System (WRS) participant. The professor died on January 2, 1999, and the beneficiary did not file for the death benefits until November 2000. On December 1, 2000, a $ 507,395 death benefit was paid to the beneficiary, which was calculated under Wis. Stat. § 40.73(1)(c) (2003-2004) based on the amount in the professor's account as of January 3, 1999, one day after his death, as provided for by Wis. Stat. § 40.73(1)(c). Between January 3, 1999 and December 1, 2000, the death benefit was held in the fixed retirement investment trust account, and although interest was earned on the funds in the account, the Department paid no interest on the death benefit when it was paid to the beneficiary on December 1, 2000. The reviewing court ruled that it agreed with the court of appeals that no unconstitutional taking occurred because the beneficiary did not acquire a property interest in a single cash sum death benefit under Wis. Stat. § 40.73(1)(c) until the beneficiary applied for a death benefit as required by Wis. Stat. § 40.71(3).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

State v. Beyer (In re Commitment of Beyer)


No. 2004AP1208


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI 2; 287 Wis. 2d 1; 707 N.W.2d 509; 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 2


October 11, 2005, Oral Argument  
January 10, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Motion denied by Beyer v. Watters, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 13243 (W.D. Wis., Feb. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Green County, Daniel L. LaRocque, Reserve Judge. (L.C. No. 1998CV137). Court: Circuit. County: Green. Judge: Daniel L. LaRocque.
State v. Beyer (In re Beyer), 2001 WI App 167, 247 Wis. 2d 13, 633 N.W.2d 627, 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 593 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Green County (Wisconsin) denied appellant committee's pro se motion for release from commitment as a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals certified the case to the supreme court pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.61 (2003-04). The supreme court accepted the certification.


OVERVIEW: After careful consideration of Wis. Stat. §§ 980.07(1) and 980.09(2)(a) and the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, the supreme court held that due process required that a Wis. Stat. ch. 980 committee be granted a probable cause hearing within a meaningful time period after the Wisconsin Department of Health and Family Services provided a copy of the annual periodic examination report to the circuit court pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.07(2). The supreme court held that the delay in holding the probable cause hearing in the committee's case was unreasonably long and violated his due process right to periodic judicial review of his Wis. Stat. ch. 980 civil commitment within a meaningful time period. Nevertheless, the supreme court disagreed with the committee's contention that he had to be released from commitment for the due process violation because he remained a sexually violent person, and release of a person who continued to be sexually violent under Wis. Stat. § 980.01(7) contravened the purposes of Wis. Stat. ch. 980 and was not required by the due process clause. The appropriate remedy was to move for a writ of mandamus or a supervisory writ.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the circuit court's order.

PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. 270 Wis. 2d 427, 678 N.W.2d 369, 2004 WI App 39. Reported at: 270 Wis. 2d 427, 678 N.W.2d 369, 2004 WI App 39 (Ct. App. 2004 - Published). Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: John J. Di Motto. (L.C. No. 95CF954690).

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a circuit court order denying his motion to enforce a previous circuit court order directing that he be placed on supervised release.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed from a decision affirming an order denying his motion to enforce a previous court order directing that he be placed on supervised release. The court affirmed however, stating that the November 2000 order granting the State's motion for reconsideration and finding that the inmate was not appropriate for supervised release, was a valid, final, appealable order, and therefore, he was not entitled to outright release from his Wis. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Haferman v. St. Clare Healthcare Found., Inc.


Case No.: 2003AP1307


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 171; 286 Wis. 2d 621; 707 N.W.2d 853; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 958


September 28, 2005, Oral Argument  
December 30, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Sauk. JUDGE: Daniel George. 2004 WI App 206 Reported at: 277 Wis. 2d 156, 689 N.W.2d 636, 2004 WI App 206 (Ct. App. 2004-Published). (L.C. No. 2002CV717).
Haferman v. St. Clare Healthcare Found., Inc., 277 Wis. 2d 156, 689 N.W.2d 636, 2004 WI App 206, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 719 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin reversed a circuit court order that allowed a medical malpractice action filed by petitioners, a minor and his parents, to proceed as timely filed. The court of appeals concluded that, even though the minor was a developmentally disabled child, the general three-year statute of limitations for medical malpractice actions, Wis. Stat. § 893.55 (2003-04), applied to bar the action. Petitioners sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals determined that other statutes of limitations applicable to children did not, by their plain language, apply to the minor's medical malpractice action. On review, the issue the court had to decide was what statute of limitations applied to a claim against a health care provider alleging injury to a developmentally disabled child. This issue required the court to interpret and apply Wis. Stat. §§ 893.16, 893.56, and 893.55 (2003-04). The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals, concluding that the legislature had not provided an applicable statute of limitations for a claim against a health care provider alleging injury to a developmentally disabled child. Therefore, the court held that the minor's action was not time-barred. The court stated that this determination was the only determination the court was able to reach without either rewriting the statutes or working an absurd and illogical result. The court noted, however, that even in the absence of a statute of limitations, the common law doctrine of laches may, in appropriate cases, be a bar to such claims.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was reversed, and the cause was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

159 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Shaw v. Leatherberry


No. 2003AP2316


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 163; 286 Wis. 2d 380; 706 N.W.2d 299; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 949


October 7, 2005, Oral Argument  
December 6, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Gerald C. Nichol, Judge. Court: Circuit. County: Dane. Judge: Gerald C. Nichol. (L.C. No. 1998CV2857).
Shaw v. Leatherberry, 2005 WI 60, 281 Wis. 2d 117, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 381 (2005).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an arrestee, sued defendants, three deputies, asserting that they subjected her to an illegal strip search, that they tortiously assaulted her, and that they subjected her to excessive force. On summary judgment, the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, dismissed the first two claims. Later, a jury found in favor of each defendant on the question of excessive force pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Plaintiff sought review.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, plaintiff asserted that the trial court erred by imposing a middle burden of proof, clear and convincing evidence, on the liability questions put to the jury in the special verdict. The Wisconsin Supreme Court noted that the issue of what burden of proof was appropriate in a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action alleging excessive force in state court was a matter of first impression. The supreme court noted that in a typical civil suit for money damages, plaintiffs had to prove their case by a preponderance of the evidence. In excessive force cases arising under § 1983, several federal jurisdictions had approved the preponderance of the evidence standard. Thus, the issue was what burden of proof to apply in state court. The Supremacy Clause imposed on state courts a constitutional duty to proceed in such manner that all the substantial rights of the parties under controlling federal law were protected. The supreme court held that the Supremacy Clause required Wisconsin courts to apply the lowest burden of proof, preponderance of the evidence, in civil rights actions under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleging excessive use of force by police personnel.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed, and the cause was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the supreme court's opinion.

Brown County v. Shannon R. (In re Daniel R.S.)


No. 2004AP1305 & 2004AP1306


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 160; 286 Wis. 2d 278; 706 N.W.2d 269; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 946


September 8, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
November 30, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 03TP34, 03TP72). Reported at: 2005 WI App 1, 277 Wis. 2d 876, 690 N.W.2d 886 (2004-Unpublished). Court: Circuit. County: Brown. Judge: John D. McKay.
Brown County v. Shannon R. (In re Daniel R.S.), 277 Wis. 2d 876, 690 N.W.2d 886, 2005 WI App 1, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 877 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that affirmed the order of the circuit court terminating her parental rights to her children pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2)(a)3 (2003-2004), on the ground that the mother had not and would not meet the conditions required for the return of her children within the 12-month period following the hearing.


OVERVIEW: The mother challenged the sufficiency of the evidence and claimed the trial court erred in excluding her expert's opinion testimony. The court held that the exclusion of the expert's testimony denied the mother her due process rights because the expert was qualified under Wis. Stat. § 907.02; the expert's testimony went to the central issue of whether the mother's parental rights should be terminated under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2)(a)3 on the ground that she was unable to meet the conditions required for the return of her children; and the mother was unable to present other testimony in her defense. The court noted held that in view of its decision that the trial court erred in excluding the testimony, it did not need to address the mother's claims of insufficient evidence or that the trial court lost competency to hear the termination by failing to meet the time limits imposed by Wis. Stat. § 48.422. The court rejected the mother's claims that the special verdict questions in the termination of parental rights proceedings were functionally equivalent to the grounds under the Indian Child Welfare Act (ICWA), 25 U.S.C.S. §§ 1901-1963, and required a higher burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals that affirmed the termination of the mother's parental rights and remanded the case for further consistent proceedings.

Marder v. Bd. of Regents of the Univ. of Wis. Sys.


No. 2003AP2755


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 159; 286 Wis. 2d 252; 706 N.W.2d 110; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 945; 23 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1283


September 27, 2005, Oral Argument  
November 29, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Marder v. Bd. of Regents, 2006 WI 108, 292 Wis. 2d 416, 718 N.W.2d 728, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 578 (2006)
Appeal after remand at Marder v. Bd. of Regents of the Univ. of Wis. Sys., 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 286 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 12, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. 276 Wis. 2d 186, 687 N.W.2d 832, 2004 WI App 177, Reported at: 276 Wis. 2d 186, 687 N.W.2d 832, 2004 WI App 177 (Ct. App. 2004-Published). Court: Circuit. County: Douglas. Judge: Robert E. Eaton. (L.C. No. 2001CV222).
Marder v. Bd. of Regents, 2004 WI App 177, 276 Wis. 2d 186, 687 N.W.2d 832, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 650 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former tenured faculty member of a state university petitioned for review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed an order of the circuit court reversing a decision of defendant state university board of regents to terminate plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: The statement of charges leading to plaintiff's dismissal included, among others, sexual misconduct with students, harassing behavior toward colleagues, and irregularities in the student newspaper accounts when plaintiff was the custodian. The court held that the legislature did not intend the contested case provisions of Wis. Stat. ch. 227 to apply to procedures in Wis. Admin. Code § UWS 4. The board promulgated through its rule-making power a complete procedure to be employed before a tenured faculty member could be terminated. Therefore, the provisions of Wis. Stat. § 36.13(5) and Wis. Admin. Code § UWS 4, which were expressly authorized by law, set out the pre-termination procedures to which plaintiff was due. In determining whether plaintiff showed that three alleged ex parte communications created an impermissibly high probability of actual bias, the court found that communication between the chancellor and a regent were not impermissible. However, the court did not have enough information about what occurred in a closed meeting under § UWS 4.08(2) to determine whether plaintiff's due process rights were violated, so remand was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals.

 

162 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Dane County v. McGrew


No. 2003AP1794


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 130; 285 Wis. 2d 519; 699 N.W.2d 890; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 404


March 10, 2005, Oral Argument  
July 19, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 02 TR 8507). Reported at: 272 Wis. 2d 856, 679 N.W.2d 927, 2004 WI App 88 (Ct. App. 2004-Unpublished). Court: Circuit. County: Dane. Judge: C. William Foust.
Dane County v. McGrew, 272 Wis. 2d 856, 679 N.W.2d 927, 2004 WI App 88, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 258 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the circuit court's decision in a civil forfeiture case. The question was whether Wis. Stat. § 345.43 (2001-02), which mandated six-person juries in civil forfeiture trials, was unconstitutional in respondent county's prosecution of appellant for speeding pursuant to Dane County, Wis., Ordinance § 69.01 and Wis. Stat. § 346.57(4)(h) (2001-02).


OVERVIEW: Appellant received a citation for exceeding the speed limit by 24 MPH in violation of Dane County, Wis., Ordinance § 69.01. Respondent county amended the citation to 25 MPH, which subjected appellant to a potential suspension of his license. The court held that causes of action under traffic laws that were in effect at the time the Wisconsin Constitution took effect were not akin to the current speeding violation. Further, although "speeding" was not a cause of action recognized at common law in 1848, other traffic violations such as driving outside one's lane could not be so easily distinguished, and the court held that it made little sense to scrutinize whether each individual traffic violation was recognized at common law so as to determine whether a violator was entitled to a six- or 12-person jury. Thus appellant did not satisfy the heavy burden of showing that Wis. Stat. § 345.43 was unconstitutional. Because he cannot show that the cause of action for a speeding violation existed at the time the Wisconsin Constitution was enacted, he has no constitutional right to a trial by a jury of 12.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals.

 

163 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Thomas v. Mallett


No. 2003AP1528


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 129; 285 Wis. 2d 236; 701 N.W.2d 523; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 397


February 1, 2005, Oral Argument  
July 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Thomas v. Mallett, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1021 (Wis. Ct. App., Dec. 16, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reported at: 275 Wis. 2d 377, 685 N.W.2d 791, 2004 WI App 131 (Ct. App. 2004-Published). Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: Timothy G. Dugan. (L.C. No. 99 CV 6411).
Thomas v. Mallett, 2004 WI App 131, 275 Wis. 2d 377, 685 N.W.2d 791, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 492 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor, by his guardian ad litem, sought review of a decision of the court of appeals (Wisconsin) that declined to extend the risk-contribution announced in Collins in the minor's action against defendant pigment manufacturers for injuries he received from lead paint in his prior residences.


OVERVIEW: The minor had cognitive deficits as a result of lead poisoning. The court of appeals concluded that because the minor had a remedy against his landlords, there was no reason to extend the risk-contribution theory. The minor was unable to identify the precise producer of the white lead carbonate pigment he ingested due to the generic nature of the pigment. The court reversed in part and extended the Collins' risk-contribution theory to white lead carbonate claims. Wis. Const. art. I, § 9 applied not only when a plaintiff was without a remedy; rather, it allowed a court to fashion an adequate remedy when one did not exist. There was no dispute that the minor was an innocent plaintiff who would be forced to bear a significant cost of his injuries if not allowed to sue the possibly negligent manufacturers, and it was clear that the manufacturers contributed to the risk of injury to the minor. Also, the factual circumstances of physical interchangeability that were present were sufficiently similar to remain within Collins' confines in that white lead carbonates were produced utilizing virtually identical chemical formulas such that all white lead carbonates were identically defective.


OUTCOME: The court reversed as to the negligence claims against the manufacturers and affirmed as to the dismissal of the civil conspiracy and enterprise liability claims. The court also held that the manufacturers' constitutional challenges to the conclusion were not ripe.

Lagerstrom v. Myrtle Werth Hospital-Mayo Health Sys.


Case No. 2003AP2027


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 124; 285 Wis. 2d 1; 700 N.W.2d 201; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 398


December 14, 2004, Submitted on Oral Briefs  
July 14, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Dunn County. William C. Stewart, Jr., Judge. Reversed and Remanded.
Lagerstrom v. Myrtle Werth Hosp.-Mayo Health Sys., 2004 WI 114, 273 Wis. 2d 659, 684 N.W.2d 140, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 650 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin) that entered judgment on the jury award in a medical malpractice case against defendants health care providers.


OVERVIEW: The estate argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by admitting evidence of collateral source payments for the purpose of determining the reasonable value of the medical services but refusing to admit evidence of the estate's potential obligation to reimburse Medicare. The supreme court agreed. The text of Wis. Stat. § 893.55(7) explicitly allowed evidence of collateral source payments to be introduced in medical malpractice actions. However, if evidence of collateral source payments from sources including Medicare, other state or federal government programs, medical insurance or write-offs, and discounted or free medical services was presented to the fact-finder, then the parties must be allowed to furnish the jury with evidence of any obligations of subrogation or reimbursement. The trial court must instruct the fact-finder that it must not reduce the reasonable value of medical services on the basis of the collateral source payments.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

165 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dubose


No. 2003AP1690-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 126; 285 Wis. 2d 143; 699 N.W.2d 582; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 400


March 2, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
July 14, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Brown. Judge: Sue E. Bischel. Reported at: 272 Wis. 2d 856, 679 N.W.2d 927, 2004 WI App 88 (Ct. App. 2004-Unpublished). (L.C. No. 02 CF 0028).
State v. Dubose, 272 Wis. 2d 856, 679 N.W.2d 927, 2004 WI App 88, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 190 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress because the out-of-court identification was unnecessarily suggestive. The supreme court agreed. There existed sufficient facts at the time of defendant's arrest to establish probable cause for his arrest. It was not necessary for the police to conduct the showups. The officers handcuffed defendant and placed him in the back seat of a squad car. By placing defendant in a squad car, the police implicitly suggested that they believed that he was the offender. Police told the witness that they might have caught "one of the guys" who had robbed him. Such a comment was suggestive and greatly increased the chance of misidentification. After the first showup was conducted and defendant was positively identified, the police still conducted two more identification procedures, another showup and a photo of defendant, at the police station. Those subsequent identification procedures were unnecessarily suggestive. Defendant had already been arrested and positively identified.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Ferdon v. Wis. Patients Comp. Fund


No. 2003AP988


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 125; 284 Wis. 2d 573; 701 N.W.2d 440; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 401


April 26, 2005, Oral Argument  
July 14, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Brown. Judge: Peter Naze. (L.C. No. 2001CV1897).
Ferdon v. Wis. Patients Comp. Fund, 2005 WI 1, 277 Wis. 2d 150, 691 N.W.2d 353, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 1039 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury verdict in favor of appellant individual, respondent Wisconsin Patients Compensation Fund moved to have the noneconomic damages reduced pursuant to the limitation established in Wis. Stat. §§ 655.017 and 893.55(4)(d) (2001-02). The trial court granted the motion, and the Court of Appeals of Wisconsin affirmed. The individual sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The individual sustained permanent injuries as an infant due to a doctor's malpractice. The jury awarded the individual $ 700,000 in noneconomic damages for injuries caused by medical malpractice and $ 403,000 for future medical expenses based on his life expectancy of 69 years. The Fund moved to have the noneconomic damages reduced pursuant to the $350,000 limitation established in §§ 655.017 and 893.55(4)(d). The individual claimed that §§ 655.017 and 893.55(4)(d) were unconstitutional in that, inter alia, they violated the equal protection guarantees of Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. The state supreme court agreed with the individual and held that §§ 655.017 and 893.55(4)(d) were unconstitutional. The state supreme court applied a rational basis level of scrutiny and found that the legislature's goals of wanting to adequately compensate malpractice victims, limit malpractice premiums, and keep the Fund's assessment level at a low rate were not rationally related to the cap as the cap punished the most severely injured victims and the facts did not support the assumption that a cap on noneconomic damages achieved any of the other stated goals.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was reversed, and the cause was remanded to the trial court to determine (1) if the Fund was liable for payment of the amount of the jury award in excess of the statutory limitation and (2) the constitutionality of other statutes and rules that required awards in excess of $100,000 to be deposited in an account over which the Fund had control.

State v. Knapp


No. 2000AP2590-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 127; 285 Wis. 2d 86; 700 N.W.2d 899; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 395


February 16, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
July 14, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Knapp, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 758 (Wis. Ct. App., Oct. 1, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Jefferson County Circuit Court, Randy R. Koschnick, Judge. Court: Circuit. County: Jefferson. Judge: Randy R. Koschnick. (L.C. No. 99CF363).
Wisconsin v. Knapp, 542 U.S. 952, 124 S. Ct. 2932, 159 L. Ed. 2d 835, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 4766 (2004)
State v. Knapp, 2003 WI 121, 265 Wis. 2d 278, 666 N.W.2d 881, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 621 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's case was on remand from the United States Supreme Court, which vacated the state supreme court's conclusion that physical evidence obtained as the direct result of a Miranda violation was inadmissible when the violation was an intentional attempt to prevent the suspect from exercising Fifth Amendment rights. The state circuit court had denied defendant's motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to suppress, which was denied. The case was currently on remand from the United States Supreme Court, which vacated its prior decision concluding that physical evidence obtained as the direct result of a Miranda violation was inadmissible when the violation was an intentional attempt to prevent the suspect from exercising his or her Fifth Amendment rights. The state supreme court reversed the circuit court's determination, holding that the fruit of the poisonous tree doctrine applied pursuant to Wis. Const. art. I, § 8. Where physical evidence was obtained as the direct result of an intentional Miranda violation, the state supreme court concluded that the Wisconsin constitution required that the evidence be suppressed. The state supreme court refused to allow those entrusted to enforce the law to intentionally subvert a suspect's constitutional rights. As it was undisputed that the physical evidence was obtained as a direct result of an intentional violation of Miranda, it was inadmissible. Further, the state supreme court retained the right to interpret its constitution to provide greater protections than its federal counterpart.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the circuit court's order and remanded for further proceedings.

Olstad v. Microsoft Corp.


2003AP1086


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 121; 284 Wis. 2d 224; 700 N.W.2d 139; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 393; 2005-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P74,918


September 22, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
July 13, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Costs and fees proceeding at, Remanded by Bettendorf v. Microsoft Corp., 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 986 (Wis. Ct. App., Dec. 22, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Jeffrey Kremers, Judge. (L.C. No. 00 CV 3042).
Olstad v. Microsoft Corp., 2004 WI 50, 271 Wis. 2d 113, 679 N.W.2d 548, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 404 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual, suing for himself and as class representative, sued defendant software company, alleging it employed monopolistic practices prohibited by Wis. Stat. § 133.03 (2001-02). The trial court granted the company's motion for summary judgment. Plaintiff appealed. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals certified the following issue: Did § 133.03 apply to interstate commerce affecting Wisconsin commerce?


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that the company controlled up to 95 percent of the market for personal computer operating systems that were compatible with a commonly-used microprocessor, and that it engaged in various forms of anticompetitive conduct to maintain its monopoly. The company noted that it was a foreign corporation and that most of the conduct complained of occurred outside Wisconsin and affected interstate commerce. The trial court dismissed the suit because it found that Wis. Stat. ch. 133 applied only to intrastate commerce. The high court disagreed. Reviewing the statutory history, it held that Wis. Stat. ch. 133 could reach interstate commerce if (1) actionable conduct occurred within Wisconsin, even if its effects were felt primarily elsewhere; or (2) the conduct "substantially affected" Wisconsinites and had impacts in Wisconsin, even if the illegal activity resulting in those impacts occurred predominantly or exclusively outside Wisconsin. The high court withdrew the language from Conley Publ'g Group v. Journal Communications, 2003 WI 119, 265 Wis. 2d 128, 665 N.W.2d 879, that the scope of Wis. Stat. ch. 133 was limited to intrastate transactions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded.

State v. Denis L.R.


Case No.: 2003AP384-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 110; 283 Wis. 2d 358; 699 N.W.2d 154; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 349


January 5, 2005, Oral Argument  
July 8, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.Appeals. 270 Wis. 2d 663, 678 N.W.2d 326, 2004 WI App 51 Reported at: 270 Wis. 2d 663, 678 N.W.2d 326, 2004 WI App 51 (Ct. App. 2004-Published). (L.C. No. 02CF235). Court: Circuit. County: Sheboygan. Judge: Gary Langhoff.
State v. Denis L.R., 270 Wis. 2d 663, 678 N.W.2d 326, 2004 WI App 51, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 102 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother, an intervenor in defendant's criminal case, sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the circuit court's order concluding that the mother waived the therapist-patient privilege of her three-year-old daughter.


OVERVIEW: The child received counseling and told her therapist that her grandfather sexually assaulted her. The clinical director reported the sexual assault to the authorities. The mother overheard the child tell the therapist that the grandfather did not sexually assault her; the mother relayed that information to her grandmother. The circuit court conducted an in-camera review of the counseling records to look for any information that either inculpated or exculpated the grandfather and found nothing. At issue in the case was whether the circuit court could conduct an in camera interview of the therapist. The appellate court concluded that the mother waived the privilege, but the supreme court affirmed on other grounds pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 48.981 and 905.04 (2001-02). It concluded that there was no privilege because an examination of the child created a reasonable ground for an opinion that she was abused and that her abuse was other than accidentally caused or inflicted by another. Because there was no privilege with respect to any communications she made for purposes of mental health treatment related to the sexual abuse, there was no need for an in camera review of the therapist.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision on other grounds.

Grant County Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. Unified Bd. of Grant & Ia. Counties (In re Jane E. P.)


No. 2003AP634


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 106; 283 Wis. 2d 258; 700 N.W.2d 863; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 343


February 4, 2005, Oral Argument  
July 7, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 02 GN 000029). 275 Wis. 2d 680, 687 N.W.2d 72, 2004 WI App 153. Reported at: 275 Wis. 2d 680, 687 N.W.2d 72, 2004 WI App 153. (Ct. App. 2004-Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Grant. JUDGE: Robert P. VanDeHey.
Grant County Dep't of Social Servs. v. Unified Bd. of Grant & Iowa Counties (In re E.P.), 275 Wis. 2d 680, 687 N.W.2d 72, 2004 WI App 153, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 547 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner board of two counties sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversing a circuit court order that dismissed a petition for guardianship filed by respondent county department of social services.


OVERVIEW: An incompetent woman (ward) lived in a nursing home in an Illinois county, and her sister was her guardian. Because many of the ward's relatives wanted her moved to Wisconsin, the department petitioned for protective placement at a private nursing home in Wisconsin and nominated the sister to remain as her guardian. The circuit court dismissed the petition based upon the ward's non-residency, and the court of appeals determined that Wis. Stat. § 55.06(3)(c), as applied to the ward, violated her constitutional right to interstate travel. In applying national probate court standards, the court held that the principles of comity were to be applied here. The court therefore remanded and held that the department should petition the Illinois county court where the ward resided for transfer of the guardianship and likewise petition the trial court in the department's county for the receipt and acceptance of the ward's guardianship. If these steps were completed, the court in circuit court would be able to place the ward at the private Wisconsin nursing home without hearing a new petition for protective placement. This would avoid the residency requirement of § 55.06(3)(c).


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the court of appeals and remanded.

State v. Jerrell C.J. (In re Jerrell C.J.)


No. 2002AP3423


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 105; 283 Wis. 2d 145; 699 N.W.2d 110; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 344


November 9, 2004, Oral Argument  
July 7, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Francis T. Wasielewski. (L.C. No. 01 JV 001168).
State v. Jerrell C.J. (In re Jerrell C.J.), 269 Wis. 2d 442, 674 N.W.2d 607, 2004 WI App 9, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1215 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Juvenile defendant was adjudged delinquent for the commission of armed robbery, party to a crime. His postdisposition motion was denied. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his written confession to the police was involuntary under the totality of the circumstances. The supreme court agreed. Defendant's young age of 14 was a strong factor weighing against the voluntariness of his confession. His limited education and low average intelligence were additional reasons for why he was susceptible to police pressure. Defendant had been arrested twice for misdemeanor offenses prior to his interrogation for the armed robbery. In both instances, he answered police questions, admitted to involvement, and was allowed to go home. The police specifically denied defendant's requests to call his parents. Not only did the detectives refuse to believe defendant's repeated denials of guilt, but they also joined in urging him to tell a different "truth," sometimes using a "strong voice" that "frightened" him. Therefore, the written confession was involuntary under the totality of the circumstances. In addition, the supreme court exercised its supervisory power to require that all custodial interrogation of juveniles be electronically recorded where feasible, and without exception when questioning occurred at a place of detention.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

State v. Bush (In re Bush)


No. 2003AP2306


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 103; 283 Wis. 2d 90; 699 N.W.2d 80; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 341


April 29, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
July 6, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bush v. Wis., 126 S. Ct. 631, 163 L. Ed. 2d 507, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 8249 (U.S., Nov. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reported at: 276 Wis. 2d 806, 688 N.W.2d 752, 2004 WI App 193 (Ct. App. 2004-Published). Source of Appeal: Court: Circuit. County: Eau Claire. (L.C. No. 97CI1). Judge: William M. Gabler.
State v. Bush (In re Bush), 276 Wis. 2d 806, 688 N.W.2d 752, 2004 WI App 193, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 770 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that he was procedurally barred from bringing a claim challenging the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (2001-02) (ch. 980). Petitioner further asked the court to conclude that ch. 980 was facially unconstitutional on substantive due process grounds.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had been convicted of numerous sex-related offenses, and after having his parole revoked he was found sexually violent and was committed under ch. 980. Petitioner sought release under Wis. Stat. § 980.09(2) (2001-02), which was denied. The court concluded that because petitioner facially challenged the constitutionality of ch. 980, his challenge went to the subject matter jurisdiction of the court, and thus jurisdiction could not be waived. The court held that the evidence supported a determination that petitioner remained dangerous. Although he was granted parole, it was not a conclusive determination of his dangerousness under ch. 980. Also, due process did not require adoption of a bright-line rule that petitioner had committed a recent overt act while on parole. The question was simply whether it was substantially probable that the person would engage in acts of sexual violence. The fact that petitioner was incarcerated for attempted sexual assault when the petition was filed, while not sufficient evidence for commitment under Wis. Stat. § 980.05(4) (2001-02), was a proper component of the evaluation of his current dangerousness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals.

Kohn v. Darlington Cmty. Sch.


No. 2003AP1067


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 99; 283 Wis. 2d 1; 698 N.W.2d 794; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 336


April 29, 2005, Oral Argument  
July 1, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reported at: 276 Wis. 2d 309, 686 N.W.2d 455, 2004 WI App 167 (Ct. App. 2004--Unpublished). Court: Circuit. County: Lafayette. Judge: Daniel L. LaRocque. (L.C. No. 01 CV 48).
Kohn v. Darlington Cmty. Schs., 276 Wis. 2d 309, 686 N.W.2d 455, 2004 WI App 167, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 545 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bleacher manufacturer appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversing the circuit court's summary judgment for the manufacturer under Wis. Stat. § 893.89 in a personal injury action alleging that school bleachers were in a dangerously defective condition when they left the control of the manufacturer and that the product caused harm to respondents, a child who fell through them, and her family.


OVERVIEW: The school purchased the bleachers from the manufacturer in 1969. The issues were whether the bleachers constituted an improvement to real property for purposes of § 893.89 and whether § 893.89 violated the right to remedy provision of Wis. Const. art. I, § 9 or equal protection rights. The court held that the bleachers constituted a permanent addition to the school in that, while they could be disassembled and moved, it would require a significant amount of time and effort. Under Wis. Stat. § 893.89(2), the manufacturer's liability exposure ended 10 years after the substantial completion to the improvement of real property, and thus § 893.89 did not violate Wis. Const. art. I, § 9 because art. I, § 9 guaranteed a remedy only for existing rights. Finally, the court concluded that Wis. Stat § 893.89 did not violate the guarantee of equal protection in the federal and state constitutions because it was not patently arbitrary or bore a rational relationship to a legitimate governmental interest because the classifications within § 893.89 rationally served the legitimate purpose of limiting the long-term liability of those involved in the improvement of real property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals.

 

174 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anson


No. 2003AP1444-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 96; 282 Wis. 2d 629; 698 N.W.2d 776; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 331


April 28, 2005, Oral Argument  
June 29, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 00 CF 306). 275 Wis. 2d 832, 686 N.W.2d 712, 2004 WI App 155. Reported at: 275 Wis. 2d 832, 686 N.W.2d 712, 2004 WI App 155 (Ct. App. 2004-Published). Court: Circuit. County: Walworth. Judge: James L. Carlson.
State v. Anson, 275 Wis. 2d 832, 686 N.W.2d 712, 2004 WI App 155, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 576 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the circuit court, of second-degree sexual assault of a child. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals reversed the convictions, and it remanded the matter for a new trial. The State sought review.


OVERVIEW: Authorities in California contacted defendant in an attempt to obtain a statement. Defendant was told that he was not under arrest, yet he was placed in a police vehicle, where he made a statement. At issue was whether the unlawfully obtained statement induced defendant to take the stand to reduce the impact of the statement. The supreme court held that the State's underlying constitutional violation of defendant's right to counsel and the circuit court's error in not suppressing the tape-recorded statement was not harmless. The State had not proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant did not take the stand in order to overcome the impact of the illegally obtained and improperly introduced statement. Even if defendant would have taken the stand in the absence of the illegally obtained confession, the State did not meet its burden in dispelling the natural inference that no testimonial admission so damaging would have been made if the prosecutor had not already spread defendant's confession before the jury. The State failed to show that defendant's testimony was obtained by means sufficiently distinguishable from the underlying illegality to be purged of the primary taint.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the appellate court's decision, which remanded the matter for a new trial.

Sukala v. Heritage Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 2003AP173


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 83; 282 Wis. 2d 46; 698 N.W.2d 610; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 320


February 2, 2005, Oral Argument  
June 22, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. 275 Wis. 2d 469, 685 N.W.2d 809, 2004 WI App 128 Reported at: 275 Wis. 2d 469, 685 N.W.2d 809, 2004 WI App 128 (Ct. App. 2004 - Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Wood JUDGE: Frederic Fleishauer. (L.C. No. 1997CV48).
Sukala v. Heritage Mut. Ins. Co., 275 Wis. 2d 469, 685 N.W.2d 809, 2004 WI App 128, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 506 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insureds, who sought additional recovery from two underinsured motorist provisions, moved for relief from all judgments, orders, releases, and stipulations pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 806.07(1)(h) (2001-2002). The circuit court denied the motion. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals reversed the circuit court's order. Defendant insurers filed petitions for review.


OVERVIEW: The insurers argued that the circuit court properly exercised its discretion in denying the insureds' § 806.07(1)(h) motion. The instant court agreed, holding that the circuit court correctly determined that there had been no change in the law in regard to the enforceability of reducing clauses at issue in this case. Because a change in the law was the basis for the insureds' motion, the circuit court appropriately exercised its discretion in denying the insureds relief from judgment. In addressing the insureds' motion, the circuit court properly identified the equitable balance it was to apply when deciding a motion under § 806.07(1)(h). When the circuit court weighed its conclusion that the law was unchanged against the finality of judgments, it held that insureds' motion had to be denied. This showed the circuit court used a rational reasoning process based on an application of the correct legal standard to the facts of record and came to a conclusion a reasonable court could make. The appellate court did not review the circuit court's decision under the erroneous exercise of discretion standard, but instead substituted its own judgment for that of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed.

State v. Fonte


No. 2003AP2097-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 77; 281 Wis. 2d 654; 698 N.W.2d 594; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 315


March 10, 2005, Oral Argument  
June 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by, Modified by State v. Fonte, 2005 WI 145, 286 Wis. 2d 77, 704 N.W.2d 912, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 768 (2005)
Reconsideration denied by State v. Fonte, 2005 WI 150, 286 Wis. 2d 104, 705 N.W.2d 664, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 936 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 2001CF306). Court: Circuit. County: Walworth. Judge: Robert J. Kennedy. Reported at: 2004 WI App 186, 276 Wis. 2d 570, 687 N.W.2d 548 (Ct. App. 2004-Unpublished).
State v. Fonte, 276 Wis. 2d 570, 687 N.W.2d 548, 2004 WI App 186, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 639 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that reversed defendant's conviction for homicide by intoxicated operation of a vehicle under Wis. Stat. § 940.09 (2001-02), due to a boating accident resulting in the death of one of his friends. The conviction was reversed based on the conclusion that a jury instruction on chemical tests for intoxication and defendant's prohibited alcohol concentration (PAC) was misleading.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that its jury instruction properly explained the law regarding chemical tests for intoxication under Wis. Stat. § 885.235 (2001-02) and did not deprive defendant of due process. The State had submitted a proposed instruction that allowed the jury to find that defendant had a PAC of 0.1 or higher at the time of his operation of the boat as prima facie evidence that he was under the influence of an intoxicant at that time. The court reversed the court of appeals judgment. The court held that the jury instruction satisfied the requirements of § 885.235(3) because the State presented expert testimony regarding the effect that the delayed drawing of defendant's blood and test results had upon defendant's PAC at the time of the accident. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to show defendant was operating the boat at the time of the accident based on his statements to police that he thought the boat was not in gear. The court rejected defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel and found that the trial court had properly examined the jury to avoid prejudice from pretrial publicity. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 940.09 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals judgment and remanded the case with directions to reinstate defendant's conviction for homicide by intoxicated operation of a vehicle.

State v. Stenklyft


No. 2003AP1533-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 71; 281 Wis. 2d 484; 697 N.W.2d 769; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 187


December 7, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
June 9, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the orders of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Daniel R. Moeser. L.C. No. 00 CF 1806.
State v. Stenklyft, 2004 WI 114, 273 Wis. 2d 659, 684 N.W.2d 140, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 653 (2004).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of causing great bodily harm by operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant under Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(a) (1999-2000). The State appealed orders of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, granting defendant's petition for sentence adjustment under Wis. Stat. § 973.195 (2003-04) and denying the State's motion for reconsideration. The case was before the court on a motion to bypass.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to a total term of imprisonment of seven and one-half years. The circuit court granted defendant's petition for early release over the State's objection. The State appealed, arguing that Wis. Stat. § 973.195 (2003-04) applied only to crimes committed after February 1, 2003--crimes governed by Truth-in-Sentencing-II. The majority of the court, who provided the concurring and dissenting opinions, held that in order to save the constitutionally of § 973.195, "shall" should be interpreted as directory, thereby giving a circuit court discretion to accept or reject an objection from a district attorney on a petition for sentence adjustment under § 973.195. The court declared unconstitutional the lead opinion's interpretation of § 973.195 to grant a district attorney a veto power over a petition for sentence adjustment. The court held that judicial power was compromised when a district attorney was given the unilateral power to end a circuit court's consideration of an inmate's petition for sentence adjustment; a district attorney's exercise of a core judicial function was barred by the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The orders were reversed and the case was remanded to the circuit court to exercise its discretion whether to grant defendant's petition for sentence adjustment, giving full consideration of the factors set forth in the concurring opinion, including the nature of the crime, the character of defendant, the protection of the public positions of the State and the victim, and other relevant factors.

Dane County Dep't of Human Servs. v. P.P. (In re Diana P.)


03-2440, 03-2441, 03-2442, 03-2443, 03-2444, 03-2445 & 03-2446


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 32; 279 Wis. 2d 169; 694 N.W.2d 344; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 142


September 9, 2004, Oral Argument  
March 23, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reported at: 269 Wis. 2d 892, 675 N.W.2d 811, 2004 WI App 37 (Ct. App. 2004-Unpublished). Court: Circuit. County: Dane. Judge: Daniel R. Moeser. (L.C. Nos. 02 TP 107, 02 TP 108, 02 TP 109, 02 TP 110, 02 TP 111, 02 TP 112 & 02 TP 113).
Dane County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Ponn P. (In re Diana P.), 269 Wis. 2d 892, 675 N.W.2d 811, 2004 WI App 37, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 84 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner County Department of Human Services brought a petition to terminate the parental rights of respondent father to seven minor children pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4). The father entered a no contest plea, and the trial court entered an order terminating parental rights. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: In terminating the father's parental rights, the trial court adopted the conclusions of a social worker's report that the children had been subject to extreme physical abuse, sexual abuse, and neglect. The father argued that Wis. Stat. § 48.424(4) was facially unconstitutional because it provided that a finding under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4) was sufficient to prove that a parent was unfit; he claimed that parental rights could therefore be terminated without a finding of unfitness in violation of substantive due process. The supreme court disagreed. The findings that were required for a court to proceed against a parent at each of the steps prior to the final step under § 48.415(4) involved an evaluation of parental fitness, and the cumulative effect of those determinations caused the finding under § 48.415(4) to amount to unfitness. As the father had multiple opportunities to contest the determinations made at each fact-finding stage and chose not to do so, but instead pled no contest to the allegation that § 48.415(4) provided a ground for terminating his parental rights, the record supported the conclusion that he was an unfit parent.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals' judgment was affirmed.

Wischer v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus. Am., Inc.


No. 01-0724, 01-1031 & 01-2486


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 26; 279 Wis. 2d 4; 694 N.W.2d 320; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 137


October 28, 2004, Oral Argument  
March 18, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Wischer v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus., 2005 WI 134, 282 Wis. 2d 724, 700 N.W.2d 276, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 568 (2005)
Reconsideration denied by Wischer v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus., 2005 WI 134, 282 Wis. 2d 724, 700 N.W.2d 276, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 567 (2005)
Reconsideration denied by Wischer v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus., 2005 WI 134, 282 Wis. 2d 724, 700 N.W.2d 276, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 571 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 99 CV 6553). 267 Wis. 2d 638, 673 N.W.2d 303, 2003 WI App 202. Reported at: 267 Wis. 2d 638, 673 N.W.2d 303, 2003 WI App 202 (Ct. App. 2003-Published). Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: Dominic S. Amato.
Wischer v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus. Am., Inc., 267 Wis. 2d 638, 673 N.W.2d 303, 2003 WI App 202, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 908 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals reversed; cause remanded to Court of Appeals for resolution of remaining unresolved issues.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate administrators brought a suit against defendant general contractor claiming that its negligence caused the death of three construction workers in a crane accident. A jury found in favor of the estates and returned, inter alia, a punitive damage award of $ 94 million. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin reversed the judgment on punitive damages based on its interpretation of Wis. Stat. § 895.85(3) (1999-2000). The estates appealed.


OVERVIEW: Three questions of law were presented for review. The supreme court held that the court of appeals had erroneously interpreted § 895.85(3) as requiring intent. Section 895.85(3) required a plaintiff to show that a defendant acted maliciously to the plaintiff or intentionally disregarded the rights of the plaintiff, not that a defendant intended to cause harm or injury to the plaintiff. The evidence was sufficient to have submitted the punitive damages award to the jury which could have believed that the crane collapsed because it was used in high winds, no wind-speed calculations were made, and the crane's load chart limitations were exceeded. Without wind calculations the 45-stories-high crane was lifting a billboard-size load of nearly one million pounds on a windy afternoon. A reasonable jury could have found that the estates had proven by clear and convincing evidence that the contractor had acted in intentional disregard of the rights of the workers, in that it was aware that its conduct was substantially certain to result in their rights being disregarded. The supreme court declined to reach the constitutionality of the amount of the punitive damages award.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals that reversed the judgment of the circuit court awarding punitive damages was reversed and the cause was remanded to the court of appeals for resolution of the remaining unresolved issues.

Schilling v. State Crime Victims Rights Bd.


No. 03-1855


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 17; 278 Wis. 2d 216; 692 N.W.2d 623; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 14


November 9, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
February 23, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Michael N. Nowakowski, Judge.
Schilling v. State Crime Victims Rights Bd., 2004 WI 114, 273 Wis. 2d 659, 684 N.W.2d 140, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 649 (2004).
State v. Marinko, 258 Wis. 2d 983, 654 N.W.2d 95, 2002 WI App 292, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1100 (2002).



DISPOSITION: Circuit court decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Crime Victims Rights Board, ordered a private reprimand under Wis. Stat. § 950.09(2)(a) (1999-2000) against respondent district attorney for violating the complainants' rights under Wis. Const. art. I, § 9m. The attorney sought judicial review of the Board's decision, and the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, reversed the Board's decision. The Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim was murdered and was survived by her two children, her mother and nine siblings. The attorney prosecuted the accused in connection with the victim's death. At the sentencing hearing the attorney played part of the tape of the 911 telephone call that the victim's son had made to the police after discovering his mother dead. The attorney turned off the tape before it had finished playing because he recognized that it was having a dramatic effect on the family members. The Board ordered a private reprimand for violating the complainants' rights to be treated with fairness, dignity, respect and sensitivity in the playing of the 911 tape at the sentencing hearing. The reviewing court held that Wis. Const. art. I, § 9m was a statement of purpose that described the policies to be promoted by the State and did not provide an enforceable, self-executing right. The first sentence of Wis. Const. art. I, § 9m did not provide a self-executing right that the Crime Victims Rights Board was empowered to enforce via private reprimand pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 950.09(2)(a) (1999-2000).


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.
