Barbara B. v. Dorian H. (In re John R. B.)


No. 03-1877


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI 6; 277 Wis. 2d 378; 690 N.W.2d 849; 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 5


November 9, 2004, Argued  
January 20, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. L.C. No. 80 PA 1109. Reported at: 2004 WI App 21, 269 Wis. 2d 543, 674 N.W.2d 681 (Ct. App. 2003-Unpublished).
Barbara B. v. Dorian H. (In re John R. B.), 269 Wis. 2d 543, 674 N.W.2d 681, 2004 WI App 21, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1140 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 2001, respondent mother filed a petition for an order to show cause, alleging that appellant father violated a 1982 child support order. The circuit court ruled against the father, concluding that application of the doctrine of equitable estoppel was inappropriate under Wis. Stat. § 767.32(1r) (2000-2001) and that the statute was constitutional. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals affirmed. The father filed a petition for review.


OVERVIEW: The father argued it violated his right to due process under the state and federal constitutions to retroactively apply Wis. Stat. § 767.32(1m), (1r) (2000-2001), which were amended in 1997, instead of the law that was in place at the time the parties entered into a stipulation that formed the basis of the 1982 child support order. The instant court concluded that retroactive applications of § 767.32(1m), (1r), were rational and did not violate the father's right to due process. Although the total amount the father would have to pay in order to satisfy the child support arrearages, plus interest, was considerable, his private interest in property was weak. The father's obligation to pay child support was explicit in the 1982 support order. The statute provided the father the opportunity to return to court and request a modification of the order. He chose not to do so. Instead, the father waited until he was called into court to pay the arrearages. The instant court, which balanced the public's interest against the father's private interest, weighed the public interest as more substantial.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

DISPOSITION:  Attorney's license to practice law revoked; costs imposed.

OVERVIEW: On review, the attorney challenged the recommendation that his license be revoked. The fees and expenses incurred by the Office of Lawyer Regulation, as itemized in its statement of costs submitted to the supreme court, were reasonable and fully documented. The attorney, as a repeat violator of the supreme court rules, was ordered to pay all of the costs.

183 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Maurin v. Hall


No. 00-0072


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 100; 274 Wis. 2d 28; 682 N.W.2d 866; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 472



July 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Maurin v. Hall, 2004 WI 138, 276 Wis. 2d 32, 689 N.W.2d 59, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 986 (2004)
Reconsideration denied by Maurin v. Hall, 2004 WI 129, 276 Wis. 2d 18, 688 N.W.2d 655, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 822 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON CERTIFICATION FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. APPEAL from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Washington County, Lawrence F. Waddick, Judge. L.C. No. 98 CV 229.
Maurin v. Hall, 2004 WI 1, 268 Wis. 2d 136, 673 N.W.2d 694, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 1178 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice and wrongful death suit arising from the death of a 5-year-old child, a jury awarded $ 2,500,000 for loss of society and companionship to plaintiff parents. The circuit court made a postjudgment ruling that the wrongful death cap on noneconomic damages was unconstitutional. Defendant doctor appealed, and the appeals court, Wisconsin, certified questions as to the interplay and constitutionality of relevant caps.


OVERVIEW: The court first addressed what limits applied to noneconomic damages in derivative wrongful death claims resulting from medical malpractice and found that such claims were covered by the medical malpractice limitations outlined in Wis. Stat. § 893.55(4) (1995-96). The amount of the cap was determined by whether the patient survived. When the patient survived, the cap was in Wis. Stat. § 893.55(4)(d). When the patient died, the cap was contained in Wis. Stat. § 895.04(4), which applied in lieu of, not in addition to, the medical malpractice cap. For claims arising between May 25, 1995, and April 27, 1998, two parents were entitled to separate awards of $ 150,000, resulting in a $ 300,000 cap. The limit on wrongful death noneconomic damages arising out of medical malpractice was constitutional. By limiting damages, the legislature did not trample on the jury's role in assessing damages or the court's powers of remittitur and additur. The cap was rationally related to the legitimate legislative objective of assuaging the fear that passions would run high, resulting in huge damage awards. Adjustments to the cap did not lead inexorably to the conclusion that changes were arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the cause for action consistent with the decision.

State v. Faust


No. 03-0952-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 99; 274 Wis. 2d 183; 682 N.W.2d 371; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 474


April 6, 2004, Oral Argument  
July 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Faust v. Wis., 543 U.S. 1089, 160 L. Ed. 2d 898, 125 S. Ct. 964, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 646 (U.S., Jan. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:   REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. 2003 WI App 243 Reported at: 267 Wis. 2d 783, 672 N.W.2d 97, 2003 WI App 243 (Ct. App. 2003-Published). Source of Appeal: Court: Circuit. County: Sheboygan. Judge: Gary Langhoff. L.C. No. 02CT145.
State v. Faust, 267 Wis. 2d 783, 672 N.W.2d 97, 2003 WI App 243, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 927 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with operating while intoxicated, Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) and operating with a prohibited alcohol concentration, Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b). The circuit court granted his motion to suppress the results of the warrantless blood test because defendant had given a voluntary breath test and thus exigent circumstances did not exist. The court of appeals, Wisconsin, affirmed, and the State sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court held that, under Wis. Const. art. I, § 11 and U.S. Const. amend. IV, exigent circumstances justifying defendant's warrantless and nonconsensual blood draw no longer existed after he gave a satisfactory, useable chemical test. The court reversed, finding that one presumptively valid chemical breath sample did not extinguish the exigent circumstances. The nature of the evidence sought, specifically the rapid dissipation of alcohol from the bloodstream, determined the exigency, not the existence of other evidence. The blood test also satisfied the Bohling test of reasonableness. A preliminary breath test indicated an alcohol concentration of 0.13, but was not admissible to prove the level of intoxication. A later chemical breath sample indicted an alcohol concentration of 0.09, which was sufficient if both of defendant's previous alcohol-related driving convictions were admitted. However, if either were inadmissible, the State would have to prove an alcohol concentration of 0.1 or higher, Wis. Stat. § 885.235(1g)(c). Given the strong state interest in removing drunk drivers from the roadways, the court could not say that the blood draw was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals.

State v. Lombard (In re Lombard)


No. 00-3318


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 95; 273 Wis. 2d 538; 684 N.W.2d 103; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 464


March 12, 2004, Oral Argument  
July 1, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 266 Wis. 2d 887, 669 N.W.2d 157, 2003 WI App 163 (Ct. App. 2003-Published). Source of Appeal: Court: Circuit. County: Dane. Judge: Robert DeChambeau. L.C. No. 00 CI 1.
State v. Lombard (In re Lombard), 266 Wis. 2d 887, 669 N.W.2d 157, 2003 WI App 163, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 711 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) affirmed a judgment declaring petitioner to be a sexually violent person and committing him under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000). Petitioner appealed on ineffective assistance of counsel grounds, asserting that his Fifth Amendment rights were violated because respondent State used, at trial, statements petitioner made to a state psychologist during the pre-petition psychological evaluation.


OVERVIEW: With respect to the issue involving petitioner's alleged Fifth Amendment violation, the lower appellate court concluded that petitioner was not entitled to a Miranda warning before being evaluated by a state psychologist, because any statements petitioner made about his past crimes could not subject him to future prosecution. As the lower appellate court concluded that a Miranda warning was not required, it held that petitioner did not suffer any prejudice as a result of his counsel's failure to object to the psychologist's testimony and report. On further appeal, the court concluded that petitioner was not entitled to Miranda warnings prior to his pre-petition evaluation. Wis. Stat. § 980.05(1m) (1999-2000) plainly contained the language "at the trial." The plain language of the statute led to the conclusion that the legislature intended that the constitutional rights available to a defendant in a criminal proceeding would apply at petitioner's ch. 980 trial. Thus, petitioner did not have the right to Miranda warnings during his pre-petition interview. Because petitioner was not entitled to the warnings, the court concluded that counsel's performance was not deficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

State v. Burris (In re Burris)

SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sex offender challenged a decision from the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which upheld a circuit court's decision to revoke his supervised release under Wis. Stat. § 980.06(d)(2) (1997-98).


OVERVIEW: The offender was convicted of a sex crime. Shortly before his release date, a court found that the offender was a sexually violent person. He was placed in a halfway house, and he was ordered to abide by certain rules. A revocation was sought based on the fact that the offender left the residence to have sexual intercourse with a married woman, he obtained a prescription for a drug that treated erectile dysfunction, he consumed alcohol, and he refused to participate in treatment. This was especially true when the court determined that the safety of others required a revocation under Wis. Stat. § 980.06(d)(2) (1997-98). Further, there was no constitutional "unfairness" in the revocation proceedings. The evidence supported the conclusion that revoking the offender's supervised release was required for the safety of others.

187 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jadowski


No. 03-1493-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 68; 272 Wis. 2d 418; 680 N.W.2d 810; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 436


April 27, 2004, Oral Argument  
June 10, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County, L. Edward Stengel, Judge. Reversed and remanded. (L.C. No. 02 CF 190).
State v. Jadowski, 2004 WI 1, 268 Wis. 2d 137, 673 N.W.2d 694, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 1181 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Circuit court order reversed; cause remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's case came before the supreme court on certification by the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) after the circuit court granted defendant's motion to introduce evidence of the victim's intentional misrepresentation of her age. He faced prosecution for a violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02 (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant faced prosecution on one count of sexual intercourse with a person who had not yet attained the age of 16 years contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.02 (1999-2000). The circuit court granted the defendant's motion to introduce evidence of the victim's intentional misrepresentation of her age and the appellate court certified two questions to the supreme court. First, was a minor sexual assault victim's intentional misrepresentation of his or her age a defense to a charge brought under § 948.02(2)? The supreme court held that § 948.02(2), read with Wis. Stat. §§ 939.23 and 939.43(2) (1999-2000), precluded a defense predicated on a child's intentional misrepresentation of her age. The second certified question was whether or not the statutes denied defendant his constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Because the legislature's forbidding a reasonable mistake of age defense in statutory rape cases had a significant historical derivation and is widespread, and because of judicial deference to the legislature's discretion, it was not violative of due process for the State legislature to forbid a defense of fraud or reasonable mistake about the age of the victim.


OUTCOME: The supreme court held that a defendant predicated on a child's intentional misrepresentation of her age was precluded. Further, the relevant statutes did not violate defendant's claimed constitutional rights.

Custodian of Records v. State (In re Doe)


No. 02-3063-W


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 65; 272 Wis. 2d 208; 680 N.W.2d 792; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 431


November 4, 2003, Oral Argument  
June 9, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by, Reconsideration denied by Custodian of Records for the Legislative Tech. Serv. Bureau v. State (In re John Doe), 2004 WI 149, 277 Wis. 2d 75, 689 N.W.2d 908, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 1022 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON CERTIFICATION FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. (L.C. No. 01 JD 6). PETITION for supervisory writ.



DISPOSITION: Supervisory writ issued quashing the subpoena of the John Doe judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court on certification from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin). Petitioner, the Director of the Legislative Technology Services Bureau (LTSB), sought a supervisory writ of assistance requesting that a subpoena be quashed in a John Doe investigation, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 968.26 (2001-02), of certain legislators and their employees for suspected criminal conduct.


OVERVIEW: The LTSB Director claimed that the confidentiality requirement of Wis. Stat. § 13.96, as it interacted with Wis. Stat. § 905.01, created an implicit statutory privilege that excused him from complying with the subpoena for electronically stored legislative communications at the LTSB. The court held that the confidentiality requirement of Wis. Stat. § 13.96 prevented voluntary disclosure to one who did not have proper authorization to receive the stored data, but it was insufficient to excuse noncompliance with a valid John Doe subpoena. The court also held that if Wis. Const. art. IV, § 16 applied to the LTSB communications, it provided only use immunity, not the right to keep all legislative communications secret. The court concluded that neither the separation of powers doctrine nor Wis. Const. art. IV, § 8 provided an absolute defense to the compulsion of a John Doe subpoena. However, the court found that the subpoena contained no specificity as to subject matter or time, thus it was overly broad. The court quashed the subpoena, with directions that the attorney general comply with particularity and probable cause requirements to produce a constitutionally sufficient subpoena.


OUTCOME: The court granted the LTSB director's request for a supervisory writ quashing the subpoena of the John Doe judge.

Gentilli v. Bd. of the Police & Fire Comm'rs


No. 02-3208


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 60; 272 Wis. 2d 1; 680 N.W.2d 335; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 423; 21 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 662


April 8, 2004, Oral Argument  
June 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  
Reconsideration denied by Gentilli v. Bd. of the Police & Fire Comm'rs, 2004 WI 124, 276 Wis. 2d 4, 689 N.W.2d 59, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 788 (2004)
Reconsideration denied by Gentilli v. Bd. of Police & Fire Comm'rs, 2004 WI 138, 276 Wis. 2d 32, 688 N.W.2d 653, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 990 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON CERTIFICATION FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Paul B. Higginbotham, Judge. L.C. No. 01-CV-1585.
Gentilli v. Bd. of the Police & Fire Comm'rs, 2004 WI 1, 268 Wis. 2d 137, 673 N.W.2d 694, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 1182 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his petition for certiorari review of a termination recommendation made by respondent board of police and fire commissioners. The case was certified for review by the Wisconsin Court of Appeals.


OVERVIEW: During a police investigation, the employee admitted to using drugs. After the board recommended termination, the employee was fired. He then sought review of the board's order in two parallel actions. One was an action under Wis. Stat. § 62.13(5)(i) (amended 1993). The second action was a review of his termination pursuant to a petition for a writ of certiorari. The circuit court determined that the employee's termination was supported by just cause. Thereafter, it dismissed the certiorari action. The employee then sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the amended version of § 62.13(5)(i) was not the exclusive remedy for a claim that the rules a subordinate was found to have violated were unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. These issues of law, even if somewhat overlapping with the issues in a proceeding brought under § 62.13(5)(i), could have been considered under certiorari because they concerned whether or not the board kept within its jurisdiction and proceeded on a correct theory of law. Finally, the court held that issue preclusion did not apply with respect to certiorari proceedings subsequent to a § 62.13(5)(i) appeal, despite the overlapping issues.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State ex rel. Kalal v. Circuit Court for Dane County (In re Criminal Complaint)


No. 02-2490-W


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 58; 271 Wis. 2d 633; 681 N.W.2d 110; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 421


January 14, 2003, Oral Argument  
May 25, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Court: Circuit. County: Dane. Judge: John V. Finn. (L.C. No. 02 GF 008000).
State ex rel. Kalal v. Dane County, 2003 WI 140, 266 Wis. 2d 60, 671 N.W.2d 847, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 826 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an employer and his wife, sought review from an order of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which declined to issue a supervisory writ against a criminal complaint that was privately filed by respondent employee, accusing petitioners of stealing funds earmarked for her retirement account. A criminal complaint had been authorized pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 968.02(3) (2001-02), and reconsideration was denied.


OVERVIEW: The employee, an attorney, complained to the police department and the district attorney (DA) about petitioners' alleged theft, and she was informed that she could proceed in whatever manner she believed necessary. Her motion for issuance of a criminal complaint as to four felony theft counts was granted pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 968.02(3). The trial court denied petitioners' motion for reconsideration, based on their claim that there was no showing that the DA had "refused" to issue the complaint. The court of appeals denied their request for a supervisory writ, and they sought further review. The court found that petitioners had no standing to seek reconsideration under § 968.02(3), as the statute directed an ex parte proceeding and no cross-examination. The court found that issuance of a supervisory writ under Wis. Stat. § 809.51(1) (2001-02) was properly denied, as there was no showing of a violation of a plain duty by the judge. After a lengthy discussion on statutory interpretation, the court found that "refuses" was to be interpreted by its plain dictionary definition and that an explicit refusal was not necessary prior to a judge's authorization of a private complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the court of appeals.

Panzer v. Doyle


No. 03-0910-OA


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 52; 271 Wis. 2d 295; 680 N.W.2d 666; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 419


January 27, 2004, Oral Argument  
May 13, 2004, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION: Rights declared; declaratory relief granted, and injunctive relief denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the Majority Leader of the Wisconsin Senate and the Speak of the Wisconsin Assembly, filed an action under Wis. Const. art. VII, § 3(2) against respondents, the Governor of Wisconsin and the Secretary of Administration, contending that respondents exceeded their authority in agreeing to certain amendments to the gaming compact entered into with the Forest County Potawatomi Tribe (Tribe).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners contended that the governor exceeded his authority in 2003 when he agreed to certain amendments to the gaming compact that the State had entered into with the Tribe, which was a federally recognized Indian tribe indigenous to Wisconsin. The supreme court held that the governor exceeded his authority when he agreed unilaterally to a compact term that permanently removed the subject of Indian gaming from the legislature's ability to establish policy and make law. The gaming compact was projected to generate additional revenue for the State at a time when additional revenue was needed. Further, the governor acted contrary to the public policy embodied in State law and therefore acted without authority by agreeing to allow the Tribe to conduct new games that were prohibited by Wis. Const. art. IV, § 24 and by Wisconsin's criminal statutes. Finally, the supreme court concluded that the governor exceeded his authority by agreeing to waive the State's sovereign immunity, an act which he had no inherent or delegated power to undertake.


OUTCOME: The supreme court granted the declaratory relief and denied the injunctive relief.

No. 03-0060, 03-0061, 03-0062


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN

October 20, 2003, Argued  
April 28, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 02 TP 000009, 02 TP 000010, 02 TP 000011). 263 Wis. 2d 413, 662 N.W.2d 360, 2003 WI App 88. Reported at 263 Wis. 2d 413, 662 N.W.2d 360, 2003 WI App 88 (Ct. App. 2003-Published). Court: Circuit. County: Monroe. Judge: Steven L. Abbott.
Monroe County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Kelli B. (In re Zachary B.), 263 Wis. 2d 413, 662 N.W.2d 360, 2003 WI App 88, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 319 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a county human services department, sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed trial court orders that terminated respondent mother's parental rights to her three sons, based on the appellate court's determination that Wis. Stat. § 48.415(7) (2001-02) could not be constitutionally applied to the mother.


OVERVIEW: The mother was a victim of long-term, continuous incest by her father, who sired her three children. The father was convicted for his criminal actions and he agreed to terminate his parental rights. When the mother was arrested on unrelated charges, the department took the children into custody, and thereafter sought to terminate the mother's rights. The trial court found the mother was an unfit parent under Wis. Stat. § 48.424(4) (2001-02) on the ground of incestuous parenthood pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(7). The appellate court reversed, holding that § 48.415(7) violated the mother's substantive due process rights because it was not narrowly tailored to advance the compelling state interests of protecting children from unfit parents, did not promote deterrence, and did not protect children from the psychological harm of being raised in an incestuous family. On appeal, the court noted that the mother had a fundamental liberty interest in parenting her children. It found that § 48.415(7) violated her substantive due process rights by rendering her unfit per se based solely on her status as an incest victim. It also impaired the public policy of protecting crime victims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court.

Wis. Citizens Concerned for Cranes & Doves v. Wis. Dep't of Natural Res.


No. 02-1166


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 40; 270 Wis. 2d 318; 677 N.W.2d 612; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 240


January 15, 2004, Oral Argument  
April 6, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. 2003 WI App 76. Reported at: 263 Wis. 2d 370, 661 N.W.2d 858, 2003 WI App 76. (Ct. App. 2003-Published) Source of Appeal: Court: Circuit County: Dane Judge: Daniel R. Moeser. L.C. No. 01 CV 1616.
Wis. Citizens Concerned for Cranes v. Wis. Dep't of Natural Res., 263 Wis. 2d 370, 661 N.W.2d 858, 2003 WI App 76, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 314 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff organization sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which found in favor of defendant, the Department of Natural Resources (DNR) and reversed an order of the circuit court declaring Wis. Admin. Code § NR 10.01(1)(h) (2000) invalid and enjoining the DNR from promulgating a rule authorizing a hunting season for mourning doves in Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: The organization commenced an action under Wis. Stat. § 227.40 (1999-2000) seeking a declaration that the DNR exceeded its authority in promulgating the dove-hunting rule. The circuit court granted the organization's request for declaratory and injunctive relief, concluding that Wis. Stat. § 29.014(1) was ambiguous. The appellate court reversed, concluding that the statute was unambiguous and expressly authorized the DNR to establish a hunting season for mourning doves. The supreme court held that the DNR had express authority under § 29.014(1) to adopt Wis. Admin. Code § NR 10.01(1)(h) (2000), because the legislature granted broad authority to the DNR to set open and closed seasons for "game" under Wis. Stat. § 29.014(1) and mourning doves fell within the unambiguous definition of "game" contained therein. Further, there was no conflict between Wis. Stat. §§ 29.014(1) and 29.039(1) (1999-2000), because mourning doves constituted "game" within the meaning of the former provision and qualified as a "non-game species" under the latter.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the appellate court's decision.

Seitzinger v. Cmty. Health Network


No. 02-2002


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 28; 270 Wis. 2d 1; 676 N.W.2d 426; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 234


November 4, 2003, Oral Argument  
March 25, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: ON CERTIFICATION FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS Source of Appeal: Court: Circuit County: Green Lake Judge: Daniel W. Klossner. L.C. No. 01 CV 92.
Seitzinger v. Cmty. Health, 2003 WI 91, 262 Wis. 2d 504, 665 N.W.2d 378, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 600 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Circuit court order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctor sought a declaration that he could be represented at a peer review hearing by a lawyer who was not licensed in Wisconsin. In the alternative, he sought admission pro hac vice of his lawyer. The circuit court found for defendant hospital. On appeal by the doctor, the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) certified two issues: whether the representation would be the practice of law and whether an exception should allow the representation.


OVERVIEW: The hospital bylaws entitled the doctor to be represented at his peer-review hearing by a member of the hospital's medical staff or by legal counsel. The doctor hired a lawyer who was licensed in New Jersey and who was board certified in the relevant medical field. The hospital asserted, and the circuit court agreed, that counsel had to be licensed to practice law in Wisconsin. The court affirmed, finding that the bylaws were a contract and that the hospital reasonably interpreted the words "legal counsel" to refer to an attorney licensed in Wisconsin. To construe the words otherwise could permit attorneys unlicensed in Wisconsin or non-attorneys to violate Wis. Stat. § 757.30 (2001-02). It was reasonable to anticipate that the lawyer would be engaging in activities that would focus on legal issues. The court declined to construct an interpretation, or create an exception, to § 757.30 that would permit an attorney unlicensed in Wisconsin to represent the doctor at his peer review hearing. Finally, the lawyer could not be admitted pro hac vice under Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 10.03(4) (2002), which required that a proceeding be before the judge permitting the nonresident representation.


OUTCOME: On the first question, the court did not answer as to all peer review hearings, but held as a matter of contract that the words "legal counsel" applied only to an attorney licensed to practice law in Wisconsin. On the second question, the court declined to create a statutory exception. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State ex rel. Ziervogel v. Wash. County Bd. of Adjustment


No. 02-1618


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 23; 269 Wis. 2d 549; 676 N.W.2d 401; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 224


December 4, 2003, Oral Argument  
March 19, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. (L.C. No. 01 CV 838). Reported at: 263 Wis. 2d 321, 661 N.W.2d 884, 2003 WI App 82 (Ct. App. 2003-Published).
State ex rel. Ziervogel v. Wash. County Bd. of Adjustment, 263 Wis. 2d 321, 661 N.W.2d 884, 2003 WI App 82, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 307 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought a zoning variance for their Washington County property. Defendant Washington County Board of Adjustment considered their variance application at a public hearing and then denied the variance. The property owners sought review via certiorari in a circuit court, which affirmed the denial. The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) affirmed. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The variance application was denied, and the denial was upheld on certiorari review and appeal for the sole reason that Kenosha County's strict "no reasonable use of the property" standard for determining unnecessary hardship had not been met. The appellate court had now concluded that the "no reasonable use" standard was no longer applicable in area variance cases and reaffirmed the Snyder definition of unnecessary hardship for area variance cases: whether compliance with area zoning restrictions would unreasonably prevent the owner from using the property for a permitted purpose or would render conformity with such restrictions unnecessarily burdensome. Whether this standard was met in this case would depend on the Board's consideration of the purpose of the zoning restriction in question (including the important public purposes of shoreland zoning generally), the effect of the restriction on the property, and the effect of a variance on the neighborhood and the larger public interest. In addition, the property owners would have to demonstrate that the hardship was based upon conditions unique to the property and was not self-created.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Roth v. LaFarge Sch. Dist. Bd. of Canvassers


No. 02-0542


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 6; 268 Wis. 2d 335; 677 N.W.2d 599; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 6


October 8, 2003, Oral Argument  
February 4, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. 2002 WI App 309. Reported at: 259 Wis. 2d 349, 655 N.W.2d 471, 2002 WI App 309 (Ct. App. 2002-Published). L.C. No. 00 CV 154. Court: Circuit. County: Monroe. Judge: Michael J. McAlpine.
Roth v. LaFarge Sch. Dist. Bd., 259 Wis. 2d 349, 655 N.W.2d 471, 2002 WI App 309, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1294 (2002).



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a challenger to the outcome of a referendum, appealed the result of a recount that upheld a tie and resulting defeat of the referendum. A circuit court found in favor of the challenger, in part by denying a motion to intervene by a third party, a proponent of the outcome. The Court of Appeals, Wisconsin, allowed the proponent to intervene and held that a "no" vote had been improperly disqualified. The challenger sought further review.


OVERVIEW: In the recount of a referendum on funding school improvements, respondent board of canvassers disqualified a "no" vote, because the mark had been erased. The board believed that the vote therefore should not be counted under Wis. Stat. § 7.50(2)(c) (1999-2000), which provided that a ballot be counted so far as the electors' intent could be ascertained. The proponent of the result questioned the board's assessment that the mark had been erased, and the appeals court agreed that the ballot should have been counted. In affirming, the court reasoned that the board's determination was one of law, as it involved the interpretation and application of the statute, and that the board erred in its application of § 7.50(2)(c). On the ballot in question, to the right of the word "no," there was a clearly visible slash mark written in pencil. The court thus found that there was a qualifying mark in a qualifying place on the ballot at issue. Section 7.50(2)(c) applied, and required the ballot to be counted, because the intent of the voter was readily ascertainable. The court also held that a decision should be rendered, regardless of whether the matter was mooted by a subsequent referendum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals' decision and held that the "no" vote should be counted, that therefore the referendum resulted in a tie vote, and that the question of funding for school improvements was defeated.

State v. Morford (In re Morford)


No. 01-2461


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI 5; 268 Wis. 2d 300; 674 N.W.2d 349; 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 4


September 9, 2003, Oral Argument

PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. 2003 WI App 1, 259 Wis 2d. 480, 655 N.W.2d 546 (2002). Court: Circuit. County: Milwaukee. Judge: Daniel L. Konkol. (L.C. No. 96 CF 966242).
State v. Morford (In re Morford), 259 Wis. 2d 480, 655 N.W.2d 546, 2003 WI App 1, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1253 (2002).



DISPOSITION: Rights declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed trial court orders granting a district attorney's motion to reconsider a decision that placed defendant on supervised release and which denied defendant's motion for reconsideration. The trial court found defendant was still a sexually violent person, and he was ordered committed to an institutional setting.


OVERVIEW: The trial court placed defendant on supervised release, but thereafter granted the district attorney's motion for reconsideration and ordered defendant committed to an institutional setting. The trial court denied defendant's motion for reconsideration, and he appealed. The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's order, concluding that Wis. Stat. § 806.07(l)(h) (1999-2000) was satisfied. Defendant sought further review, and the court found that Wis. It was noted that a determination had been made that defendant was an appropriate candidate for supervised release, but he remained institutionalized awaiting placement. The court found that the issue came within exceptions to the mootness doctrine, in that it was an issue of great public importance, recurred with some frequency, and was likely to arise again. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 806.07(1) was improperly applied to the facts, as Wis. Stat. § 980.08(6m) was better suited for granting the relief sought, regardless of whether the defendant had actually been placed on supervised release.


OUTCOME: The court declared the rights of defendant, based on the error of the court of appeals.

State v. Knapp


No. 00-2590-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI 121; 265 Wis. 2d 278; 666 N.W.2d 881; 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 621


April 23, 2003, Oral Argument  
July 22, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 22, 2003. As Corrected August 14, 2003.
Vacated by, Remanded by Wisconsin v. Knapp, 542 U.S. 952, 159 L. Ed. 2d 835, 124 S. Ct. 2932, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 4766 (U.S., 2004)
Reinstated by, in part State v. Knapp, 2005 WI 127, 285 Wis. 2d 86, 700 N.W.2d 899, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 395 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON CERTIFICATION FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. APPEAL from a judgment of the Jefferson County Circuit Court, Randy R. Koschnick, Judge. L.C. No. 99 CF 363.
State v. Knapp, 2002 WI 121, 257 Wis. 2d 123, 653 N.W.2d 893, 2002 Wisc. LEXIS 1050 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for murder. The trial court granted in part and denied in part defendant's motions to suppress evidence. Both the State and defendant appealed. The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin certified the following question: Should physical evidence obtained as the direct result of a Miranda violation be suppressed when the violation was an intentional attempt to prevent the suspect from exercising his Fifth Amendment rights?


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for a parole violation the day after the victim was killed. When the police went to arrest him, without giving a Miranda warning, the police asked defendant what clothes he had been wearing the night before. Defendant pointed to a pile of clothes on the floor, and a sweatshirt contained the victim's blood on one sleeve. The questioning by the police continued at the station without any Miranda warnings. Other evidence was seized when defendant's brother allowed the police to search his house and the room defendant rented. The state supreme court: (1) affirmed the suppression of the sweatshirt, as its discovery was the direct result of an intentional Miranda violation and overruled State v. Yang, 2000 WI App 63, 233 Wis. 2d 545, 608 N.W.2d 703; (2) affirmed the suppression of the statements given to the police, as defendant had not been advised of his rights, but also allowed the statements to be used for impeachment purposes; (3) held that defendant's brother had apparent authority to give consent to the police to search defendant's room in the brother's house; and (4) affirmed the decision to admit hearsay evidence used to implicate a third party suspect.


OUTCOME: The court's of appeals' question was answered in the affirmative, and the grant of the motion to suppress the evidence seized as a result of the violation was affirmed. The court reversed the trial court's grant of the motion to suppress evidence seized from defendant's apartment. The court affirmed the suppression of defendant's statements, except for their use during cross-examination of defendant.

 

200 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thiel


No. 01-1589-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI 111; 264 Wis. 2d 571; 665 N.W.2d 305; 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 611


April 30, 2003, Argued  
July 15, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. L.C. No. 99-CF-503. Reported at: 2002 WI App 292, 258 Wis. 2d 981, 654 N.W.2d 94 (Ct. App. 2002-Unpublished). County: La Crosse. Judge: Dale T. Pasell.
State v. Thiel, 258 Wis. 2d 981, 654 N.W.2d 94, 2002 WI App 292, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1094 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed a circuit court's decision to grant defendant a new trial on the charge of sexual exploitation by a therapist and found that any deficient performance by defendant's counsel was not prejudicial to his defense.


OVERVIEW: The complainant told the police that she engaged in sexual relations with defendant, her psychiatrist, but admitted that she submitted a semen sample that was not defendant's. Counsel, although needing more time to prepare, abided by defendant's request not to seek a continuance. Defendant was convicted of sexual exploitation. The court held that the court of appeals erred in denying a new trial because the cumulative effect of counsel's deficiencies prejudiced defendant to the extent that it undermined confidence in the trial's outcome. The court concluded that the representation was constitutionally inadequate because counsel failed to read all discovery materials, which contained a medical report that the complainant was enraged at defendant for refusing to support her disability claim; investigate her credibility by interviewing neighbors who never saw her at defendant's house and discover that she had difficulty locating the house and did not have a driver's license; failed to prevent the admission of a prior consistent statement; and misunderstood Wis. Stat. § 972.11(3) (1999-2000) as preventing the State from presenting the complainant's medical and personal records.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and remanded the cause against defendant to the circuit court for a new trial.
